			<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Gaza War (2008–09)</h1>

<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;border-bottom:1px solid #aaa;line-height:1.5em;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gaza_Strip_map2.svg" class="image"><img alt="Gaza Strip map2.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Gaza_Strip_map2.svg/300px-Gaza_Strip_map2.svg.png" width="300" height="367" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Gaza_Strip_map2.svg/450px-Gaza_Strip_map2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Gaza_Strip_map2.svg/600px-Gaza_Strip_map2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="725" data-file-height="888" /></a><br />
Map of Gaza</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2">
<table style="width:100%;margin:0;padding:0;border:0">
<tr>
<th style="padding-right:1em">Date</th>
<td>27 December 2008 – 18 January 2009<br />
(3&#160;weeks and 1&#160;day)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th style="padding-right:1em">Location</th>
<td><span class="location"><a href="/wiki/Gaza_Strip" title="Gaza Strip">Gaza Strip</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_District_(Israel)" class="mw-redirect" title="South District (Israel)">Southern Israel</a></span></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th style="padding-right:1em">Result</th>
<td>
<p>Israeli military victory<sup id="cite_ref-Aviation_Week_2009-05-11_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Aviation_Week_2009-05-11-2">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-jpost.com_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jpost.com-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nytimes.com_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes.com-4">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Victorious.2C_but_vilified:_Israel_has_.27destroyed_its_image_and_its_soul.27_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Victorious.2C_but_vilified:_Israel_has_.27destroyed_its_image_and_its_soul.27-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>Israel declared <a href="/wiki/Unilateral" class="mw-redirect" title="Unilateral">unilateral</a> ceasefire, 12 hours later Hamas announced a <a href="/wiki/Tahdiya" title="Tahdiya">one-week ceasefire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-xinhua_one_week_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xinhua_one_week-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cbc.ca_one_week_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cbc.ca_one_week-7">[7]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Effects_of_the_Gaza_War#Gaza_humanitarian_crisis" class="mw-redirect" title="Effects of the Gaza War">Humanitarian crisis</a> and deterioration of infrastructure and basic services in Gaza.<sup id="cite_ref-ocha_report_1_2_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ocha_report_1_2-8">[8]</a></sup></li>
<li>Number of <a href="/wiki/List_of_Palestinian_rocket_attacks_on_Israel,_2009" title="List of Palestinian rocket attacks on Israel, 2009">rockets</a> being fired from Gaza reduced.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)#Post-war_military_assessment" title="Gaza War (2008–09)">See results</a></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
</td>
</tr>

<p>IDF: 4,000<sup id="cite_ref-Israel_vows_no_let-up_over_Gaza_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Israel_vows_no_let-up_over_Gaza-11">[11]</a></sup>–20,000<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> deployed in ground invasion and tens of thousands of reservists mobilized<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> (176,000 total active personnel)<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>

<td colspan="2" style="font-size:90%;border-top:1px solid #aaa;"><b>*</b>255 (<a href="/wiki/Palestinian_Centre_for_Human_Rights" title="Palestinian Centre for Human Rights">PCHR</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-PCHRCASFIG_30-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PCHRCASFIG-30">[30]</a></sup> or 265 (B'Tselem)<sup id="cite_ref-BTselem_fatalities_OCL_31-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BTselem_fatalities_OCL-31">[31]</a></sup> police officers were killed.</td>
</tr>
</table>

<div id="Gaza.E2.80.93Israel_conflict" style="font-size:114%"><span style="line-height:1.6em"><a href="/wiki/Gaza%E2%80%93Israel_conflict" title="Gaza–Israel conflict">Gaza–Israel conflict</a></span></div>
</th>
</tr>
<tr style="height:2px">
<td colspan="2"></td>

<tr>
<td colspan="2" class="navbox-list navbox-odd hlist" style="width:100%;padding:0px">

</div>
<p>The <b>Gaza War</b>, also known as <b>Operation Cast Lead</b> (<span lang="he" dir="rtl" xml:lang="he">מבצע עופרת יצוקה</span>‎),<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> also known as the <b>Gaza Massacre</b> (<span lang="ar" dir="rtl" xml:lang="ar">مجزرة غزة</span>‎)<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> and the <b>Battle of al-Furqan</b> (<span lang="ar" dir="rtl" xml:lang="ar">معركة الفرقان</span>‎) by Hamas,<sup id="cite_ref-Abdul-Hameed_al-Kayyali_2009_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abdul-Hameed_al-Kayyali_2009-42">[42]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Maximilian_Felsch.2C_2011_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Maximilian_Felsch.2C_2011-43">[43]</a></sup> was a three-week armed conflict between Palestinians in the <a href="/wiki/Gaza_Strip" title="Gaza Strip">Gaza Strip</a> and <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> that <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_the_2008%E2%80%932009_Israel%E2%80%93Gaza_conflict#27_December_2008" class="mw-redirect" title="Timeline of the 2008–2009 Israel–Gaza conflict">began</a> on 27 December 2008 and ended on 18 January 2009 in a unilateral ceasefire.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<p>Israel's stated goal was to stop indiscriminate <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_rocket_attacks_on_Israel" title="Palestinian rocket attacks on Israel">Palestinian rocket fire</a> into Israel<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> and weapons smuggling into the Gaza strip.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-guardian.co.uk_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian.co.uk-48">[48]</a></sup> Israeli forces attacked police stations, military targets including weapons caches and suspected rocket firing teams,<sup id="cite_ref-Defense_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Defense-49">[49]</a></sup> as well as political and administrative institutions in the opening assault, striking in the densely populated cities of <a href="/wiki/Gaza_City" title="Gaza City">Gaza</a>, <a href="/wiki/Khan_Yunis" title="Khan Yunis">Khan Yunis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rafah" title="Rafah">Rafah</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-UNFFMGCReport_pdf_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNFFMGCReport_pdf-50">[50]</a></sup> After hostilities broke out, Palestinian groups fired rockets in response to what they characterized as "massacres".<sup id="cite_ref-bbc1309_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc1309-51">[51]</a></sup> The international community considers indiscriminate attacks on civilians and civilian structures that do not discriminate between civilians and military targets as <a href="/wiki/Geneva_conventions#Protocols" class="mw-redirect" title="Geneva conventions">illegal under international law</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-HRW_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HRW-52">[52]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ICRC-humanShieldsArt51_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ICRC-humanShieldsArt51-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p>An Israeli ground invasion began on 3 January. Infantry commanders were given an unprecedented level of access to coordinate with air, naval, artillery, intelligence, and combat engineering units during this second phase. Various new technologies and hardware were also introduced. On 5 January, the IDF began operating in the densely populated urban centers of Gaza. During the last week of the offensive (from 12 January), Israel mostly hit targets it had damaged before and struck Palestinian rocket-launching units.<sup id="cite_ref-Israeli_Arsenal_15-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Israeli_Arsenal-15">[15]</a></sup> Hamas intensified its rocket and mortar attacks against civilian targets in southern Israel, reaching the major cities of <a href="/wiki/Beersheba" title="Beersheba">Beersheba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ashdod" title="Ashdod">Ashdod</a> for the first time during the conflict.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> Israeli politicians ultimately decided against striking deeper within Gaza amid concerns of higher casualties on both sides and rising international criticism. The conflict ended on 18 January, when Israel first declared a <a href="/wiki/Unilateral" class="mw-redirect" title="Unilateral">unilateral</a> ceasefire, followed by Hamas' announcing a <a href="/wiki/Tahdiya" title="Tahdiya">one-week ceasefire</a> twelve hours later.<sup id="cite_ref-xinhua_one_week_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xinhua_one_week-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cbc.ca_one_week_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cbc.ca_one_week-7">[7]</a></sup> Israel completed its withdrawal on 21 January.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p>The conflict resulted in between 1,166 and 1,417 Palestinian and 13 Israeli deaths (4 from friendly fire).<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/Shin_Bet" title="Shin Bet">Shin Bet</a>, after the conflict, there was a decrease in <a href="/wiki/List_of_Palestinian_rocket_attacks_on_Israel" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Palestinian rocket attacks on Israel">Palestinian rocket attacks</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Shabak_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shabak-59">[59]</a></sup> In September 2009, a <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Fact_Finding_Mission_on_the_Gaza_Conflict" title="United Nations Fact Finding Mission on the Gaza Conflict">UN special mission</a>, headed by the South African Justice <a href="/wiki/Richard_Goldstone" title="Richard Goldstone">Richard Goldstone</a>, produced a <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Fact_Finding_Mission_on_the_Gaza_Conflict#Report" title="United Nations Fact Finding Mission on the Gaza Conflict">report</a> accusing both Palestinian militants and the IDF of <a href="/wiki/War_crime" title="War crime">war crimes</a> and possible crimes against humanity, and recommended bringing those responsible to justice.<sup id="cite_ref-BBCSept15a_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCSept15a-60">[60]</a></sup> In January 2010, the Israeli government released a response criticizing the Goldstone Report and disputing its findings.<sup id="cite_ref-Mfa.gov.ila_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mfa.gov.ila-61">[61]</a></sup> In 2011, Goldstone wrote that he no longer believed that Israel intentionally targeted civilians in Gaza.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> The other authors of the report, <a href="/wiki/Hina_Jilani" title="Hina Jilani">Hina Jilani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christine_Chinkin" title="Christine Chinkin">Christine Chinkin</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Desmond_Travers" title="Desmond Travers">Desmond Travers</a>, rejected Goldstone's re-assessment.<sup id="cite_ref-afp1404_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-afp1404-63">[63]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-g2011-04-14_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-g2011-04-14-64">[64]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Human_Rights_Council" title="United Nations Human Rights Council">United Nations Human Rights Council</a> ordered Israel to conduct various repairs of the damages. On 21 September 2012, the United Nations Human Rights Council concluded that 75% of civilian homes destroyed in the attack were not rebuilt.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Israeli%E2%80%93Palestinian_conflict" title="Israeli–Palestinian conflict">Israeli–Palestinian conflict</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gaza%E2%80%93Israel_conflict" title="Gaza–Israel conflict">Gaza–Israel conflict</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rocket_and_mortar_attacks_on_southern_Israel" class="mw-redirect" title="Rocket and mortar attacks on southern Israel">Rocket and mortar attacks on southern Israel</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Blockade_of_the_Gaza_Strip" title="Blockade of the Gaza Strip">Blockade of the Gaza Strip</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_the_Gaza_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Timeline of the Gaza War">Timeline of the Gaza War</a>; <a href="/wiki/List_of_Palestinian_rocket_attacks_on_Israel,_2008" title="List of Palestinian rocket attacks on Israel, 2008">List of Palestinian rocket attacks on Israel, 2008</a>; and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Palestinian_rocket_attacks_on_Israel,_2009" title="List of Palestinian rocket attacks on Israel, 2009">List of Palestinian rocket attacks on Israel, 2009</a></div>
<p>The Gaza Strip is a coastal strip of land on the eastern shore of the Mediterranean Sea bordering Egypt and Israel. Israel controls Gaza's airspace and territorial waters and restricts the movement of people or goods in or out of Gaza.<sup id="cite_ref-AI_briefing_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AI_briefing-66">[66]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-isrlpa13698_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-isrlpa13698-67">[67]</a></sup> The UN, <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a> and many other international bodies and <a href="/wiki/Non-governmental_organization" title="Non-governmental organization">NGOs</a> consider Israel to be the occupying power.<sup id="cite_ref-AI_briefing_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AI_briefing-66">[66]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-isrlpa13698_67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-isrlpa13698-67">[67]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cnn2009-01-06_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnn2009-01-06-68">[68]</a></sup> Israel maintains that its occupation of Gaza ended following the completion of its <a href="/wiki/Israel%27s_unilateral_disengagement_plan" class="mw-redirect" title="Israel's unilateral disengagement plan">unilateral disengagement plan</a> in 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-is_Gaza_still_occupied_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-is_Gaza_still_occupied-69">[69]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following <a href="/wiki/Hamas" title="Hamas">Hamas</a>'s electoral victory in the <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_legislative_election,_2006" title="Palestinian legislative election, 2006">January 2006 legislative elections</a><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> and formation of the Hamas-led PA government on March, the <a href="/wiki/Quartet_on_the_Middle_East" title="Quartet on the Middle East">Quartet</a> (United States, Russia, United Nations, and European Union) conditioned future foreign assistance to the PA on the future government's commitment to nonviolence, recognition of the state of Israel, and acceptance of previous agreements. Hamas has rejected such demands, leading to Quartet suspension of its foreign assistance program and <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> imposing <a href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%932007_economic_sanctions_against_the_Palestinian_National_Authority" class="mw-redirect" title="2006–2007 economic sanctions against the Palestinian National Authority">economic sanctions</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-U.S._Foreign_Aid_to_the_Palestinians_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-U.S._Foreign_Aid_to_the_Palestinians-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<p>In June 2007, after the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Gaza_(2007)" title="Battle of Gaza (2007)">military takeover</a> of Gaza by Hamas and the overthrowing of Fatah, the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Palestinian_National_Authority" title="President of the Palestinian National Authority">President of the Palestinian National Authority</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mahmoud_Abbas" title="Mahmoud Abbas">Mahmoud Abbas</a>, dismissed the Hamas-led government and formed a government in the <a href="/wiki/West_Bank" title="West Bank">West Bank</a>, bypassing the Hamas-dominated parliament.<sup id="cite_ref-Gaza_journalists_caught_up_in_Hamas-Fatah_legitimacy_argument_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gaza_journalists_caught_up_in_Hamas-Fatah_legitimacy_argument-74">[74]</a></sup> Israel imposed a ground, air, and maritime <a href="/wiki/Blockade_of_the_Gaza_Strip" title="Blockade of the Gaza Strip">blockade</a>, and announced it would allow only humanitarian supplies into the Strip.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC7838618_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC7838618-75">[75]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AnthonyHCordesman_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AnthonyHCordesman-76">[76]</a></sup> Palestinian groups were partially able to bypass the blockade through tunnels, some of which are said to have been used for weapons smuggling.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<p>Between 2005 and 2007, Palestinian groups in Gaza fired about 2,700 locally made Qassam rockets into Israel, killing four Israeli civilians and injuring 75 others. During the same period, Israel fired more than 14,600 155&#160;mm artillery shells into the Gaza Strip, killing 59 Palestinians and injuring 270. According to the <a href="/wiki/Office_for_the_Coordination_of_Humanitarian_Affairs" class="mw-redirect" title="Office for the Coordination of Humanitarian Affairs">Office for the Coordination of Humanitarian Affairs</a>, between 2005 and 2008, 116 Israelis, including civilians and Israeli security forces, which includes <a href="/wiki/Israeli_police" class="mw-redirect" title="Israeli police">Israeli police</a>, <a href="/wiki/Israeli_Border_Police" class="mw-redirect" title="Israeli Border Police">Israeli Border Police</a> and members of the armed services, were killed in both Israel and the <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_Territories" class="mw-redirect" title="Palestinian Territories">Palestinian Territories</a> in "direct conflict related incidents" and 1,509 were injured.<sup id="cite_ref-ocha_background_dead_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ocha_background_dead-78">[78]</a></sup> During this time, 1,735 Palestinians, including civilians and militants from various groups, were killed and 8,308 wounded in "direct conflict related incidents".<sup id="cite_ref-ocha_background_dead_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ocha_background_dead-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2008_six-month_ceasefire">2008 six-month ceasefire</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: 2008 six-month ceasefire">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2008_Israel%E2%80%93Hamas_ceasefire" title="2008 Israel–Hamas ceasefire">2008 Israel–Hamas ceasefire</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Israelis_killed_by_Palestinians_in_Israel_and_Palestinians_killed_by_Israelis_in_Gaza_-_2008_prior_to_Gaza_War.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Israelis_killed_by_Palestinians_in_Israel_and_Palestinians_killed_by_Israelis_in_Gaza_-_2008_prior_to_Gaza_War.png/220px-Israelis_killed_by_Palestinians_in_Israel_and_Palestinians_killed_by_Israelis_in_Gaza_-_2008_prior_to_Gaza_War.png" width="220" height="160" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Israelis_killed_by_Palestinians_in_Israel_and_Palestinians_killed_by_Israelis_in_Gaza_-_2008_prior_to_Gaza_War.png/330px-Israelis_killed_by_Palestinians_in_Israel_and_Palestinians_killed_by_Israelis_in_Gaza_-_2008_prior_to_Gaza_War.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Israelis_killed_by_Palestinians_in_Israel_and_Palestinians_killed_by_Israelis_in_Gaza_-_2008_prior_to_Gaza_War.png/440px-Israelis_killed_by_Palestinians_in_Israel_and_Palestinians_killed_by_Israelis_in_Gaza_-_2008_prior_to_Gaza_War.png 2x" data-file-width="1075" data-file-height="781" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rock_mort_gaza_2008.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Rock_mort_gaza_2008.JPG/220px-Rock_mort_gaza_2008.JPG" width="220" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Rock_mort_gaza_2008.JPG/330px-Rock_mort_gaza_2008.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Rock_mort_gaza_2008.JPG/440px-Rock_mort_gaza_2008.JPG 2x" data-file-width="909" data-file-height="620" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">

Rocket hits in Israel, January–December 2008<sup id="cite_ref-rockmort_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rockmort-79">[79]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 19 June 2008, an Egyptian-brokered six-month "lull" or <a href="/wiki/2008_Israel%E2%80%93Hamas_ceasefire" title="2008 Israel–Hamas ceasefire">pause in hostilities between Israel and Hamas</a> went into effect.<sup id="cite_ref-kershner_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kershner-80">[80]</a></sup> The agreement had no mutually agreed text or enforcement mechanism and eventually collapsed.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt-truce_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt-truce-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<p>The agreement required Hamas to end rocket and mortar attacks on <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> and to enforce the lull throughout Gaza. In addition, Israel insisted that the agreement would include an end to Hamas' military buildup in Gaza and movement toward the release of Corporal Shalit.<sup id="cite_ref-Israel_Agrees_to_Truce_with_Hamas_on_Gaza_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Israel_Agrees_to_Truce_with_Hamas_on_Gaza-82">[82]</a></sup> Hamas said all of Gaza's militant groups would abide by the truce.<sup id="cite_ref-Israel_confirms_Hamas_ceasefire_deal_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Israel_confirms_Hamas_ceasefire_deal-83">[83]</a></sup> Defense Ministry Official Amos Gilad, the Israeli envoy to the talks, stressed that Israel demanded a ceasefire, meaning that even one single rocket fired will be seen as a violation of the agreement. He added that Egypt, on its side, is committed to preventing the smuggling activity from Gaza.<sup id="cite_ref-Top_Defense_Ministry_official:_If_Shalit_is_not_released.2C_Rafah_stays_closed_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Top_Defense_Ministry_official:_If_Shalit_is_not_released.2C_Rafah_stays_closed-84">[84]</a></sup> Gilad also said that Israel would hold Hamas responsible for attacks from Gaza.<sup id="cite_ref-Israel_confirms_Hamas_ceasefire_deal_83-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Israel_confirms_Hamas_ceasefire_deal-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<p>In exchange, Israel agreed to ease the embargo and to halt military raids into Gaza.<sup id="cite_ref-Israel_Agrees_to_Truce_with_Hamas_on_Gaza_82-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Israel_Agrees_to_Truce_with_Hamas_on_Gaza-82">[82]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Israel_reopens_third_Gaza_crossing_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Israel_reopens_third_Gaza_crossing-85">[85]</a></sup> As part of the deal Egypt had promised to stop the smuggling of arms and weapons from its territory into Gaza.<sup id="cite_ref-Israel_confirms_Hamas_ceasefire_deal_83-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Israel_confirms_Hamas_ceasefire_deal-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Implementation">Implementation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Implementation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The truce started slowly, with the UN recording seven IDF violations of the ceasefire between 20 and 26 June, and three violations by Palestinian groups not affiliated with Hamas between 23 and 26 June.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> Several mortars and Qassam rockets were fired at Israel in late June.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup></p>
<p>Israel and Hamas accused each other of bad faith and of violations of the Egyptian-mediated truce. Israel noted that rocket fire from Gaza never stopped entirely ("between June 19 and November 4, 20 rockets,<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> and 18 mortar shells <sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> were fired at Israel") and that weapons smuggling was not halted,<sup id="cite_ref-ITIC-2008-12_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ITIC-2008-12-92">[92]</a></sup> while Hamas accused Israel of never allowing the major renewal of goods' flow into Gaza and of conducting raids that killed Hamas fighters.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt-truce_81-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt-truce-81">[81]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Guardian20091105_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian20091105-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the month prior to 4 November, Israel-Palestinian violence fell to its lowest level since the start of the al-Aqsa intifada in September 2000<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>. One rocket and 1 mortar shell were fired at Israel in October.<sup id="cite_ref-ITIC-2009-02-01_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ITIC-2009-02-01-94">[94]</a></sup> Several Israeli violations were reported: In South Gaza on 3 October the IDF fired on two unarmed Palestinians near the border and sent soldiers into the strip to arrest them and detain them in Israel. On the 27 October IDF soldiers fired into Gaza for unknown reasons damaging a school in <a href="/wiki/Khuza%27a,_Khan_Yunis" title="Khuza'a, Khan Yunis">Khuza'a</a> and injuring one child. Palestinian fishing boats off the Gaza coast were fired upon on four separate occasions during the month wounding two fisherman. Throughout the month of October 2008 a single Palestinian violation was reported: 1 rocket was fired into Israel causing no damage or injuries. At the end of the month the American Secretary of State <a href="/wiki/Condoleezza_Rice" title="Condoleezza Rice">Condoleezza Rice</a> sent a message to Hamas acknowledging their efforts to keep the peace.<sup id="cite_ref-JPSPrelude_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JPSPrelude-95">[95]</a></sup> According to a joint Tel Aviv-European University study, based on <a href="/wiki/B%27tselem" class="mw-redirect" title="B'tselem">B'tselem</a>'s data, 79% of all breaks in a lull of violence since the Second Intifada were due to Israeli actions, while Hamas and other factions were responsible for 8% of such violations.<sup id="cite_ref-LeVine_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LeVine-96">[96]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-operation_actions">Pre-operation actions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Pre-operation actions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Violence_in_the_Israeli%E2%80%93Palestinian_conflict_2008" class="mw-redirect" title="Violence in the Israeli–Palestinian conflict 2008">Violence in the Israeli–Palestinian conflict 2008</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="4_November_incident">4 November incident</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 4 November incident">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 4 November 2008, Israel launched a military incursion into a residential area of Dayr al-Balah in central Gaza. paratroopers reconnaissance battalion commanded by <a href="/wiki/Yaron_Finkelman" title="Yaron Finkelman">Yaron Finkelman</a> operating in Operation Double Challenge killed six terrorists and demolished the opening of a tunnel concealed within a building 300 meters from the fence on the Gaza Strip border.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> Israel stated its aim was to destroy what it said was a tunnel on the Gaza-Israel border dug by militants to infiltrate into Israel and abduct soldiers, however an Israeli defense official was quoted in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Times" title="The Washington Times">The Washington Times</a></i> acknowledging that Israel wanted to "send Hamas a message".<sup id="cite_ref-JPSPrelude_95-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JPSPrelude-95">[95]</a></sup> The assault, according to <a href="/wiki/Mark_LeVine" title="Mark LeVine">Mark LeVine</a> was unprovoked, and several Hamas members were killed. The following day, the siege of the Gaza Strip intensified.<sup id="cite_ref-LeVine_96-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LeVine-96">[96]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> According to Israel, the raid was not a violation of the ceasefire, but a legitimate step to remove an immediate threat. Israeli infantry, tanks, and bulldozers entered 250 m into the Gaza Strip, the first major incursion since the June truce. A gunfight broke out, in which one Hamas fighter was killed. Hamas responded with a barrage of mortar and rocket fire at Israeli troops. Three Israeli airstrikes on Hamas mortar and rocket positions then killed five Hamas fighters. According to eyewitnesses, another three Hamas fighters were wounded in an Israeli <a href="/wiki/Unmanned_aerial_vehicle" title="Unmanned aerial vehicle">UAV</a> strike over the el-Burejj refugee camp.<sup id="cite_ref-Rockets_fired_after_Gaza_clashes_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rockets_fired_after_Gaza_clashes-100">[100]</a></sup> Three Israeli soldiers were also wounded during the operation. Hamas said it would take revenge for what it perceived as an act of Israeli aggression that had violated the truce.<sup id="cite_ref-Rockets_fired_after_Gaza_clashes_100-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rockets_fired_after_Gaza_clashes-100">[100]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> Hamas launched 35 rockets into southern Israel in what was described by Hamas spokesman Fawzi Barhoum as a "response to Israel's massive breach of the truce", stating that "The Israelis began this tension and they must pay an expensive price. They cannot leave us drowning in blood while they sleep soundly in their beds."<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian20091105_93-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian20091105-93">[93]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-hider_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hider-102">[102]</a></sup></p>
<p>The intensity of rocket attacks targeted at Israeli cities near Gaza sharply increased during November 2008, approaching pre-truce levels. Clashes also took place along the border, during which 11 Palestinian militants were killed.<sup id="cite_ref-novattacks_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-novattacks-103">[103]</a></sup> In the period between 4 Novembe incident and mid-December, more than 200 Qassam rockets and mortar shells landed in the western Negev region. Israel has frequently shut down the crossings in response to rocket attacks on its towns.<sup id="cite_ref-sofer_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sofer-104">[104]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="December">December</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: December">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 13 December, Israel announced that it favored extending the cease-fire, provided Hamas adhered to the conditions.<sup id="cite_ref-sofer_104-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sofer-104">[104]</a></sup> On 14 December, a Hamas delegation in Cairo proposed that Hamas was prepared to stop all rocket attacks against Israel if the Israelis would open up the Gaza border crossings and pledge not to launch attacks in Gaza.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> On the same day, Hamas officials said that earlier reports, quoting Khaled Meshaal as saying there would be no renewal of the truce, were inaccurate. A Hamas spokesman said that the lull would not be renewed, "as long as there is no real Israeli commitment to all of its conditions".<sup id="cite_ref-Gaza-Israel_truce_in_jeopardy_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gaza-Israel_truce_in_jeopardy-106">[106]</a></sup> A spokesman for the Israeli Prime Minister replied that Israel was committed to the truce but "it's clear there can't be a one-sided ceasefire, ... where rockets are everyday coming from the Gaza Strip targeting Israeli civilians."<sup id="cite_ref-Gaza-Israel_truce_in_jeopardy_106-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gaza-Israel_truce_in_jeopardy-106">[106]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 17 December, a 40-year-old Palestinian was killed by IDF fire in Northern Gaza.<sup id="cite_ref-harel_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-harel-107">[107]</a></sup> The following day, 18 December, Hamas declared the end of the cease-fire, a day before the truce officially expired.<sup id="cite_ref-TIMELINE_-_Israeli-Hamas_violence_since_truce_ended_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TIMELINE_-_Israeli-Hamas_violence_since_truce_ended-108">[108]</a></sup> More than 20 rockets were fired from Gaza into southern Israel on that day.<sup id="cite_ref-Hamas_says_it_will_not_renew_ceasefire_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hamas_says_it_will_not_renew_ceasefire-109">[109]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 19 December, Hamas refused to enter talks to renew the six-month truce and a Hamas spokesman announced that it would not extend the cease-fire.<sup id="cite_ref-harel_107-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-harel-107">[107]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Hamas_says_it_will_not_renew_ceasefire_109-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hamas_says_it_will_not_renew_ceasefire-109">[109]</a></sup> Palestinian sources said that Hamas wanted to renew the truce, but only on improved terms – a complete opening of the border crossings with Israel, the opening of the Rafah border crossing with Egypt, a complete ban on Israeli military activity in Gaza and an extension of the truce to the West Bank as well. Israel was not ready to accept these terms.<sup id="cite_ref-harel_107-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-harel-107">[107]</a></sup> This was confirmed by <a href="/wiki/Yuval_Diskin" title="Yuval Diskin">Yuval Diskin</a>, head of <a href="/wiki/Shin_Bet" title="Shin Bet">Shin Bet</a> (Israel's internal security agency), at an <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_Israel" title="Cabinet of Israel">Israeli cabinet</a> meeting on 21 December. Diskin said he thought Hamas was "interested in continuing the truce, but wants to improve its terms ... it wants us to lift the siege of Gaza, stop attacks, and extend the truce to include the <a href="/wiki/West_Bank" title="West Bank">West Bank</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> Three Qassam rockets fired from the northern Gaza Strip landed in Israel.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 22 December, Israeli Defense Minister <a href="/wiki/Ehud_Barak" title="Ehud Barak">Ehud Barak</a> said that his country will not accept the ongoing rocket fire from the Palestinian militants in the Gaza Strip, Israeli Foreign Minister <a href="/wiki/Tzipi_Livni" title="Tzipi Livni">Tzipi Livni</a>, who had supported the truce until recently, suggested that military actions be taken against the Hamas government in Gaza.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 23 December, senior Hamas leader <a href="/wiki/Mahmoud_al-Zahar" title="Mahmoud al-Zahar">Mahmoud al-Zahar</a> said that Hamas was willing to renew the cease-fire under the original terms, demanding an Israeli commitment to refrain from any military operation in the Strip and to keep the border crossings open. Speaking with Egyptian newspaper <i>al-Ahram</i>, al-Zahar said that the movement would reassess the situation in Gaza once the 24 hours during which Hamas vowed to halt rocket fire had ended.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> Despite the temporary ceasefire declared by the armed Palestinian factions, eight Qassam rockets and eight mortar shells hit the Negev.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> Also that day, <a href="/wiki/Israeli_Defense_Forces" class="mw-redirect" title="Israeli Defense Forces">Israeli Defense Forces</a> killed three Palestinian militants, stating they were planting explosives on the border.<sup id="cite_ref-PHRMG_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PHRMG-116">[116]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 24 December, an Israeli airstrike hit a group of militants in Gaza Strip. An Israeli military spokesman said that the militants had fired mortars at Israel. Palestinian medics said that one Hamas militant was killed in the strike and two other Palestinians were wounded, including a cameraman from Hamas' television station.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> On that day, Hamas military wing issued a statement saying that it began an operation code-named "Operation Oil Stain". 87 Palestinian mortar shells, <a href="/wiki/Katyusha_rocket_launcher" title="Katyusha rocket launcher">Katyusha</a> and <a href="/wiki/Qassam_rocket" title="Qassam rocket">Qassam rockets</a> hit the Negev.<sup id="cite_ref-maan_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-maan-118">[118]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-katz_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-katz-119">[119]</a></sup> Hamas said that it would expand the "Oil Stain" and put thousands of Israelis "under fire". Hamas said it was ready for the war: "far greater than surrendering to Israeli threats and that they became much more prepared to counter Israeli aggression and to defend themselves than in the past."<sup id="cite_ref-maan_118-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-maan-118">[118]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 25 December, after Israel had "wrapped up preparations for a broad offensive", <a href="/wiki/Israeli_Prime_Minister" class="mw-redirect" title="Israeli Prime Minister">Israeli Prime Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Ehud_Olmert" title="Ehud Olmert">Ehud Olmert</a> delivered a final warning in an interview with the Arabic language satellite channel <a href="/wiki/Al-Arabiya" class="mw-redirect" title="Al-Arabiya">al-Arabiya</a>. He said "I am telling them now, it may be the last minute, I'm telling them stop it. We are stronger."<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> Another 6 Qassams landed in southern Israel.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Proceeding">Proceeding</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Proceeding">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_the_Gaza_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Timeline of the Gaza War">Timeline of the Gaza War</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Incidents_in_the_Gaza_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Incidents in the Gaza War">Incidents in the Gaza War</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Israeli_offensive">Israeli offensive</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Israeli offensive">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Israel began planning for a military operation as early as six months before the conflict by collecting intelligence on potential targets. The IDF also engaged in a disinformation campaign to give Hamas a false sense of security and to take them by surprise. Defense minister <a href="/wiki/Ehud_Barak" title="Ehud Barak">Ehud Barak</a> stated that the offensive was the result of Israel's "patience running out" over the rocket attacks.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ravid_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ravid-123">[123]</a></sup> According to Israeli officials, its subsequent 27 December offensive took Hamas by surprise, thereby increasing militant casualties.<sup id="cite_ref-ravid_123-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ravid-123">[123]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Air_strikes">Air strikes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Air strikes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Oferet-Yetzuka-F16I.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Oferet-Yetzuka-F16I.jpg/220px-Oferet-Yetzuka-F16I.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Oferet-Yetzuka-F16I.jpg/330px-Oferet-Yetzuka-F16I.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Oferet-Yetzuka-F16I.jpg/440px-Oferet-Yetzuka-F16I.jpg 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Oferet-Yetzuka-F16I.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Israeli F-16I of the <a href="/wiki/107_Squadron_(Israel)" title="107 Squadron (Israel)">107th Squadron</a> preparing for <a href="/wiki/Takeoff" title="Takeoff">takeoff</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At 11:30&#160;am on 27 December 2008, Israel launched the campaign titled Operation Cast Lead. It began with an opening wave of <a href="/wiki/Airstrike" title="Airstrike">airstrikes</a> in which <a href="/wiki/F-16" class="mw-redirect" title="F-16">F-16</a> fighter jets and <a href="/wiki/AH-64_Apache" class="mw-redirect" title="AH-64 Apache">AH-64 Apache</a> attack helicopters<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> simultaneously struck 100 preplanned targets within a span of 220 seconds. There was a 95% success rate with zero misses in the opening attack according to the Israeli Air Force.<sup id="cite_ref-In_Gaza.2C_Both_Sides_Reveal_New_Gear_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-In_Gaza.2C_Both_Sides_Reveal_New_Gear-125">[125]</a></sup> Thirty minutes later, a second wave of 64 jets and helicopters struck at an additional 60 targets. The air strikes hit Hamas headquarters, government offices and 24 police stations.<sup id="cite_ref-Israeli_Arsenal_15-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Israeli_Arsenal-15">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-126">[126]</a></sup> An Israeli <a href="/wiki/Unmanned_aerial_vehicle" title="Unmanned aerial vehicle">UAV</a> airstrike on the police headquarters of Gaza City killed 40 people, including several dozen police cadets at their graduation ceremony.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> Approximately 140 members of Hamas were killed, including <a href="/wiki/Tawfik_Jaber" title="Tawfik Jaber">Tawfik Jaber</a>, head of Hamas' police force.<sup id="cite_ref-JPOST_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JPOST-128">[128]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Reuters1_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters1-129">[129]</a></sup> Israeli Foreign Minister Tzipi Livni told reporters that Israel would strike all targets associated with what she called the "illegitimate, terrorist government of Hamas".<sup id="cite_ref-In_Gaza.2C_Both_Sides_Reveal_New_Gear_125-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-In_Gaza.2C_Both_Sides_Reveal_New_Gear-125">[125]</a></sup></p>
<p>At least 225–230 Palestinians were killed and more than 700 injured on the first day of air strikes. Civilians, including children, were among the casualties.<sup id="cite_ref-Reuters1_129-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters1-129">[129]</a></sup> Although media reported that most of the dead were "Hamas security forces" or "Hamas operatives",<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> police officers are, according to <a href="/wiki/B%27Tselem" title="B'Tselem">B'Tselem</a>, presumed to be civilians and likely not legitimate objects of attack under international humanitarian law.<sup id="cite_ref-BTselem_explanation_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BTselem_explanation-132">[132]</a></sup> Human rights groups critically note that the attacks began around the time children were leaving school.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> The Israeli attack was the deadliest one-day death toll in 60 years of conflict between the Israelis and Palestinians, a day that was called the "Massacre of Black Saturday" by Palestinians in Gaza.<sup id="cite_ref-Alarabiya1_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alarabiya1-134">[134]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> Hamas responded with a rocket barrage on Southern Israel, and Palestinian factions in the Gaza Strip kept Southern Israel under constant rocket fire during the entire war. <a href="/wiki/Beersheba" title="Beersheba">Beersheba</a> suffered two rocket attacks, the farthest Palestinian rockets had ever reached. Palestinian rocket fire killed three Israeli civilians and one soldier in the early days of the conflict.<sup id="cite_ref-Timeline_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timeline-136">[136]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the weeks following the initial air raids <a href="/wiki/F-16I" class="mw-redirect" title="F-16I">F-16Is</a> and <a href="/wiki/AH-64_Apache" class="mw-redirect" title="AH-64 Apache">AH-64 Apaches</a> continued to target Hamas facilities while also inflicting severe damage to Palestinian infrastructure.<sup id="cite_ref-azcentral.com4Jan2009_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-azcentral.com4Jan2009-137">[137]</a></sup> Israel used the 2000-pound <a href="/wiki/Mark_84_bomb" title="Mark 84 bomb">Mark 84</a> <a href="/wiki/Joint_Direct_Attack_Munition" title="Joint Direct Attack Munition">Joint Direct Attack Munition</a> to attack buildings and tunnels along the Gaza-Sinai border. The 500-pound variant was used against underground bunkers.<sup id="cite_ref-In_Gaza.2C_Both_Sides_Reveal_New_Gear_125-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-In_Gaza.2C_Both_Sides_Reveal_New_Gear-125">[125]</a></sup> Israel also used the new PB500A1 laser-guided hard-target penetration bomb, which was developed by <a href="/wiki/Israel_Military_Industries" title="Israel Military Industries">Israel Military Industries</a>, and is based on the 1000-pound <a href="/wiki/Mark_83_bomb" title="Mark 83 bomb">Mark 83</a>. There were unconfirmed reports of the IAF also using the <a href="/wiki/GBU-39_Small_Diameter_Bomb" class="mw-redirect" title="GBU-39 Small Diameter Bomb">GBU-39 Small Diameter Bomb</a> for the first time.<sup id="cite_ref-Aviation_Week_2009-05-11_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Aviation_Week_2009-05-11-2">[2]</a></sup> Israeli aircraft also used synthetic aperture radar <a href="/wiki/Targeting_pods" class="mw-redirect" title="Targeting pods">targeting pods</a> and high-resolution imaging pods.<sup id="cite_ref-In_Gaza.2C_Both_Sides_Reveal_New_Gear_125-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-In_Gaza.2C_Both_Sides_Reveal_New_Gear-125">[125]</a></sup> After being grounded six months prior, the Israeli fleet of <a href="/wiki/AH-1_Cobra" class="mw-redirect" title="AH-1 Cobra">AH-1F Cobra</a> helicopter gunships were rushed back into service for the operation.<sup id="cite_ref-IPS_Arsenal_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IPS_Arsenal-138">[138]</a></sup> The Israeli Air Force also used <a href="/wiki/Unmanned_aerial_vehicle" title="Unmanned aerial vehicle">unmanned aerial vehicles</a> firing Israeli-manufactured <a href="/wiki/Spike_(missile)" title="Spike (missile)">Spike</a> missiles.</p>
<p>According to the IAF, 80% of the bombs used by the IAF were precision weapons, and 99% of the air strikes hit their targets.<sup id="cite_ref-Examining_the_Conduct_of_IDF_Operations_in_Gaza_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Examining_the_Conduct_of_IDF_Operations_in_Gaza-139">[139]</a></sup> A study by the <a href="/wiki/Center_for_Strategic_and_International_Studies" title="Center for Strategic and International Studies">Center for Strategic and International Studies</a> points out that when possible, IAF executed strikes using the smallest precision-guided weapons, and coordinated air strikes and the use of artillery weapons using GPS, in a systematic effort to limit collateral damage.<sup id="cite_ref-AnthonyHCordesman_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AnthonyHCordesman-76">[76]</a></sup> In a 2009 interview, Major General <a href="/wiki/Ido_Nehushtan" class="mw-redirect" title="Ido Nehushtan">Ido Nehushtan</a> said that the only use of non-<a href="/wiki/Precision-guided_munition" title="Precision-guided munition">precision-guided munitions</a> from the Israeli Air Force was in open areas.<sup id="cite_ref-DefenseNews_2009-03-08_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DefenseNews_2009-03-08-140">[140]</a></sup> He went on to say: "We had to find ways to do things as precisely and proportionately as possible, while focusing on how to differentiate between terrorists and uninvolved civilians.<sup id="cite_ref-DefenseNews_2009-03-08_140-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DefenseNews_2009-03-08-140">[140]</a></sup></p>
<p>The IDF also targeted homes of Hamas commanders, noting: "Destruction of hundreds of Hamas leaders' homes [is] one of the keys to the offensive's success. The homes serve as weapons warehouses and headquarters, and shelling them has seriously hindered Hamas capabilities."<sup id="cite_ref-Ynet_IDF_Ponders_Response_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ynet_IDF_Ponders_Response-141">[141]</a></sup> Several high-ranking Hamas commanders were killed, including <a href="/wiki/Nizar_Rayan" title="Nizar Rayan">Nizar Rayan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Abu_Zakaria_al-Jamal" title="Abu Zakaria al-Jamal">Abu Zakaria al-Jamal</a>, and Jamal Mamduch. Hamas leaders often died along with their families in their homes. According to a Hamas spokesperson and Rayyan's son, the IDF warned Rayan, by contacting his cell phone, that an attack on his house was imminent.<sup id="cite_ref-Independent_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Independent-142">[142]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-telegraph_rayan_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph_rayan-143">[143]</a></sup> Some Hamas leaders hid in the basements of the Shifa Hospital complex in Gaza City in the belief that they would be protected by human shields.<sup id="cite_ref-shifa_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shifa-144">[144]</a></sup> Hamas Interior Minister <a href="/wiki/Said_Seyam" title="Said Seyam">Said Seyam</a>, Hamas Interior Ministry Security Director Saleh Abu Sharkh, and local Hamas militia leader Mahmoud Abu Watfah were killed on 15 January in an Israeli airstrike in <a href="/wiki/Jabalia" title="Jabalia">Jabalia</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Orphanschoolmosque.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Orphanschoolmosque.jpg/220px-Orphanschoolmosque.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Orphanschoolmosque.jpg/330px-Orphanschoolmosque.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Orphanschoolmosque.jpg/440px-Orphanschoolmosque.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Orphanschoolmosque.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Destroyed building in <a href="/wiki/Rafah" title="Rafah">Rafah</a>, 12 January 2009</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Among IDF's measures to reduce civilian casualties were the extensive use of leaflets and phone messages to warn Palestinians, including families in high-risk areas and families of Hamas personnel, to leave the area or to avoid potential targets.<sup id="cite_ref-AnthonyHCordesman_76-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AnthonyHCordesman-76">[76]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-IDFphones_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IDFphones-145">[145]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nytimestraps_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimestraps-146">[146]</a></sup> Israel used A-4 Skyhawks to deliver more than 2 million leaflets urging the population to evacuate.<sup id="cite_ref-DefenseNews_2009-03-08_140-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DefenseNews_2009-03-08-140">[140]</a></sup> In a practice codenamed <a href="/wiki/Roof_knocking" title="Roof knocking">roof knocking</a>, the IDF issued warning calls before air strikes on civilian buildings. Typically, Israeli intelligence officers and <a href="/wiki/Shin_Bet" title="Shin Bet">Shin Bet</a> security servicemen contacted residents of a building in which they suspected storage of military assets and told them that they had 10–15 minutes to flee the attack.<sup id="cite_ref-In_Gaza.2C_Both_Sides_Reveal_New_Gear_125-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-In_Gaza.2C_Both_Sides_Reveal_New_Gear-125">[125]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-jpost_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jpost-147">[147]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-haretz-rk_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-haretz-rk-148">[148]</a></sup> At several instances, the IDF has also used a sound bomb to warn civilians before striking homes.<sup id="cite_ref-IDFphones_145-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IDFphones-145">[145]</a></sup> In some cases, IDF commanders called off airstrikes, when residents of suspected houses have been able to gather on its roof.<sup id="cite_ref-IDFphones_145-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IDFphones-145">[145]</a></sup> IAF developed small bomb that is designed not to explode as it was aimed at empty areas of the roofs to frighten residents into leaving the building.<sup id="cite_ref-AnthonyHCordesman_76-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AnthonyHCordesman-76">[76]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nytimestraps_146-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimestraps-146">[146]</a></sup> Israel's military used low-explosive missiles to warn civilians of imminent attack and to verify that buildings were evacuated before attacks.<sup id="cite_ref-DefenseNews_2009-03-08_140-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DefenseNews_2009-03-08-140">[140]</a></sup> Some of the attacks took place sooner than the warning suggested and many calls were not followed up with attacks.<sup id="cite_ref-ocha_report_1_2_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ocha_report_1_2-8">[8]</a></sup> The Israeli Government report notes that while the warning systems implemented by the IDF did not eliminate all harm to civilians, they were apparently effective, because in many incidents aerial video surveillance by IDF forces confirmed the departure of numerous residents from targeted areas as a direct result of the warnings before the attacks. While Israel is not a party to the <a href="/wiki/Protocol_I" title="Protocol I">Protocol I</a>, Israel accepts its provisions as reflective of customary international law.<sup id="cite_ref-Factual_and_legal_aspects_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Factual_and_legal_aspects-149">[149]</a></sup></p>
<p>By 3 January 2009, the Palestinian death toll stood at 400, with 25% estimated to be civilian casualties.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> The air offensive continued throughout the ground invasion that followed, and as of 15 January Israeli forces had carried out 2,360 air strikes.<sup id="cite_ref-Sengupta1501_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sengupta1501-151">[151]</a></sup> No safe haven or bomb shelters existed, making this one of the rare conflicts where civilians had no place to flee.<sup id="cite_ref-ocha_report_1_7_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ocha_report_1_7-152">[152]</a></sup> The IAF had so far carried out 555 aerial sorties and 125 helicopter missions, and dozens of <a href="/wiki/Unmanned_aerial_vehicle" title="Unmanned aerial vehicle">UAV</a> flight hours were logged.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Naval_operations">Naval operations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Naval operations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Israeli_Navy" title="Israeli Navy">Israeli Navy</a> attacked Hamas' rocket launchers and outposts, command and control centers, a Hamas patrol boat, and the office of Hamas Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Ismail_Haniyeh" title="Ismail Haniyeh">Ismail Haniyeh</a>, using the <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Weapon_System" class="mw-redirect" title="Typhoon Weapon System">Typhoon Weapon System</a> and <a href="/wiki/Surface_to_surface_missile" class="mw-redirect" title="Surface to surface missile">Surface to surface missiles</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup> The navy coordinated with other Israeli forces and used powerful shipboard sensors to acquire and shell targets on land.<sup id="cite_ref-In_Gaza.2C_Both_Sides_Reveal_New_Gear_125-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-In_Gaza.2C_Both_Sides_Reveal_New_Gear-125">[125]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DefenseNews_2009-05-11_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DefenseNews_2009-05-11-155">[155]</a></sup> Records of the attacks published by the navy indicate that for the first time vessels were equipped with <a href="/wiki/Spike_(missile)" title="Spike (missile)">Spike ER</a> electro-optically guided anti-armor missiles. Videos of an attack showed precision hits from a <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Weapon_System" class="mw-redirect" title="Typhoon Weapon System">Typhoon</a> stabilizing gun despite a rolling sea. Versions of the Spike were also used by ground units<sup id="cite_ref-Aviation_Week_2009-05-11_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Aviation_Week_2009-05-11-2">[2]</a></sup> and possibly by helicopters or <a href="/wiki/Unmanned_aerial_vehicle" title="Unmanned aerial vehicle">unmanned aerial vehicles</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Shayetet_13" title="Shayetet 13">Shayetet 13</a> naval <a href="/wiki/Commando" title="Commando">commandos</a> were also deployed to attack targets on land,<sup id="cite_ref-Haaretz_2009-01-15_21-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Haaretz_2009-01-15-21">[21]</a></sup> and reportedly attacked an <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iranian</a> ship loaded with arms for Hamas, which was docking in <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> On 28 December, Naval vessels shelled the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Gaza" title="Port of Gaza">Port of Gaza</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Timeline_136-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timeline-136">[136]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 29 December, the <a href="/wiki/Free_Gaza_Movement" title="Free Gaza Movement">Free Gaza Movement</a> relief boat <i>Dignity</i> carrying volunteer doctors with 3.5 tons of medical supplies, human rights activists (Among them <a href="/wiki/Caoimhe_Butterly" title="Caoimhe Butterly">Caoimhe Butterly</a> and former <a href="/wiki/United_States_Representative" class="mw-redirect" title="United States Representative">US Representative</a> <a href="/wiki/Cynthia_McKinney" title="Cynthia McKinney">Cynthia McKinney</a>), and a <a href="/wiki/CNN" title="CNN">CNN</a> reporter was involved in an altercation with Israeli patrol boats. The captain of the Free Gaza vessel said that their vessel had been rammed intentionally and that there had been no warning before it had been rammed.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup> An Israeli spokesman disputed this, and said the collision was caused by the <i>Dignity</i> attempting to outmaneuver the patrol boats after disobeying Israeli orders to turn back.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 4 January the Israeli Navy extended its blockade of the Gaza Strip to 20 nautical miles.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup></p>
<p>Throughout the war, the Israeli Navy employed <a href="/wiki/Sa%27ar_4.5_class_missile_boat" class="mw-redirect" title="Sa'ar 4.5 class missile boat">Sa'ar 4.5 class missile boats</a> and <a href="/wiki/Super_Dvora_Mk_III_class_patrol_boat" class="mw-redirect" title="Super Dvora Mk III class patrol boat">Super Dvora Mk III class patrol boats</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Ground_invasion">Ground invasion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Ground invasion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/2009_Ibrahim_al-Maqadna_Mosque_strike" title="2009 Ibrahim al-Maqadna Mosque strike">2009 Ibrahim al-Maqadna Mosque strike</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zeitoun_incident" title="Zeitoun incident">Zeitoun incident</a></div>
<p>IDF infantry and armor units amassed near the Gaza border on 28 December, engaging in a <a href="/wiki/Blockade" title="Blockade">blockade</a> of the strip.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gazasmoke.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Gazasmoke.JPG/220px-Gazasmoke.JPG" width="220" height="178" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Gazasmoke.JPG/330px-Gazasmoke.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Gazasmoke.JPG/440px-Gazasmoke.JPG 2x" data-file-width="541" data-file-height="438" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gazasmoke.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Explosion in Gaza, 12 January 2009<sup id="cite_ref-War_On_Gaza_Day_17_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-War_On_Gaza_Day_17-161">[161]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Samouni2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Samouni2.jpg/220px-Samouni2.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Samouni2.jpg/330px-Samouni2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Samouni2.jpg/440px-Samouni2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="450" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Samouni2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/International_Solidarity_Movement" title="International Solidarity Movement">ISM</a> photo:"Damage to the Zeitoun neighbourhood"</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On the evening of 3 January Israel began the ground operation with a massive <a href="/wiki/Artillery" title="Artillery">artillery</a> barrage all along the Gaza boundary, and ground forces were sent into Gaza for the first time since the start of the conflict.<sup id="cite_ref-Time_January_3.2C_2009_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Time_January_3.2C_2009-162">[162]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-haaretz-groundInvasion_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-haaretz-groundInvasion-163">[163]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ynet_ground_troops_started_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ynet_ground_troops_started-164">[164]</a></sup> The ground invasion, termed the 'second stage' of Operation Cast Lead, sought to control open areas and encircle towns and refugee camps from which militants continued to launch rockets, but not penetrate densely populated areas.<sup id="cite_ref-Israeli_Arsenal_15-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Israeli_Arsenal-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Paratroopers_Brigade" title="Paratroopers Brigade">Paratroopers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Golani_Brigade" title="Golani Brigade">Golani</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Givati_Brigade" title="Givati Brigade">Givati</a> brigades simultaneously entered the Gaza Strip from several unexpected directions to avoid reported <a href="/wiki/Booby_trap" title="Booby trap">booby traps</a> while also outflanking opposing forces. The <a href="/wiki/401st_Brigade_(IDF)" title="401st Brigade (IDF)">401st Armored Brigade</a> used <a href="/wiki/Merkava" title="Merkava">Merkava Mark IV</a> tanks to quickly block access from Rafah and Khan Yunis to Gaza City, cutting supply lines to Hamas from the south.<sup id="cite_ref-Aviation_Week_2009-05-11_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Aviation_Week_2009-05-11-2">[2]</a></sup> The move put psychological pressure on Hamas while also forcing combatants to withdraw from the front line. Israeli forces took strategic hilltops to better control areas.<sup id="cite_ref-Time_January_3.2C_2009_162-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Time_January_3.2C_2009-162">[162]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_Weapons_Found_in_a_Mosque_During_Cast_Lead_(2).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_Weapons_Found_in_a_Mosque_During_Cast_Lead_%282%29.jpg/220px-Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_Weapons_Found_in_a_Mosque_During_Cast_Lead_%282%29.jpg" width="220" height="327" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_Weapons_Found_in_a_Mosque_During_Cast_Lead_%282%29.jpg/330px-Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_Weapons_Found_in_a_Mosque_During_Cast_Lead_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_Weapons_Found_in_a_Mosque_During_Cast_Lead_%282%29.jpg/440px-Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_Weapons_Found_in_a_Mosque_During_Cast_Lead_%282%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1417" data-file-height="2105" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_Weapons_Found_in_a_Mosque_During_Cast_Lead_(2).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Weapons found in a mosque during Operation Cast Lead, according to the IDF</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Israeli advance was spearheaded by <a href="/wiki/Combat_Engineering_Corps" title="Combat Engineering Corps">Combat Engineering Corps</a> sappers opening routes and allowing the ground forces to advance while dismantling <a href="/wiki/Booby_trap" title="Booby trap">booby traps</a> set up in great numbers by Hamas, often set to detonate upon entry to a building. <a href="/wiki/Improvised_explosive_device" title="Improvised explosive device">Improvised explosive devices</a> (IED) were a concern for Israeli soldiers.<sup id="cite_ref-Belfast_Telegraph_2010-02-04_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Belfast_Telegraph_2010-02-04-25">[25]</a></sup> One Israeli commander said that booby traps were found in a mosque and one-third of the houses. He said that some of the traps were designed to assist in taking IDF soldiers captive. All such attempts failed.<sup id="cite_ref-jpost.com_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jpost.com-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NY_Times_2009-01-16_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NY_Times_2009-01-16-165">[165]</a></sup> The IDF used <a href="/wiki/IDF_Caterpillar_D9" title="IDF Caterpillar D9">D9 armored bulldozers</a> to ensure that paths were cleared of IEDs. These bulldozers were also used to destroy tunnels. The unmanned, remote-controlled version of the D9 (called Black Thunder) were also used. In one case an armored D9 knocked down a door, which triggered an explosion of a building full of explosive on top of the D9. The D9 survived the explosion and building's collapse. <a href="/wiki/Combat_engineer" title="Combat engineer">Combat engineers</a> that inspected the rubbles found a tunnel, cache of weapons and remains of a <a href="/wiki/Suicide_bomber" class="mw-redirect" title="Suicide bomber">suicide bomber</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup> Viper miniature robots were deployed by Israeli forces for the first time. These were used for various tasks including the disabling of IEDs. Along with blocking mobile phone communication, the IDF employed electronic jamming equipment to disable remote operated explosives.<sup id="cite_ref-IPS_Arsenal_138-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IPS_Arsenal-138">[138]</a></sup> Among others, The IDF used the new Bull Island system for the first time to identify booby traps in buildings. Bull Island uses a camera shaped like a tennis ball that can be thrown into a building to transfer 360-degree imagery to the troops outside of the structure.<sup id="cite_ref-Israeli_Arsenal_15-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Israeli_Arsenal-15">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Aviation_Week_2009-02-23_17-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Aviation_Week_2009-02-23-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>Israeli artillery units worked closely with battalion commanders.<sup id="cite_ref-DefenseNews_2009-05-11_155-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DefenseNews_2009-05-11-155">[155]</a></sup> For the first time, the Sheder Ham digitized data, mapping, and command-and-control system linked the Artillery Corps into the Army's overall C4I network.<sup id="cite_ref-IPS_Arsenal_138-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IPS_Arsenal-138">[138]</a></sup> Israel artillery fired approximately 7,000 rounds during the conflict. An Israel Defense Forces colonel stated that tactics and procedures had to suit the difficult urban environment. The number of rounds in the 22-day conflict was 5% of the total fired during the 34-day Lebanon war. Under the condition of anonymity, another officer said that close air support missions accounted for more than 90% of rounds fired. He also said that about half of those were MA25A1 incendiary-based smoke rounds used to mask troop movements.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Oketz_Unit" title="Oketz Unit">Oketz Unit</a>, the IDF's dog-handling corps, performed 33 successful missions during the war, with specially trained sniffer and attack dogs and their handlers leading advancing forces. In every mission that involved Oketz dogs, there were no casualties among soldiers. Three dogs were killed by enemy fire during the war.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup></p>
<p>Hamas guerrillas sometimes emerged from tunnels to fire at IDF soldiers, then pulled back to lure troops into built-up areas. In one case, a Palestinian dressed in an Israeli Army uniform opened fire on a group of soldiers, but was killed before he could cause any casualties. In several instances, would-be <a href="/wiki/Suicide_bomber" class="mw-redirect" title="Suicide bomber">suicide bombers</a> with explosive vests charged Israeli soldiers, but all were killed before they could reach their targets.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup></p>
<p>Israeli ground troops entered Beit Lahiya and Beit Hanoun in northern Gaza in the early hours of 4 January.<sup id="cite_ref-aljazeera4jan_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aljazeera4jan-169">[169]</a></sup> Israeli forces reportedly bisected Gaza and surrounded <a href="/wiki/Gaza_City" title="Gaza City">Gaza City</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-haaretz-groundInvasion_163-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-haaretz-groundInvasion-163">[163]</a></sup> but restricted their movements to areas that were not heavily urbanised.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The IDF stated that it had targeted forty sites, including weapons depots and rocket launch sites. The Israeli military said that 50 Hamas fighters were killed and dozens more wounded.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup> At least 25 Palestinian rockets were fired into Southern Israel, wounding a woman in <a href="/wiki/Sderot" title="Sderot">Sderot</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Timeline_136-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timeline-136">[136]</a></sup> One Israeli soldier was killed and 19 other soldiers were wounded in <a href="/wiki/Jabalia" title="Jabalia">Jabalia</a> when a mortar shell fired by Hamas fighters landed on their patrol.</p>
<p>As Israeli tanks and troops seized control of large parts of the Gaza Strip, tens of thousands of Gazans fled their homes amid artillery and gunfire, and flooded into the inner parts of Gaza city.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup> On 5 January, IDF forces began operating in the densely populated urban centers of Gaza. Gun battles broke out between the IDF and Hamas on the streets of Gaza as the IDF surrounded the city.<sup id="cite_ref-reutersjan5_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reutersjan5-172">[172]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup> IDF combat units were sent in to capture Hamas fighters, and were met with grenades and mortar fire. The Israeli military said that 80–100 Hamas fighters were killed and 100 captured during heavy ground fighting. Some 40 rockets and mortar shells were fired at Israel, injuring four civilians.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup> Israel continued to launch airstrikes and naval bombardments.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hamas_Hides_Launcher_in_Mosque_During_Cast_Lead.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Hamas_Hides_Launcher_in_Mosque_During_Cast_Lead.jpg/220px-Hamas_Hides_Launcher_in_Mosque_During_Cast_Lead.jpg" width="220" height="328" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Hamas_Hides_Launcher_in_Mosque_During_Cast_Lead.jpg/330px-Hamas_Hides_Launcher_in_Mosque_During_Cast_Lead.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Hamas_Hides_Launcher_in_Mosque_During_Cast_Lead.jpg/440px-Hamas_Hides_Launcher_in_Mosque_During_Cast_Lead.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1417" data-file-height="2110" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hamas_Hides_Launcher_in_Mosque_During_Cast_Lead.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
IDF forces discover weapons in a mosque during Operation Cast Lead in the Gaza Strip.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 6 January, heavy fighting took place between Israeli troops and Palestinian militants on the outskirts of the northern district of Gaza City, while Israeli helicopter gunships pounded militant positions. The IDF reportedly widened its attacks to <a href="/wiki/Khan_Yunis" title="Khan Yunis">Khan Yunis</a> in southern Gaza, after heavy fighting on the edges of <a href="/wiki/Deir_al-Balah" title="Deir al-Balah">Deir al-Balah</a> in central Gaza.<sup id="cite_ref-Timeline_136-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timeline-136">[136]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Al-Fakhura_school_incident" title="Al-Fakhura school incident">Al Fakhura school</a> was hit by Israeli mortar fire, and reports on deaths and if militants were among the casualties varied.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-jpost_idf_releases_177-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jpost_idf_releases-177">[177]</a></sup> The attack was originally reported as being on the school.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup> In northern Gaza City, Palestinian gunmen ambushed an Israeli patrol, killing one soldier and wounding four.
