The patrol returned fire, hitting some of the gunmen,<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup> while in <a href="/wiki/Jabalya" class="mw-redirect" title="Jabalya">Jabalya</a>, an Israeli tank fired a shell into an abandoned building as <a href="/wiki/Golani_Brigade" title="Golani Brigade">Golani Brigade</a> soldiers were taking cover in it, killing 3 soldiers and wounding 24. The casualties were extracted under the cover of heavy artillery fire and helicopters dropping illumination bombs.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup> In a separate friendly fire incident, an Israeli officer was killed by a misdirected artillery shell. In all, at least 70 Palestinians and 5 Israelis were killed on 6 January.<sup id="cite_ref-Timeline_136-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timeline-136">[136]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Arms_interdiction_and_the_Sudan_strike">Arms interdiction and the Sudan strike</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Arms interdiction and the Sudan strike">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2009_Sudan_airstrikes" title="2009 Sudan airstrikes">2009 Sudan airstrikes</a></div>
<p>In January and February 2009, there was a series of two air strikes in <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a> and one in the <a href="/wiki/Red_Sea" title="Red Sea">Red Sea</a> allegedly conducted by Israel against a convoy of 17 trucks containing <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iranian</a> arms, possibly <a href="/wiki/Fajr-3" title="Fajr-3">Fajr-3</a> artillery rockets, being smuggled to the Gaza Strip through Sudan. A total of 39 were reported killed, with Iranian Revolutionary Guard operatives possibly among the dead.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-haaretz0328_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-haaretz0328-182">[182]</a></sup> The attack was widely reported to have been conducted by Israeli aircraft, while the Israeli government hinted that it was behind the attack.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup> Naval commandos from the elite <a href="/wiki/Shayetet_13" title="Shayetet 13">Shayetet 13</a> unit were reportedly involved in the operation, which included an attack on an Iranian arms ship docking in <a href="/wiki/Port_Sudan" title="Port Sudan">Port Sudan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Attack_on_Gaza_City">Attack on Gaza City</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Attack on Gaza City">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:GazaWPshelling.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/GazaWPshelling.gif/220px-GazaWPshelling.gif" width="220" height="179" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/GazaWPshelling.gif/330px-GazaWPshelling.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b8/GazaWPshelling.gif 2x" data-file-width="428" data-file-height="349" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:GazaWPshelling.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Phosphorus" title="Phosphorus">Phosphorus</a> <a href="/wiki/Cluster_bombs" class="mw-redirect" title="Cluster bombs">cluster bombs</a> dropped on populated areas on 11 January</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 7 January, Israel carried out 40 airstrikes overnight. Dozens of other targets were attacked by aircraft and artillery during the day, and the Gaza-Egypt border was bombed after Israeli aircraft dropped leaflets onto <a href="/wiki/Rafah" title="Rafah">Rafah</a>, urging the residents to leave. A total of 20 Palestinians were killed. A total of 20 rockets were fired into Southern Israel.<sup id="cite_ref-Timeline_136-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timeline-136">[136]</a></sup> Israel temporarily halted its attacks for three hours to provide a "humanitarian respite".<sup id="cite_ref-Al_Jazeera_Timeline_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Al_Jazeera_Timeline-185">[185]</a></sup> On 8 January, an exchange of fire took place in Gaza City. Hamas suffered heavy losses, but an Israeli officer of the <a href="/wiki/Golani_Brigade" title="Golani Brigade">Golani Brigade</a> was also killed. In Northern Gaza, snipers opened fire on Israeli forces conducting an operation, killing an Israeli soldier. Another Israeli soldier was lightly wounded. The IDF soldiers identified the origin of the fire and returned fire, directly hitting the snipers. In another incident, several mortar shells were fired at <a href="/wiki/Givati_Brigade" title="Givati Brigade">Givati Brigade</a> soldiers, who responded with mortar fire and were aided by IAF airstrikes.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup> In Central Gaza, a force of IDF soldiers entered a building near the Kissfum crossing. As the force entered, Hamas fighters fired an anti-tank rocket at them, killing one Israeli officer and wounding one soldier. Israeli aircraft also hit more than 40 Hamas targets in Gaza.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup> Israeli troops shot and killed Hamas commander Amir Mansi and wounded two other Hamas fighters as they operated a mortar.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup> The IAF attacked over 60 Hamas targets. A rocket fired from Gaza wounded seven IDF soldiers in Southern Israel. On 10 January, the Israeli military said that another 40 sites were targeted, and that 15 Hamas fighters were killed.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup> On 11 January, the IDF started the third stage of the operation with an attack on the suburbs of <a href="/wiki/Gaza_City" title="Gaza City">Gaza City</a>. Israeli forces pushed into the south of the city and reached a key junction to its north. During their advance, Hamas and Islamic Jihad fighters ambushed Israeli troops at several locations, and heavy fighting ensued, in which 40 Hamas and Islamic Jihad fighters were killed.<sup id="cite_ref-JPOST_128-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JPOST-128">[128]</a></sup> Additionally, the IAF reported that Hamas operatives had tried to shoot down an IAF plane with <a href="/wiki/Anti-Aircraft" class="mw-redirect" title="Anti-Aircraft">anti-aircraft missiles</a> for the first time since operations in Gaza began. Heavy machine gun fire against helicopters had also been unsuccessful.<sup id="cite_ref-haaretz-Hamas-fired-missiles_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-haaretz-Hamas-fired-missiles-26">[26]</a></sup> Two Hamas fighters were killed by an Israeli airstrike in the Southern Gaza Strip. A Palestinian woman was also killed by Israeli artillery fire.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup> Israeli forces continued to push deeper into heavily populated areas around Gaza City. Fierce clashes were reported in the Southern suburb of <a href="/wiki/Sheikh_Ijlin" title="Sheikh Ijlin">Sheikh Ajleen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Timeline_136-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timeline-136">[136]</a></sup> On 12 January, nearly 30 rockets and mortars were fired at Southern Israel, damaging a house in <a href="/wiki/Ashkelon" title="Ashkelon">Ashkelon</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Day_18_of_War_on_Gaza.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Day_18_of_War_on_Gaza.PNG/220px-Day_18_of_War_on_Gaza.PNG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Day_18_of_War_on_Gaza.PNG/330px-Day_18_of_War_on_Gaza.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Day_18_of_War_on_Gaza.PNG/440px-Day_18_of_War_on_Gaza.PNG 2x" data-file-width="768" data-file-height="576" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Day_18_of_War_on_Gaza.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Palestinian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Palestinian people">Palestinians</a> in a Gaza city neighbourhood on Day 18 of the War in Gaza<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 13 January, Israeli tanks continued their advance toward the headquarters of Hamas' preventive security building from the al-Karramah neighborhood in the northwest and the <a href="/wiki/Tel_al-Hawa" title="Tel al-Hawa">Tel al-Hawa</a> neighborhood in the northeast. The Israeli Army also said that 25 mortars and rockets were fired into Southern Israel.<sup id="cite_ref-Timeline_136-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timeline-136">[136]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup> Before dawn, during the night, Israeli troops and tanks supported by artillery and helicopters advanced 300 metres into Tel al-Hawa, a neighborhood with several high-rise buildings, while Israeli gunboats shelled Hamas targets along the coast.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup> As troops entered the narrow streets, heavy street fighting with militants ensued leaving three Israeli soldiers wounded and 30 Hamas militants dead or wounded, according to the IDF. By morning IDF soldiers were still advancing slowly towards the city center and several buildings were in flames in Tel al-Hawa, where most of the fighting took place. Five Israeli soldiers were wounded during clashes with militants, and an officer was severely wounded by an explosion inside a booby-trapped building.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup> The push into the neighorhood was Israel's deepest incursion into Gaza City. There was widespread <a href="/wiki/Desertion" title="Desertion">desertion</a> by members of the Qassam Brigades in the face of the IDF advance.<sup id="cite_ref-jpost.com_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jpost.com-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 15 January, Israeli <a href="/wiki/Artillery" title="Artillery">artillery</a> started an intense bombardment of the city while fighting was still going on in the streets. Troops and tanks advanced deeper into the city following the shelling. The Israeli military claimed to have killed dozens of militants since breaching the city limits four days earlier, while they suffered 20–25 soldiers wounded. Among buildings hit by shellfire was the al-Quds hospital, Gaza's second-largest, in the <a href="/wiki/Tel_al-Hawa" title="Tel al-Hawa">Tel al-Hawa</a> neighborhood. At least 14 rockets were fired from Gaza into Israel, wounding five and severely damaging a house in <a href="/wiki/Sderot" title="Sderot">Sderot</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Timeline_136-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timeline-136">[136]</a></sup></p>
<p>Almost all members of Hamas' approximately 100-man strong "Iranian Unit" were killed during a battle in the Zeytoun neighborhood on 15 January. Members of the military wing had previously travelled to Iran for training by the Iranian Revolutionary Guard. According to Palestinian sources, Iran was preparing for an end to the fighting and promised money and resources to rebuild military capabilities and infrastructure destroyed during the fighting.<sup id="cite_ref-Haaretz_2001-01-16_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Haaretz_2001-01-16-195">[195]</a></sup></p>
<p>The headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Relief_and_Works_Agency" class="mw-redirect" title="United Nations Relief and Works Agency">United Nations Relief and Works Agency</a> (UNRWA) was also shelled on 15 January. There were 3 people injured and tons of food and fuel intended for 750,000 Palestinian refugees were destroyed.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup> The Associated Press initially reported that an anonymous Israeli military official stated that Gaza militants had fired anti-tank weapons and machine guns from inside the compound. Israeli Prime Minister Ehud Olmert said "it is absolutely true that we were attacked from that place, but the consequences are very sad and we apologize for it, I don't think it should have happened and I'm very sorry." After UNRWA dismissed this as "nonsense", Israel ordered an army investigation into the incident.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup> Israeli officials afterwards "came forward to say that preliminary results showed that the militants ran for safety inside the U.N. compound after firing on Israeli forces from outside".<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 16 January, more than 50 Israeli airstrikes were carried out against militants, tunnels, and a mosque suspected of being used as a weapons store. Israeli forces continued their push into Gaza City, while <a href="/wiki/Israeli_Navy" title="Israeli Navy">Israeli Navy</a> vessels shelled militant targets in support.<sup id="cite_ref-Al_Jazeera_Timeline_185-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Al_Jazeera_Timeline-185">[185]</a></sup> About 10 rockets were fired into Southern Israel.<sup id="cite_ref-Timeline_136-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timeline-136">[136]</a></sup> Palestinian militants fired 15 rockets into Israel, wounding eight people including a pregnant woman.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Givati_Brigade" title="Givati Brigade">Givati Brigade</a> penetrated the deepest into Gaza City. The brigade's reconnaissance battalion swept into the Tel al-Hawa neighborhood and took over two 15-story buildings in search of Hamas operatives two days before the cease fire went into effect. About 40 Palestinian fighters were killed during the operation. The commander of the brigade, Colonel Ilan Malka, was critical of Hamas' use of civilian houses and said that he "took many steps to prevent our soldiers from getting hurt". Malka told reporters that the IDF had initially predicted each battalion would lose six or seven soldiers.<sup id="cite_ref-A_necessary_operation_199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A_necessary_operation-199">[199]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Israeli government considered a third phase of the operation with the intent of dealing a "knock out blow" to Hamas. Military and intelligence assessments indicating that shifting the goal to destroying Hamas would require additional weeks of deep ground incursions into urban areas and refugee camps. This was expected to result in heavy casualties on both sides and among civilians, reduce the strong domestic support for the war, and increase international criticism.<sup id="cite_ref-Israeli_Arsenal_15-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Israeli_Arsenal-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Humanitarian_ceasefires">Humanitarian ceasefires</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Humanitarian ceasefires">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Due to the number of civilian casualties and the deteriorating humanitarian situation, Israel faced significant international pressure for a ceasefire, the establishment of a <a href="/wiki/Humanitarian_corridor" title="Humanitarian corridor">humanitarian corridor</a>, access to the population of Gaza and the lifting of the blockade.<sup id="cite_ref-UN-090107Humanitarian_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN-090107Humanitarian-200">[200]</a></sup> On 7 January, Israel opened a humanitarian corridor to allow the shipment of aid into Gaza. The Israeli army agreed to interrupt fighting for three hours and Hamas agreed not to launch rockets during the pause.<sup id="cite_ref-VOAtruce_201-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VOAtruce-201">[201]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-recess_203-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-recess-203">[203]</a></sup> Israel repeated the ceasefire either daily or every other day. Aid officials and the UN praised the truce, but said it was not enough as fighting usually resumed immediately following the humanitarian ceasefires.<sup id="cite_ref-VOAtruce_201-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VOAtruce-201">[201]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mars_204-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mars-204">[204]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Haaretz_truce_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Haaretz_truce-205">[205]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-HumanitarianTruce_206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HumanitarianTruce-206">[206]</a></sup> An Israeli Government report, published in July 2009, notes that during the period between 8 and 17 January, Hamas fired a total of 44 rockets and mortars at Israel during humanitarian pauses.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup> An independent report commissioned jointly by the Israeli NGO <a href="/wiki/Physicians_for_Human_Rights" title="Physicians for Human Rights">Physicians for Human Rights</a> and the Palestinian Medical Relief Society notes that according to testimonies by local witnesses, there were several cases where IDF ground forces breached the daily ceasefire agreement.<sup id="cite_ref-PHR-PMRS_208-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PHR-PMRS-208">[208]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Palestinian_paramilitary_activity">Palestinian paramilitary activity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Palestinian paramilitary activity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:A_rocket_fired_from_a_civilian_area_in_Gaza_towards_civilian_areas_in_Southern_Israel.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/A_rocket_fired_from_a_civilian_area_in_Gaza_towards_civilian_areas_in_Southern_Israel.jpg/220px-A_rocket_fired_from_a_civilian_area_in_Gaza_towards_civilian_areas_in_Southern_Israel.jpg" width="220" height="140" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/A_rocket_fired_from_a_civilian_area_in_Gaza_towards_civilian_areas_in_Southern_Israel.jpg/330px-A_rocket_fired_from_a_civilian_area_in_Gaza_towards_civilian_areas_in_Southern_Israel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/A_rocket_fired_from_a_civilian_area_in_Gaza_towards_civilian_areas_in_Southern_Israel.jpg/440px-A_rocket_fired_from_a_civilian_area_in_Gaza_towards_civilian_areas_in_Southern_Israel.jpg 2x" data-file-width="995" data-file-height="635" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:A_rocket_fired_from_a_civilian_area_in_Gaza_towards_civilian_areas_in_Southern_Israel.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
According to <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a> rockets from Gaza were fired from populated areas.<sup id="cite_ref-Human_Rights_Watch.2C_Rockets_from_Gaza_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Human_Rights_Watch.2C_Rockets_from_Gaza-209">[209]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>According to Abu Ahmed, the official media spokesman of the <a href="/wiki/Al-Quds_Brigades" title="Al-Quds Brigades">Al-Quds Brigades</a>, the military wing of the <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Jihad_Movement_in_Palestine" title="Islamic Jihad Movement in Palestine">Palestinian Islamic Jihad</a> movement, Palestinian paramilitary factions in Gaza worked together, operationally and otherwise, to repel the Israeli attack on Gaza. Abu Ahmed told <i><a href="/wiki/Asharq_al-Awsat" class="mw-redirect" title="Asharq al-Awsat">Asharq al-Awsat</a></i> during the war that, "everybody helps everybody else with regards to food, weapons, and first aid; there is no difference between a member 'Al Quds Brigade' or 'Al Qassam Brigade [military wing of Hamas]' or 'Al-Aqsa Martyrs Brigade' or 'Abu Ali Mustafa Brigade [military wing of Popular Front for the Liberation of Palestine or PFLP]'. For everybody's goal is the same and their compass is pointing in the same direction, and that is to drive out the occupation and defeat them, and disrupt their plan to dissolve the Palestinian Cause."<sup id="cite_ref-Sharq_210-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sharq-210">[210]</a></sup> Hamas said that "rockets fired from Gaza were meant to hit military targets, but because they are unguided, they hit civilians by mistake."<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_211-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-211">[211]</a></sup></p>
<p>Political representatives for Hamas, Islamic Jihad, the PFLP, <a href="/wiki/As-Sa%27iqa" title="As-Sa'iqa">Saiqa</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Popular_Struggle_Front" class="mw-redirect" title="Popular Struggle Front">Popular Struggle Front</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Revolutionary_Palestinian_Communist_Party" title="Revolutionary Palestinian Communist Party">Revolutionary Communist Party</a>, <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_Liberation_Organisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Palestinian Liberation Organisation">Palestinian Liberation Organisation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fatah" title="Fatah">Fatah</a>'s 'Intifada' faction, and a number of other Palestinian factions in <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a> formed a temporary alliance during the offensive as well. They issued a joint statement refusing "any security arrangements that affect the resistance and its legitimate right to struggle against the occupation", and refusing proposals suggesting international forces be sent to Gaza. The coalition also affirmed that any peace initiatives must include an end to the blockade, and an opening of all of Gaza's crossings, including the Rafah crossing with Egypt.<sup id="cite_ref-Bauer0123_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bauer0123-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Preparation">Preparation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Preparation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:191px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Grad_Beersheba.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Grad_Beersheba.jpg/189px-Grad_Beersheba.jpg" width="189" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Grad_Beersheba.jpg/284px-Grad_Beersheba.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Grad_Beersheba.jpg/378px-Grad_Beersheba.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Grad_Beersheba.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A Grad rocket hitting Beersheba.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Hamas used the months leading to the war to prepare for urban warfare, which was to give them a chance to inflict casualties on the Israeli military.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">[212]</a></sup> Militants booby-trapped houses and buildings and built an extensive system of tunnels in preparation for combat.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">[213]</a></sup> A Hamas fighter reported that the group had prepared a tunnel network in Gaza city that would allow Hamas to engage the IDF in urban warfare.<sup id="cite_ref-times12Jan_214-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-times12Jan-214">[214]</a></sup> IDF commanders said that many Hamas members have dug tunnels for themselves under their homes and hid weapon caches in them.<sup id="cite_ref-IDF:_Hamas_built_underground_city_215-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IDF:_Hamas_built_underground_city-215">[215]</a></sup> Some houses were booby-trapped with mannequins, explosives and adjacent tunnels: Israeli officers said that houses were set up this way so that "Israeli soldiers would shoot the mannequin, mistaking it for a man; an explosion would occur; and the soldiers would be driven or pulled into the hole, where they could be taken prisoner." A colonel estimated that one-third of all houses encountered were booby-trapped.<sup id="cite_ref-NY_Times_2009-01-16_165-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NY_Times_2009-01-16-165">[165]</a></sup> IDF Brigadier-General Eyal Eisenberg said that roadside bombs were planted in TV satellite dishes, adding that Hamas booby-trapping of homes and schools was "monstrous" and "inhumane".<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">[216]</a></sup> Ron Ben-Yishai, an Israeli military correspondent embedded with invading ground forces, stated that entire blocks of houses were booby-trapped and wired in preparation for urban confrontation with the IDF. Israel said a map showing the deployment of explosives and Hamas forces in the al-Atatra neighborhood in northern Gaza was found. The map reportedly showed that Hamas placed many explosives and firing positions in residential areas, several mosques, and next to a gas station.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">[217]</a></sup> Israel deployed the elite <a href="/wiki/Sayeret_Yahalom" class="mw-redirect" title="Sayeret Yahalom">Sayeret Yahalom</a> combat engineering unit throughout the brigades with new equipment including miniature robots and improved wall-breaching munitions to counter the booby-traps.<sup id="cite_ref-Aviation_Week_2009-05-11_2-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Aviation_Week_2009-05-11-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_Weapons_Cache_in_Northern_Gaza.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_Weapons_Cache_in_Northern_Gaza.jpg/220px-Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_Weapons_Cache_in_Northern_Gaza.jpg" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_Weapons_Cache_in_Northern_Gaza.jpg/330px-Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_Weapons_Cache_in_Northern_Gaza.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_Weapons_Cache_in_Northern_Gaza.jpg/440px-Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_Weapons_Cache_in_Northern_Gaza.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1936" data-file-height="2574" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_Weapons_Cache_in_Northern_Gaza.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
An example of a weapons cache found in northern Gaza.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>According to <i><a href="/wiki/Jane%27s_Defence_Weekly" title="Jane's Defence Weekly">Jane's Defence Weekly</a></i>, armed groups in Gaza counted <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_domestic_weapons_production" title="Palestinian domestic weapons production">domestically produced</a> anti-armor <a href="/wiki/Rocket-propelled_grenade" title="Rocket-propelled grenade">RPGs</a> like <a href="/wiki/Batar" title="Batar">al-Battar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Al-Bana" title="Al-Bana">Banna 1</a> and Banna 2 in their arsenal.<sup id="cite_ref-UNFFMGCReportp454_218-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNFFMGCReportp454-218">[218]</a></sup> Hamas and Islamic Jihad also manufactured a variety of <a href="/wiki/Improvised_explosive_device" title="Improvised explosive device">improvised explosive devices</a> (IEDs), some of which were anti-personnel bombs and others were planted on the sides of roads or underground to be activated against tanks and armored personnel carriers. According to <i><a href="/wiki/The_Jerusalem_Post" title="The Jerusalem Post">The Jerusalem Post</a></i>, some of the IEDs were manufactured from medicine bottles transferred to the Gaza Strip as humanitarian aid by Israel.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">[219]</a></sup> The same newspaper also reported that Hamas representatives said they were fighting with the aid of armored vehicles and weapons confiscated from the <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_National_Authority" title="Palestinian National Authority">Palestinian National Authority</a>, given by Israel, the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> and other countries.<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">[220]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_Weapons_Cache_in_Northern_Gaza_(1).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_Weapons_Cache_in_Northern_Gaza_%281%29.jpg/220px-Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_Weapons_Cache_in_Northern_Gaza_%281%29.jpg" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_Weapons_Cache_in_Northern_Gaza_%281%29.jpg/330px-Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_Weapons_Cache_in_Northern_Gaza_%281%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_Weapons_Cache_in_Northern_Gaza_%281%29.jpg/440px-Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_Weapons_Cache_in_Northern_Gaza_%281%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2586" data-file-height="1931" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_Weapons_Cache_in_Northern_Gaza_(1).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A weapons cache in found in northern Gaza.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At least one Palestinian witness told an Italian reporter that on many roofs of the tall buildings that were hit by Israeli bombs, including UN building, there were rocket-launchers or Hamas look-outs.<sup id="cite_ref-Maximum_600_Palestinians_died_in_Gaza_221-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Maximum_600_Palestinians_died_in_Gaza-221">[221]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Gaza_doctor_refutes_casualties_reported_in_Cast_Lead_op_222-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gaza_doctor_refutes_casualties_reported_in_Cast_Lead_op-222">[222]</a></sup> On 27 January, the Shin Bet released details given by Hamas captives, including the militants' use of mosques for weapon caches and military training. Militants admitted to the location of Hamas weapon storage sites, in tunnels, in the homes of activists, and in citrus groves and mosques, and told of theory instruction given in mosques as well.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">[223]</a></sup> Following the visit of the British Army veteran Colonel <a href="/wiki/Tim_Collins_(British_Army_officer)" title="Tim Collins (British Army officer)">Tim Collins</a> to the ruins of one of the mosques targeted by the IDF in Rafah, he said that in his view the evidencies of the secondary explosion, that could have indicated weapon's storage in the mosque, are present.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">[224]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Palestinian_rockets_in_Gaza">Palestinian rockets in Gaza</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Palestinian rockets in Gaza">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>According to <a href="/wiki/Human_Right_Watch" class="mw-redirect" title="Human Right Watch">Human Right Watch</a>, On 24 December 2008, a rocket struck a bedroom of a family living in the <a href="/wiki/Tel_al-Hawa" title="Tel al-Hawa">Tel al-Hawa</a> area in southern Gaza City, critically wounding one man. The brother of this victim told after the incident no armed group came to apologize. "I was next door in my home when this all happened. When one of those responsible tried to bargain for the shrapnel, I said that if no one took responsibility I will go to the courts, so Hamas came to me privately and admitted it." On 26 December 2008, a Palestinian rocket struck north of <a href="/wiki/Beit_Lahiya" class="mw-redirect" title="Beit Lahiya">Beit Lahiya</a>, a house was hit killing two cousins and wounding another. The grandfather described the rocket as about one meter in length; according to Human Rights Watch examination the diameter of the pipe is 120&#160;mm. The grandfather said the rocket was taken by Hamas policemen for investigation: "After he left, the war started and we never heard from him again. We got the compensation given to all victims of the war."<sup id="cite_ref-Human_Rights_Watch.2C_Rockets_from_Gaza_209-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Human_Rights_Watch.2C_Rockets_from_Gaza-209">[209]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Rocket_attacks_into_Israel">Rocket attacks into Israel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Rocket attacks into Israel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_rocket_attacks_on_Israel" title="Palestinian rocket attacks on Israel">Palestinian rocket attacks on Israel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_political_violence" title="Palestinian political violence">Palestinian political violence</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Beersheva_kindergarten_after_rocket_attack_from_Gaza.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Beersheva_kindergarten_after_rocket_attack_from_Gaza.jpg/170px-Beersheva_kindergarten_after_rocket_attack_from_Gaza.jpg" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Beersheva_kindergarten_after_rocket_attack_from_Gaza.jpg/255px-Beersheva_kindergarten_after_rocket_attack_from_Gaza.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Beersheva_kindergarten_after_rocket_attack_from_Gaza.jpg/340px-Beersheva_kindergarten_after_rocket_attack_from_Gaza.jpg 2x" data-file-width="682" data-file-height="1024" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Beersheva_kindergarten_after_rocket_attack_from_Gaza.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Kindergarten" title="Kindergarten">Kindergarten</a> classroom in <a href="/wiki/Beersheba" title="Beersheba">Beersheba</a> hit by <a href="/wiki/BM-21_Grad" title="BM-21 Grad">Grad</a> rocket from Gaza<sup id="cite_ref-dec31_ynetnews_225-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dec31_ynetnews-225">[225]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After the initial Israeli aerial assault, Hamas quickly dispersed both its personnel and weapons and equipment.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">[226]</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a> rockets from Gaza were fired from populated areas, an Islamic Jihad fighter said: "the most important thing is achieving our military goals.... We stay away from the houses if we can, but that's often impossible."<sup id="cite_ref-Human_Rights_Watch.2C_Rockets_from_Gaza_209-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Human_Rights_Watch.2C_Rockets_from_Gaza-209">[209]</a></sup> According to BBC, Palestinian groups had been firing "in response to Israeli massacres".<sup id="cite_ref-bbc1309_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc1309-51">[51]</a></sup> The strike range of Hamas rockets had increased from 16&#160;km (9.9&#160;mi) to 40&#160;km (25&#160;mi) since early 2008 with the use of improved <a href="/wiki/Qassam_rocket" title="Qassam rocket">Qassam</a> and <a href="/wiki/BM-21" class="mw-redirect" title="BM-21">factory-made</a> rockets.<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">[227]</a></sup> These attacks resulted in civilian casualties and damage to infrastructure.<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">[228]</a></sup> Rockets reached major Israeli cities <a href="/wiki/Ashdod" title="Ashdod">Ashdod</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beersheba" title="Beersheba">Beersheba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gedera" title="Gedera">Gedera</a> for the first time, putting one-eighth of Israel's population in rocket range.<sup id="cite_ref-AP_2009-01-13_229-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AP_2009-01-13-229">[229]</a></sup> On 3 January 2009 <a href="/wiki/Ma%27an_News_Agency" title="Ma'an News Agency">Ma'an News Agency</a> reported: "The Al-Qassam Brigades, military wing of Hamas, said that after a week since the start of the 'Battle of Al-Furqan [the criterion]' it has managed to fire 302 rockets, at an average of 44 rockets daily."<sup id="cite_ref-bbc1309_51-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc1309-51">[51]</a></sup> As of 13 January 2009, Palestinian militants had launched approximately 565 rockets and 200 mortars at Israel since the beginning of the conflict, according to Israeli security sources.<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">[230]</a></sup> A source close to Hamas described the movement's use of stealth when firing: "They fired rockets in between the houses and covered the alleys with sheets so they could set the rockets up in five minutes without the planes seeing them. The moment they fired, they escaped, and they are very quick."<sup id="cite_ref-parsing_231-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-parsing-231">[231]</a></sup> It is reported that 102 rockets and 35 mortars were fired by Fatah, Hamas' chief rival.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">[232]</a></sup></p>
<p>Besides the rockets fired by the <a href="/wiki/Qassam_Brigades" class="mw-redirect" title="Qassam Brigades">Qassam Brigades</a> of Hamas, other factions claimed responsibility for rockets fired into Israel and attacks on Israeli soldiers, including Al-Aqsa Martyrs' Brigades (affiliated with <a href="/wiki/Fatah" title="Fatah">Fatah</a>), the Abu Ali Mustapha Brigades, the Quds Brigades and the <a href="/wiki/Popular_Resistance_Committees" title="Popular Resistance Committees">Popular Resistance Councils</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Bauer0123_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bauer0123-1">[1]</a></sup> A Fatah official stated that the rocket attacks by his faction contradicted the official position of <a href="/wiki/Mahmoud_Abbas" title="Mahmoud Abbas">Mahmoud Abbas</a>, Fatah leader and President of the <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_National_Authority" title="Palestinian National Authority">Palestinian National Authority</a>. Abbas had called on all sides to cease hostilities unconditionally.</p>
<p>Militants fired over 750 rockets and mortars from Gaza into Israel during the conflict.<sup id="cite_ref-jpost_total_rockets_233-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jpost_total_rockets-233">[233]</a></sup> Bersheeba and Gedera were the farthest areas hit by rocket or mortars.<sup id="cite_ref-jpost_total_rockets_233-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jpost_total_rockets-233">[233]</a></sup> The rockets killed three civilians and one IDF soldier and wounded 182 people, with another 584 people suffering from shock and anxiety.<sup id="cite_ref-Israeli_MFA_234-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Israeli_MFA-234">[234]</a></sup> The rockets also caused property damage, including damage to three schools.<sup id="cite_ref-dec31_ynetnews_225-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dec31_ynetnews-225">[225]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">[235]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">[236]</a></sup> Senior Hamas official Mahmoud al-Zahar stated during the operation "they [Israeli forces] shelled everyone in Gaza.... They shelled children and hospitals and mosques, ... and in doing so, they gave us legitimacy to strike them in the same way."<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">[237]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a> noted in the open letter to <a href="/wiki/Ismail_Haniyeh" title="Ismail Haniyeh">Ismail Haniyeh</a> that despite his Foreign Ministry stance as part of response to the <a href="/wiki/Goldstone_Report" class="mw-redirect" title="Goldstone Report">Goldstone Report</a>, Palestinian armed groups remain responsible for firing rockets indiscriminately or deliberately at Israeli civilian objects. HRW also noted that Palestinian militants put Palestinian civilians at risk of Israeli counter-attacks by launching rockets from populated areas.<sup id="cite_ref-Hamas:_Investigate_Attacks_on_Israeli_Civilians_238-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hamas:_Investigate_Attacks_on_Israeli_Civilians-238">[238]</a></sup> The UN fact finding mission stated that the firing of rockets at Israel constituted a deliberate attack against the civilian population and was in violation of international law.<sup id="cite_ref-UNFFMGCReport_pdf_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNFFMGCReport_pdf-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<p>After the war, the Izz ad-Din al-Qassam Brigades revealed new rockets it used during Israel's military operation and published pictures of weapons (<a href="/wiki/Tandem-charge" title="Tandem-charge">Tandem</a> and <a href="/wiki/RPG-29" title="RPG-29">RPG-29</a> anti-armor rockets) that it could secretly smuggle to Gaza.<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">[239]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kassam_hit_sderot.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Kassam_hit_sderot.jpg/220px-Kassam_hit_sderot.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Kassam_hit_sderot.jpg/330px-Kassam_hit_sderot.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Kassam_hit_sderot.jpg/440px-Kassam_hit_sderot.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2724" data-file-height="2043" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kassam_hit_sderot.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Repairs being made to water pipe after it was hit a by a rocket.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Besides being hit with rockets fired from Gaza, Israel experienced other attacks along the borders with Lebanon and Syria.<sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">[240]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Unilateral_ceasefires">Unilateral ceasefires</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Unilateral ceasefires">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>On 17 January, Israeli officials announced a <a href="/wiki/Unilateralism" title="Unilateralism">unilateral</a> <a href="/wiki/Ceasefire" title="Ceasefire">ceasefire</a>. Israeli Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Ehud_Olmert" title="Ehud Olmert">Ehud Olmert</a> declared the ceasefire effective that night, at 00:00 GMT on 18 January.<sup id="cite_ref-ceasefire_241-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ceasefire-241">[241]</a></sup> The ceasefire consisted of two phases: "First a ceasefire is declared. If Hamas stops firing rockets then Israel pulls its forces out of the Gaza Strip. If rocket fire resumes then the IDF goes back in, this time with the international backing gained by having tried a truce." Olmert declared that the military objectives had been met.<sup id="cite_ref-haaretz18Jan_242-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-haaretz18Jan-242">[242]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">[243]</a></sup> Hamas initially "vowed to fight on",<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">[244]</a></sup> and responded that any continued Israeli presence in Gaza would be regarded as an act of war. Farzi Barhoum, a Hamas spokesman, said before the ceasefire began, "The occupier must halt his fire immediately and withdraw from our land and lift his blockade and open all crossings and we will not accept any one Zionist soldier on our land, regardless of the price that it costs."<sup id="cite_ref-ceasefire_rockets_bbc_245-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ceasefire_rockets_bbc-245">[245]</a></sup> Palestinian militants resumed rocket fire into southern Israel the following Sunday morning, four of the six fired landed in or near <a href="/wiki/Sderot" title="Sderot">Sderot</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ceasefire_rockets_ynet_246-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ceasefire_rockets_ynet-246">[246]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">[247]</a></sup> The Israeli military returned fire and launched an air strike against the rocket launching site in northern Gaza.<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">[248]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 18 January <a href="/wiki/Hamas" title="Hamas">Hamas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Jihad_Movement_in_Palestine" title="Islamic Jihad Movement in Palestine">Islamic Jihad</a> and other paramilitias said they would stop launching rockets into Israel for one week and demanded "the withdrawal of the enemy forces from the Gaza Strip within a week, along with the opening of all the crossings for the entry of humanitarian aid, food and other necessities for our people in the Gaza Strip".<sup id="cite_ref-haaretz18Jan2_249-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-haaretz18Jan2-249">[249]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">[250]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BBC-Hamas-ceasefire_251-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-Hamas-ceasefire-251">[251]</a></sup> Three days later, the last Israeli troops left Gaza.<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">[252]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since the unilateral ceasefires were declared on 17 January, militants have fired rockets and mortar shells from Gaza,<sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">[253]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">[254]</a></sup> and the IDF has launched airstrikes against Gaza.<sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">[255]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Continued_negotiations">Continued negotiations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Continued negotiations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Egyptian mediators held discussions with Israel and Hamas about extending the cease-fire by a year or more. Hamas and Fatah met to allow both to play a role in rebuilding.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT0128_256-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT0128-256">[256]</a></sup> Israel began pressuring Egypt to do more to stop weapons smuggling into Gaza, the halting of which is one of Israel's central demands in extending a cease-fire. On 27 January 2009, <a href="/wiki/Foreign_Minister_of_Egypt" class="mw-redirect" title="Foreign Minister of Egypt">Foreign Minister of Egypt</a> <a href="/wiki/Ahmed_Aboul_Gheit" title="Ahmed Aboul Gheit">Ahmed Aboul Gheit</a> discouraged Britain, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> and <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> from sending warships to patrol the waters off Gaza, which the three European nations felt could help halt seaborne smuggling. Gheit said such efforts would harm Europe's relations with the Arab world. Egypt also opposed proposals for European troops to be stationed on the border between Gaza and Egypt to monitor smuggling tunnels.<sup id="cite_ref-WP0128_257-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WP0128-257">[257]</a></sup></p>
<p>Israel, along with many Western and some Arab countries, wanted international aid groups to control aid from donations around the world, so that Hamas would not receive credit for the rebuilding. To speed up reconstruction, Hamas agreed that it would not insist on collecting reconstruction money itself and would allow donated money to flow through different avenues based on the various alliances, although Hamas ultimately expected to administer the aid. But advisors to senior Hamas political leader <a href="/wiki/Ismail_Haniyeh" title="Ismail Haniyeh">Ismail Haniyeh</a> said Israel's willingness to open the border for humanitarian aid only was unacceptable, as Hamas would need much more to rebuild its economy and provide relief for citizens. Haniyeh aides said the cease-fire is contingent on a full border opening.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT0128_256-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT0128-256">[256]</a></sup></p>
<p>Shortly after becoming <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">President of the United States</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> directed newly appointed special envoy to the Middle East <a href="/wiki/George_J._Mitchell" title="George J. Mitchell">George J. Mitchell</a> to visit Israel, the <a href="/wiki/West_Bank" title="West Bank">West Bank</a>, Egypt, Jordan, <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a> for peace talks. Mitchell began his meetings in Cairo on 27 January 2009, and Obama said his visit was part of the President's campaign promise to listen to both sides of the Israeli–Palestinian conflict and work toward a Middle East peace deal. Mitchell did not plan to talk to Hamas, but instead focus on talks with the more moderate <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_National_Authority" title="Palestinian National Authority">Palestinian Authority</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-WP0128_257-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WP0128-257">[257]</a></sup> A spokesman for Haniyeh said he respected Mitchell, but was disappointed with the envoy's decision not to hold discussions with Hamas.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT0128_256-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT0128-256">[256]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Ehud_Olmert" title="Ehud Olmert">Ehud Olmert</a> stated that Israel would not agree to a long term truce or lift the blockade on Gaza without the freeing of <a href="/wiki/Gilad_Shalit" title="Gilad Shalit">Gilad Shalit</a>, an IDF soldier held captive in Gaza since June 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_shalit_ceasefire_258-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc_shalit_ceasefire-258">[258]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">[259]</a></sup> Hamas demanded that Israel release 1,400 <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_prisoners" class="mw-redirect" title="Palestinian prisoners">Palestinian prisoners</a> in exchange for Shalit and such negotiations be kept separate from ceasefire negotiations.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_truce_captives_260-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc_truce_captives-260">[260]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-war_military_assessment">Post-war military assessment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Post-war military assessment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The war was an Israeli <a href="/wiki/Tactical_victory" title="Tactical victory">tactical victory</a> and a significant tactical defeat for Hamas.<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes.com_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes.com-4">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261">[261]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-haaretz.com_262-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-haaretz.com-262">[262]</a></sup> Al-Qassam Brigades reported in "The outcome of al-Qassam operations during the Battle of <i>al-Furqan</i>" they killed 102 Israeli soldiers. On 19 January 2009, a spokesperson for the group said on <a href="/wiki/Al-Arabiya" class="mw-redirect" title="Al-Arabiya">al-Arabiya</a> "Israel lost 'at least 80 soldiers' in the fighting" and said about Hamas losses "only 48 fighters slain in Israel war". According to United Nations report of the Independent International Fact-Finding Mission of Human Rights Council, which was on General Assembly's agenda on 29 October 2009: "The large discrepancy in the data confirms the Mission's observations below in the report about the reliability of the information about the Gaza military operations posted on websites of al-Qassam and other Palestinian armed groups."<sup id="cite_ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263">[263]</a></sup> In November 2010, the Hamas Interior Minister acknowledged that around 700 militants part of Hamas and affiliated factions were killed in the war.<sup id="cite_ref-AFP_300_fighters_killed_264-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AFP_300_fighters_killed-264">[264]</a></sup></p>
<p>Several senior Hamas military commanders and politburo members were killed, as well as approximately 50 explosives experts.<sup id="cite_ref-jpost.com_3-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jpost.com-3">[3]</a></sup> Hamas experienced "widespread desertion" in the face of the Israeli advance.<sup id="cite_ref-jpost.com_3-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jpost.com-3">[3]</a></sup> Hamas also lost a very large amount of weaponry and equipment; key storage facilities were discovered under mosques and public buildings.<sup id="cite_ref-jpost.com_3-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jpost.com-3">[3]</a></sup> A former <a href="/wiki/Shin_Bet" title="Shin Bet">Shin Bet</a> deputy director who co-authored a report on the war noted, "Hamas had planned to stand and fight, but the Iz al-Qassam Brigades proved unequal to the task ... and consequently they failed to match the public image Hamas has tried so hard to present of stalwart, proficient Islamic warriors."<sup id="cite_ref-haaretz.com_262-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-haaretz.com-262">[262]</a></sup></p>
<p>In addition, the Israeli operation greatly curtailed years of Hamas rocket fire, returning a sense of normalcy to Southern Israel.<sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265">[265]</a></sup> In the year before the war, Hamas had fired over 3,300 rockets at Israel's Gaza periphery towns. That number dropped to less than 300 in the ten months following the conflict.<sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266">[266]</a></sup></p>
<p>Defense analyst David Eshel stated, "The success of Operation Cast Lead in the densely populated Gaza Strip shows that an industrial military that coordinates operations among land, air and sea units, makes effective use of advanced technology, and shares intelligence and leads from the front can decisively defeat an asymmetrical enemy." He further noted, "Israel used a variety of tactics to outflank and defeat Hamas in its own territory. These included long-term planning, meticulous intelligence-gathering, deception and disinformation."<sup id="cite_ref-Aviation_Week_2009-05-11_2-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Aviation_Week_2009-05-11-2">[2]</a></sup> As a result of its poor performance, Hamas relieved at least two brigade commanders on Iranian advice, and reportedly stripped 100 fighters of their membership. The organization decided to initiate a thorough investigation of the conduct of its fighters during the operation.<sup id="cite_ref-jpost.com_3-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jpost.com-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">[267]</a></sup> Hamas' leadership modified its tactical doctrine. The Qassam Brigades intensified military training at its various training camps and military academy in the <a href="/wiki/Nuseirat_refugee_camp" class="mw-redirect" title="Nuseirat refugee camp">Nuseirat refugee camp</a>. The new training was thought to be more offensive, with a focus on hitting the rear of an IDF force. <a href="/wiki/Hezbollah" title="Hezbollah">Hezbollah</a> operatives were suspected of involvement in the program. In contrast to the pre-war period, when Hamas openly displayed its capabilities, the nature of the program was kept classified.<sup id="cite_ref-jpost.com_3-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jpost.com-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Israeli army said it destroyed about 80% of the tunnels between Gaza and Egypt that were being used to bring in weapons and rocket components. Residents in Rafah said they cleared away debris and discovered that many of the tunnels were intact, though they acknowledged the destruction of many.<sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268">[268]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Casualties">Casualties</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Casualties">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Casualties_of_the_Gaza_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Casualties of the Gaza War">Casualties of the Gaza War</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">

Video of Israelis running to bomb shelters during a rocket attack in 2009.</div>
