</div>
<p>Human Rights organisations and the UN counted just above 1,400 Palestinian deaths,<sup id="cite_ref-PCHRCASFIG_30-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PCHRCASFIG-30">[30]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BTselem_fatalities_OCL_31-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BTselem_fatalities_OCL-31">[31]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Goldstone_casualties_269-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Goldstone_casualties-269">[269]</a></sup> Israel acknowledged 1,166 deaths.<sup id="cite_ref-idf_updated_death_toll_32-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-idf_updated_death_toll-32">[32]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Reuters_Israels_Gaza_toll_270-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters_Israels_Gaza_toll-270">[270]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to PCHR, among the Palestinian deaths were 926 unarmed civilians, 255 police officers, and 236 fighters.<sup id="cite_ref-PCHRCASFIG_30-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PCHRCASFIG-30">[30]</a></sup> B’Tselem counted 248 killed police officers.<sup id="cite_ref-BTselem_fatalities_OCL_31-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BTselem_fatalities_OCL-31">[31]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Al_Mezan_Center_for_Human_Rights" title="Al Mezan Center for Human Rights">Al Mezan Centre for Human Rights</a> said in January 2009, that 1,268 people were killed, among them 288 children and 103 women, and 85% of those killed were not combatants. The IDF tallied 295 killed civilians, least 709 armed militants and 162 undetermined.<sup id="cite_ref-idf_updated_death_toll_32-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-idf_updated_death_toll-32">[32]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Reuters_Israels_Gaza_toll_270-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters_Israels_Gaza_toll-270">[270]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Hamas Interior Minister <a href="/wiki/Fathi_Hamad" title="Fathi Hamad">Fathi Hamad</a> stated that between 200 and 300 Hamas fighters, another 150 security forces and 250 policemen were killed.<sup id="cite_ref-AFP_300_fighters_killed_264-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AFP_300_fighters_killed-264">[264]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ma.27an_200-300_killed_271-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ma.27an_200-300_killed-271">[271]</a></sup></p>
<p>3 Israeli civilians were killed and 6 soldiers.<sup id="cite_ref-BTselem_fatalities_OCL_31-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BTselem_fatalities_OCL-31">[31]</a></sup> Additionally, 4 soldiers were killed by "<a href="/wiki/Friendly_fire" title="Friendly fire">Friendly fire</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-latimes2009jan13_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-latimes2009jan13-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Civilians_versus_combatants">Civilians versus combatants</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Civilians versus combatants">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="rquote floatright" role="presentation" style="border-collapse:collapse; border-style:none; float:right; margin:0.5em 0.75em; width:33%;">
<tr style="text-align:left; vertical-align:top;">
<td style="color:#b2b7f2; font-size:3.3em; font-family:'Times New Roman',serif; font-weight:bold; padding:4px 2px 2px; width:0.5em; line-height: 1em;">“</td>
<td style="padding:0 10px;">During the 2008-2009 Gaza fighting I personally erased a key detail—that Hamas fighters were dressed as civilians and being counted as civilians in the death toll—because of a threat to our reporter in Gaza. (The policy was then, and remains, not to inform readers that the story is censored unless the <a href="/wiki/Censorship" title="Censorship">censorship</a> is Israeli. Earlier this month, the AP's Jerusalem news editor reported and submitted a story on Hamas intimidation; the story was shunted into deep freeze by his superiors and has not been published.)</td>
<td style="color:#b2b7f2; font-size:3.3em; font-family:'Times New Roman',serif; font-weight:bold; padding:4px 2px 2px; text-align:right; vertical-align:bottom; width:0.5em; line-height: 1em;">”</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td class="rquotecite" colspan="3" style="padding-top:10px; font-size:smaller; line-height:1em; text-align:right;"><cite>—&#160;<a href="/wiki/Matti_Friedman" title="Matti Friedman">Matti Friedman</a><sup id="cite_ref-MFriedman_272-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MFriedman-272">[272]</a></sup></cite></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>In any conflict, the ratio of combatant and civilian deaths is a highly sensitive topic. During the fighting in the Gaza War, the main source for the number of Palestinian casualties was Hamas' Ministry of Health in Gaza. The <a href="/wiki/ICRC" class="mw-redirect" title="ICRC">ICRC</a> used these figures, but at a later stage it made its own assessment.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_bell_273-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_bell-273">[273]</a></sup> Because Israel allowed very few international workers and journalists in Gaza during much of the conflict, it has been difficult to verify the figures independently.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_bell_273-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_bell-273">[273]</a></sup></p>
<p>In <i><a href="/wiki/The_Jerusalem_Post" title="The Jerusalem Post">The Jerusalem Post</a></i>, Israeli-Arab journalist <a href="/wiki/Khaled_Abu_Toameh" title="Khaled Abu Toameh">Khaled Abu Toameh</a> suggested that killed fighters in civilian clothes led to the over-counting of civilian casualties and under-counting Hamas military casualties, as Palestinian casualties arrived at hospitals without weapons or any other signs revealing they were fighters.<sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274">[274]</a></sup></p>
<p>B'Tselem wrote that its fatalities classification was based on the guidelines of the International Committee of the Red Cross (ICRC) published in June 2009. The PCHR civilian count includes Hamas members killed in what the PCHR assessed were non-combat situations. The Al Mezan centre defined combatants as "those taking up arms against Israeli troops." <sup id="cite_ref-BBC_bell_273-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_bell-273">[273]</a></sup> The Israeli <a href="/wiki/International_Institute_for_Counter-Terrorism" title="International Institute for Counter-Terrorism">International Institute for Counter-Terrorism</a><sup id="cite_ref-275" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-275">[275]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Scholars_for_Peace_in_the_Middle_East" title="Scholars for Peace in the Middle East">SPME</a><sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276">[276]</a></sup> have contested the classifications of B'Tselem and PCHR.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Gazan_police">Gazan police</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Gazan police">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>During the conflict Israel targeted numerous police facilities in Gaza. Many of these attacks occurred during the first minutes of the operations resulting in the deaths of 99 policemen and nine other members of the public.<sup id="cite_ref-UNFFMGCReport_pdf_50-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNFFMGCReport_pdf-50">[50]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-btselemcasualties_277-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-btselemcasualties-277">[277]</a></sup> The attacks on Police during the first day of the operation included the bombing of a police cadet graduation ceremony, killing scores of police cadets along with family members who had come to attend the celebration. Police cadets killed in the incident included traffic police and musicians in the police orchestra.<sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278">[278]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279">[279]</a></sup> The UN fact finding mission established that approximately 240 Gaza policemen were killed by Israeli forces during the course of the conflict constituting over one sixth of the total Palestinian casualties.<sup id="cite_ref-UNFFMGCReport_pdf_50-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNFFMGCReport_pdf-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Legality">Legality</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Legality">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>The UN Fact Finding Mission analysed the police institutions in Gaza from the time Hamas gained control. They concluded that the Gaza police were a civilian law-enforcement agency and that Israel's blanket targeting of the Gaza police was therefore a violation of international humanitarian law.<sup id="cite_ref-UNFFMGCReport_pdf_50-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNFFMGCReport_pdf-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a> stated that police are presumptively civilians but on a specific case by case basis can be considered valid targets if formally incorporated into the armed forces of a party to a conflict or directly participate in the hostilities. They stressed that blanket decisions must not be made about police being legitimate targets and that a decision that police and police stations are legitimate military targets depends on whether those police play a role in fighting against Israel, or whether a particular police station is used to store weapons or for some other military purpose.<sup id="cite_ref-hrw_civilians_release_280-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrw_civilians_release-280">[280]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/B%27Tselem" title="B'Tselem">B'Tselem</a> also states that police officers are presumed to be civilians and likely not legitimate objects of attack under international humanitarian law.<sup id="cite_ref-BTselem_explanation_132-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BTselem_explanation-132">[132]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Israeli_views">Israeli views</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Israeli views">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>The Israeli Orient Research Group reported that 78 of the 89 killed during this first IAF strike were terror operatives, many of them belonging to the militant group, al-Qassam Brigades.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The Jerusalem Centre for Public Affairs further reported that 286 of the 343 police officers killed during the offensive were members of terror organizations and that another 27 fighters belonged to units undergoing infantry training.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> It noted that the security apparatuses participated in terror activity and that the Hamas leadership presented these organizations as at the forefront of the jihad for liberating all of Palestine.<sup id="cite_ref-281" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-281">[281]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-282" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-282">[282]</a></sup></p>
<p>The IDF made clear that it regards police under the control of Hamas i Jerusalem Pos |archiv Gaza to be equivalent to the enemies armed fighters, including them in the militant's count.<sup id="cite_ref-UNFFMGCReport_pdf_50-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNFFMGCReport_pdf-50">[50]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Reuters_Israels_Gaza_toll_270-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters_Israels_Gaza_toll-270">[270]</a></sup> A government paper published pictures of four men that were killed during the military operations that they claim were downloaded from Palestinian websites. The men are identified in the different pictures as both policemen and members of al-Qassam Brigades.<sup id="cite_ref-Consent_and_advise_283-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Consent_and_advise-283">[283]</a></sup> Israeli <a href="/wiki/Intelligence_and_Terrorism_Information_Center" title="Intelligence and Terrorism Information Center">Intelligence and Terrorism Information Center</a> (ITIC) alleged that the distinction between the internal security forces and Hamas military wing is not sharply defined and cites Gaza police officials who said that police were instructed to fight the enemy in case of an invasion into the Gaza Strip.<sup id="cite_ref-Mounting_evidence_indicates_284-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mounting_evidence_indicates-284">[284]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-285" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-285">[285]</a></sup> Many security force members were reported to "moonlight" with the militant group, Izzidin al-Qassam Brigades.<sup id="cite_ref-286" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-286">[286]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Gazan_rockets">Gazan rockets</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Gazan rockets">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>During the conflict, Palestinian groups fired rockets targeting Israeli civilians in the cities of Ashdod, Beersheba and Gedera placing 1/8 of the Israeli population at risk. The military wing of Hamas said that after a week from the start, it had managed to fire 302 rockets, at an average of 44 rockets daily. 102 rockets and 35 mortars were fired by Fatah at Israel. Over 750 rockets and mortars were fired from Gaza into Israel during the conflict wounded 182 civilians, killing 3 people, and causing minor suffering to another 584 people suffering from shock and anxiety. Several rockets landed in schools and one fell close to a kindergarten, all located in residential areas. The UN fact finding mission stated that this constituted a deliberate attack against the civilian population and was unjustifiable in international law.<sup id="cite_ref-dec31_ynetnews_225-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dec31_ynetnews-225">[225]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-jpost_total_rockets_233-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jpost_total_rockets-233">[233]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Israeli_MFA_234-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Israeli_MFA-234">[234]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Aftermath">Aftermath</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Aftermath">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Israel was victorious militarily, but its reputation was harmed.<sup id="cite_ref-Victorious.2C_but_vilified:_Israel_has_.27destroyed_its_image_and_its_soul.27_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Victorious.2C_but_vilified:_Israel_has_.27destroyed_its_image_and_its_soul.27-5">[5]</a></sup> The international community continued to isolate Hamas (except for <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a> and <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a>), because it rejected the <a href="/wiki/Quartet_on_the_Middle_East" title="Quartet on the Middle East">Quartet</a> demands to recognize Israel, accept the <a href="/wiki/Oslo_accords" class="mw-redirect" title="Oslo accords">Oslo accords</a> peace initiative and abandon violence in exchange for international recognition as representatives of the Palestinian people.<sup id="cite_ref-Hamas_rejects_U.S._demand_to_recognize_Israel_287-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hamas_rejects_U.S._demand_to_recognize_Israel-287">[287]</a></sup> In the months following the war, Hamas suspended its use of rockets and shifted focus to winning support at home and abroad through cultural initiatives and public relations, with the aim to build a "cultural resistance". Hamas officials stated that "The current situation required a stoppage of rockets. After the war, the fighters needed a break and the people needed a break."<sup id="cite_ref-Hamas_Shifts_From_Rockets_to_Culture_War_288-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hamas_Shifts_From_Rockets_to_Culture_War-288">[288]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Propaganda_and_psychological_warfare">Propaganda and psychological warfare</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Propaganda and psychological warfare">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hamas">Hamas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Hamas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Before and during the conflict, Hamas' senior representatives released a number of statements designed to avert Israeli decision-makers from launching any military operation in Gaza and to cause demoralization among Israelis. Before the end of the pre-conflict ceasefire, Hamas boasted that it had countless surprises awaiting Israeli troops, should they advance.<sup id="cite_ref-Psychological_Tricks_to_Demoralize_the_Enemy_289-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Psychological_Tricks_to_Demoralize_the_Enemy-289">[289]</a></sup> Hamas representatives threatened on several occasions to abduct Israeli soldiers, and during the ground invasion tried to spread rumors that it actually had captured or killed more Israeli soldiers.<sup id="cite_ref-Israel.27s_Gaza_war_adds_psychological_operations_290-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Israel.27s_Gaza_war_adds_psychological_operations-290">[290]</a></sup></p>
<p>On a video broadcast on Al-Aqsa TV on 10 January showing the names of Israeli towns hit by rockets, it was implied Tel-Aviv is the next target and that 'all options are open'.<sup id="cite_ref-Operation_Cast_Lead_Update_No_12_291-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Operation_Cast_Lead_Update_No_12-291">[291]</a></sup> Also, Hamas sent messages in Hebrew to Israeli citizens' mobile phones warning: "Rockets on all cities, shelters will not protect you."<sup id="cite_ref-Hamas_leader_killed_in_airstrike_as_Israelis_reject_ceasefire_call_292-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hamas_leader_killed_in_airstrike_as_Israelis_reject_ceasefire_call-292">[292]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-guardian-psychwar_293-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-psychwar-293">[293]</a></sup></p>
<p>Hamas instrumentalized the Israeli soldier <a href="/wiki/Gilad_Shalit" title="Gilad Shalit">Gilad Shalit</a> as a form of psychological weapon, declaring that he had been wounded by Israeli fire, later announcing that his condition was no longer of interest to them.<sup id="cite_ref-Psychological_Tricks_to_Demoralize_the_Enemy_289-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Psychological_Tricks_to_Demoralize_the_Enemy-289">[289]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to IDF spokesman, Hamas' ruses in the battlefield included booby traps throughout Gaza's neighborhoods, such as mannequins placed at apartment entrances and rigged to explode when the soldiers approach.<sup id="cite_ref-Israel.27s_Gaza_war_adds_psychological_operations_290-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Israel.27s_Gaza_war_adds_psychological_operations-290">[290]</a></sup></p>
<p>Arab television stations reported Hamas-provided statistics for Israeli casualties on the assumption that Israel is distorting its own figures of soldiers killed and wounded.<sup id="cite_ref-The_unreported_battle_with_Hamas:_psychological_warfare_294-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_unreported_battle_with_Hamas:_psychological_warfare-294">[294]</a></sup></p>
<p>A study by the <a href="/wiki/Center_for_Strategic_and_International_Studies" title="Center for Strategic and International Studies">Center for Strategic and International Studies</a> notes that Hamas propaganda both rejected Hamas responsibility for the fighting and used it to attack the Palestinian Authority.<sup id="cite_ref-AnthonyHCordesman_76-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AnthonyHCordesman-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<p>Dr. Tal Pavel from Israeli think-tank <a href="/wiki/International_Policy_Institute_for_Counter-Terrorism" class="mw-redirect" title="International Policy Institute for Counter-Terrorism">International Policy Institute for Counter-Terrorism</a> (ICT) said that Hamas uses its Web sites to make comparisons between Israel and Nazi Germany, portraying Israel as a destructive, oppressive regime afraid of Hamas rockets raining on Tel Aviv.<sup id="cite_ref-The_unreported_battle_with_Hamas:_psychological_warfare_294-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_unreported_battle_with_Hamas:_psychological_warfare-294">[294]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Israel">Israel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Israel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The day before the beginning of the offensive on 27 December the <a href="/wiki/Israel_Defense_Forces" title="Israel Defense Forces">IDF</a> pulled troops back from the border and used its radio channels to broadcast talk of a "lull" to achieve a disinformation coup to lure Hamas fighters out of hiding.<sup id="cite_ref-ap-msnbc-psych-war_295-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ap-msnbc-psych-war-295">[295]</a></sup></p>
<p>A broadcaster in Islamic Jihad's Voice of Jerusalem radio station in Gaza City reported that IDF have been breaking into his station signal "least once an hour" during conflict intensification to broadcast messages to Gaza's population that their problems were due to Hamas. The Israelis also dropped leaflets with similar messages and contact info to report about the whereabouts of militant leaders and weapons caches.<sup id="cite_ref-ap-msnbc-psych-war_295-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ap-msnbc-psych-war-295">[295]</a></sup> The leaflets also noted, "The Israeli army will respond if the rocket fire continues."<sup id="cite_ref-guardian-psychwar_293-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-psychwar-293">[293]</a></sup> In war zones, leaflets warned local residents that they had to flee. It also warned residents that their homes would be targeted if they were located in an area of possible target.<sup id="cite_ref-Jazeera_2009-01-03_296-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jazeera_2009-01-03-296">[296]</a></sup> Dr. Yaniv Levitan of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Haifa" title="University of Haifa">University of Haifa</a> said that the aim of the flyers was not to demoralize the civil population, but to implant recognition in hearts and minds that Hamas has failed, that there is an option of choosing another path.<sup id="cite_ref-The_unreported_battle_with_Hamas:_psychological_warfare_294-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_unreported_battle_with_Hamas:_psychological_warfare-294">[294]</a></sup></p>
<p>IDF spokespersons often reported that scores of demoralized Hamas fighters had been observed deserting. According to Ephraim Kam, deputy head of the Institute of National Security Studies at Tel Aviv University, the claim could not be confirmed but it strengthened the Israeli population's will to continue and undermined the confidence of Hamas in Gaza.<sup id="cite_ref-Psychological_Tricks_to_Demoralize_the_Enemy_289-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Psychological_Tricks_to_Demoralize_the_Enemy-289">[289]</a></sup></p>
<p>There was a mistrust of phone calls warning messages to people that they have "just minutes to evacuate before they bomb the house". According to a human rights lawyer at the <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_Center_for_Human_Rights" class="mw-redirect" title="Palestinian Center for Human Rights">Palestinian Center for Human Rights</a> (PCHR), despite the hundreds of phone calls to families warning their house is about to be blown up, only 37 were destroyed, presumably as of the 3 January date.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian-psychwar_293-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-psychwar-293">[293]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversies_regarding_tactics">Controversies regarding tactics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Controversies regarding tactics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-move" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Mergefrom.svg/50px-Mergefrom.svg.png" width="50" height="20" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Mergefrom.svg/75px-Mergefrom.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Mergefrom.svg/100px-Mergefrom.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="50" data-file-height="20" /></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">It has been suggested that <i><a href="/wiki/International_Law_and_the_Gaza_War" class="mw-redirect" title="International Law and the Gaza War">International Law and the Gaza War</a></i> be <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Merging" title="Wikipedia:Merging">merged</a> into this article. (<a href="/wiki/Talk:Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)" title="Talk:Gaza War (2008–09)">Discuss</a>) <small><i>Proposed since August 2014.</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/International_Law_and_the_Gaza_War" class="mw-redirect" title="International Law and the Gaza War">International Law and the Gaza War</a></div>
<p>Both Israel and Hamas were accused of using controversial military tactics during the 2008–2009 Gaza War.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversial_tactics_allegedly_used_by_Hamas">Controversial tactics allegedly used by Hamas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Controversial tactics allegedly used by Hamas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Civilians_as_human_shields">Civilians as human shields</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Civilians as human shields">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Israel maintains that Hamas uses civilians, and especially children, as <a href="/wiki/Human_shield" title="Human shield">human shields</a>, as a part of its war doctrine. They said that Hamas repeatedly called upon Palestinian civilians to gather near buildings where they feared that the IDF was about to launch air-strikes against Hamas targets. They documented several examples of what they described as "calls in the Hamas controlled Gaza media for Palestinians civilians to serve as human shields". They released footage allegedly showing Hamas' Al-Aqsa TV calling upon children to form a human shield at various structures in Gaza to prevent anticipated IDF airstrikes, and an Al-Aqsa TV News broadcast describing how a crowd of civilians gathered on the roof of Abu Bilal al-Ja'abeer to stop the IDF from executing an airstrike.<sup id="cite_ref-MFA_297-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MFA-297">[297]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-298" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-298">[298]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Israel_Defense_Forces" title="Israel Defense Forces">IDF</a> released a video taken by an <a href="/wiki/UAV" class="mw-redirect" title="UAV">UAV</a> drone during the war, saying that it showed a Hamas militant launching a rocket from a roof of a residential house and then leaving surrounded by children to avoid being targeted by the IDF.<sup id="cite_ref-299" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-299">[299]</a></sup> Later, the IDF and <a href="/wiki/Israeli_Ministry_of_Foreign_Affairs" class="mw-redirect" title="Israeli Ministry of Foreign Affairs">Israeli Ministry of Foreign Affairs</a> compiled a film accusing Hamas of a systematic use of civilian infrastructure and civilians as a <a href="/wiki/Human_shield" title="Human shield">human shield</a>. The film includes photos and videos documenting Hamas' uses of a human shield, as well as incitement of children and using them for paramilitary activity and even as <a href="/wiki/Suicide_bomber" class="mw-redirect" title="Suicide bomber">suicide bombers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-300" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-300">[300]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-301" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-301">[301]</a></sup> Israeli Air Force videos allegedly show terrorists using groups of children as cover to escape from combat areas and joining groups of children.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceC_302-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceC-302">[302]</a></sup></p>
<p>The former commander of the British forces in Afghanistan, Col. <a href="/wiki/Richard_Kemp" title="Richard Kemp">Richard Kemp</a>, testified at UN Human Rights Council 12th Special Session that Israel encountered an "enemy that deliberately positioned its military capability behind the human shield of the civilian population".<sup id="cite_ref-303" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-303">[303]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-304" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-304">[304]</a></sup></p>
<p>The commander of the military-terrorist wing of the PFLP-GC in the Gaza Strip stated in an interview that some areas did not present a problem because of the "population and building density" that would "provide the resistance with a shield".<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceC_302-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceC-302">[302]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_Hamas_Operation_Center.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_Hamas_Operation_Center.jpg/220px-Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_Hamas_Operation_Center.jpg" width="220" height="194" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_Hamas_Operation_Center.jpg/330px-Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_Hamas_Operation_Center.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_Hamas_Operation_Center.jpg/440px-Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_Hamas_Operation_Center.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1453" data-file-height="1279" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces_-_Hamas_Operation_Center.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Hamas operation centre in the middle of a civilian area.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Professor Newton, expert in laws of armed conflict testifying in front of United Nations Fact Finding Mission criticised a statement by a Hamas brigade commander who said, "The entire people of Gaza are the combatants and therefore, it is appropriate for us to issue warnings and then whether – if, even if they disregard them, to occupy their basement or their house or their backyard." Professor Newton stated that the legal obligation was to never commingle civilian and military objectives.<sup id="cite_ref-Public_hearings_.E2.80.93_Geneva.2C_Afternoon_Session_of_7_July_2009_305-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Public_hearings_.E2.80.93_Geneva.2C_Afternoon_Session_of_7_July_2009-305">[305]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Intelmaps1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/6f/Intelmaps1.jpg/220px-Intelmaps1.jpg" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/6f/Intelmaps1.jpg/330px-Intelmaps1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/6f/Intelmaps1.jpg/440px-Intelmaps1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2228" data-file-height="1552" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Intelmaps1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Hamas Deployment in Northern Sector of Gaza City</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Intelmaps2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a7/Intelmaps2.jpg/220px-Intelmaps2.jpg" width="220" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a7/Intelmaps2.jpg/330px-Intelmaps2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a7/Intelmaps2.jpg/440px-Intelmaps2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2250" data-file-height="1584" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Intelmaps2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Hamas Deployment in the "Tel-Zaatar" Region</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> quotes a study published by the Israel-based <a href="/wiki/Intelligence_and_Terrorism_Information_Center" title="Intelligence and Terrorism Information Center">Intelligence and Terrorism Information Center</a>, charging Hamas with methodically building its military infrastructure in the heart of population centers. According to the study, Hamas not only hides among the population, but has made a main component of its combat strategy "channeling" the army into the densely populated areas to fight.<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes_study_306-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes_study-306">[306]</a></sup> During the Gaza War, Hamas invested great effort in preventing civilians from leaving neighborhoods that were in the line of fire and letting them flee to the south of the Strip.<sup id="cite_ref-Cracks_in_Hamas_307-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cracks_in_Hamas-307">[307]</a></sup></p>
<p>After Israeli forces fired shells near a UN school in Gaza killing around 30 people, Israel's military said the shelling was in response to mortar fire from within the school and asserted that Hamas were using civilians as cover. They stated that the dead near the school included Hamas members of a rocket launching cell. Two residents of the area confirmed that a group of militants were firing mortar shells from near the school and identified two of the victims as Hamas militants.<sup id="cite_ref-308" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-308">[308]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Goldstone report found indications that Palestinian armed groups launched rockets from urban areas. The Mission was not been able to obtain any direct evidence of specific intent of shielding the rocket launchers from counterstrokes by the Israeli armed forces.<sup id="cite_ref-UNreportp146_309-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNreportp146-309">[309]</a></sup> From a legal perspective, the report said that the launching of attacks close to civilian buildings would have unnecessarily exposed the civilian population of Gaza and violated the customary rules of international humanitarian law and the right to life of the endangered civilians.<sup id="cite_ref-UNFFMGCReport_pdf_50-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNFFMGCReport_pdf-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Goldstone report concluded that there was evidence of the presence of Palestinian armed groups in residential areas. The report noted that because of the densely populated nature of the northern half of the Gaza strip, once the Israeli forces gained control of the outlying areas in the first few days of the ground invasion, most, if not all, locations still accessible to the Palestinian militants would have been in urban areas. It would be difficult to avoid mixing with the civilian population in the small and overcrowded Gaza Strip. The report concluded that the Israeli Government had not produced any evidence to support its allegation that Palestinian combatants "mingle routinely with civilians in order to cover their movements".<sup id="cite_ref-UNreportp146_309-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNreportp146-309">[309]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to the book <i>The Goldstone Report 'Reconsidered<span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span></i>, a compilation of essays authored by legal scholars and published by the pro-Israel group <a href="/wiki/NGO_Monitor" title="NGO Monitor">NGO Monitor</a>, the conclusions were false and largely based on unverified claims made by NGOs.<sup id="cite_ref-310" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-310">[310]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-311" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-311">[311]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Combatant_use_of_civilian_clothes">Combatant use of civilian clothes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Combatant use of civilian clothes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>A <i>New York Times</i> journalist asserted that Hamas militants were fighting in civilian clothes.<sup id="cite_ref-nytimestraps_146-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimestraps-146">[146]</a></sup> Some NGO reports suggested that in general members of Palestinian armed groups did not wear military uniforms and mixed with the civilian population.<sup id="cite_ref-UNreportp146_309-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNreportp146-309">[309]</a></sup></p>
<p>The UN Fact Finding Mission (Goldstone Mission), however, concluded in its report: ″While reports reviewed by the Mission credibly indicate that members of Palestinian armed groups were not always dressed in a way that distinguished them from civilians, the Mission found no evidence that Palestinian combatants mingled with the civilian population with the intention of shielding themselves from attack.″e<sup id="cite_ref-UNreportp146_309-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNreportp146-309">[309]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Military_use_of_medical_facilities_and_uniforms">Military use of medical facilities and uniforms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Military use of medical facilities and uniforms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>An IDF investigation concluded that Hamas forced the <a href="/wiki/International_Red_Cross_and_Red_Crescent_Movement" title="International Red Cross and Red Crescent Movement">Red Crescent</a> to hand over medic and nurse uniforms for its operatives and commandeered ambulances for fighters transportation during the War. Palestinian civilians living in Gaza detailed Hamas' attempts to hijack ambulances and the wearing of paramedic uniforms by Hamas fighters. An ambulance driver registered with and trained by the Palestinian Red Crescent Society spoke of Hamas' efforts to "lure the ambulances into the heart of a battle to transport fighters to safety" and the hijacking of the al-Quds Hospital's fleet of ambulances.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_312-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-312">[312]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-JpostHaniyehHid_313-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JpostHaniyehHid-313">[313]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Hamas_tried_to_hijack_ambulances_during_Gaza_war_314-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hamas_tried_to_hijack_ambulances_during_Gaza_war-314">[314]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Weighing_Crimes_and_Ethics_in_the_Fog_of_Urban_Warfare_315-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Weighing_Crimes_and_Ethics_in_the_Fog_of_Urban_Warfare-315">[315]</a></sup></p>
<p>The IDF claimed that Hamas operated a command and control center inside <a href="/wiki/Al-Shifa_Hospital" title="Al-Shifa Hospital">Shifa Hospital</a> in Gaza City throughout the War, and that Hamas field commanders exploited the daily cessation in fighting that the IDF established for humanitarian purposes to receive instructions from senior Hamas officials. Addressing the Israeli cabinet, an intelligence official claimed that senior members of Hamas sought refuge in the sub-level floors believing that Israel would not target them for fear that such a strike would invariably lead to heavy collateral damage to the hospital patients in the upper floors.<sup id="cite_ref-shifa_144-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shifa-144">[144]</a></sup> Next to the hospital, Militants set up posts that were used for the firing of mortars. Underneath a mosque that was located alongside the hospital was discovered a tunnel leading to the maternity ward, which was used by Hamas operatives to move undetected. After an Israeli airstrike on the central prison, which resulted in prisoners being released into the streets, several of the 115 prisoners accused of collaboration with Israel who had not yet been tried were executed by Hamas militants wearing civilian clothes in the Shifa hospital compound.<sup id="cite_ref-316" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-316">[316]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10_Gazan_hospitals_317-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10_Gazan_hospitals-317">[317]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Intelligence_and_Terrorism_Information_Center" title="Intelligence and Terrorism Information Center">Intelligence and Terrorism Information Center</a>, an Israel-based group with close ties to the Israeli military establishment,<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes_study_306-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes_study-306">[306]</a></sup> reported that Hamas made extensive use of the Al-Fahoura Medical Centre and that they established a military camp and training base next to it. The ITIC released aerial pictures showing tunnels dug around the building and the medical centre and that the area surrounding the hospital was heavily mined. Rockets were launched in close proximity of the centre. The ITIC report stated that Hamas used 10 Gazan hospitals for launching rockets at Israeli towns and for attacking IDF troops.<sup id="cite_ref-10_Gazan_hospitals_317-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10_Gazan_hospitals-317">[317]</a></sup></p>
<p>Hamas also set up a command centre within a children's hospital located in the Nasser neighbourhood of Gaza City, which was used by top Hamas leadership on the night of 27 December. Senior Hamas commanders also set up a command center in a Red Crescent Society clinic in Khan Yunis.<sup id="cite_ref-JpostHaniyehHid_313-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JpostHaniyehHid-313">[313]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10_Gazan_hospitals_317-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10_Gazan_hospitals-317">[317]</a></sup></p>
<p>An IDF probe, released on 22 April 2009, stated that a UN vehicle was attacked by Israeli forces because a Palestinian anti-tank squad was being unloaded from the vehicle.<sup id="cite_ref-JpostHaniyehHid_313-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JpostHaniyehHid-313">[313]</a></sup></p>
<p>Amnesty International rejected the charges by Israel that Hamas had systematically used medical facilities, vehicles and uniforms as a cover, stating that no evidence had been provided proving such actions.<sup id="cite_ref-Jpost0202_318-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jpost0202-318">[318]</a></sup> Further, <a href="/wiki/Magen_David_Adom" title="Magen David Adom">Magen David Adom</a>'s submission to the UN Mission investigating the war stated "there was no use of PRCS ambulances for the transport of weapons or ammunition ... [and] there was no misuse of the emblem by PRCS."<sup id="cite_ref-UNFFMGCReportp144_319-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNFFMGCReportp144-319">[319]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following its investigations the Goldstone report concluded that it "did not find any evidence to support the allegations that hospital facilities were used by the Gaza authorities or by Palestinian armed groups to shield military activities and that ambulances were used to transport combatants or for other military purposes".<sup id="cite_ref-UNFFMGCReport_pdf_50-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNFFMGCReport_pdf-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversial_tactics_allegedly_used_by_Israel">Controversial tactics allegedly used by Israel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Controversial tactics allegedly used by Israel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Collective_punishment">Collective punishment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Collective punishment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Fact_Finding_Mission_on_the_Gaza_Conflict" title="United Nations Fact Finding Mission on the Gaza Conflict">United Nations Fact Finding Mission on the Gaza Conflict</a> found that Israel, at least in part, targeted the people of Gaza as a whole. The Mission gave its opinion that ″the operations were in furtherance of an overall policy aimed at punishing the Gaza population for its resilience and for its apparent support for Hamas, and possibly with the intent of forcing a change in such support.″<sup id="cite_ref-320" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-320">[320]</a></sup> Judge Goldstone later at least partially resiled from this conclusion.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Disproportionate_force">Disproportionate force</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Disproportionate force">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Israel was widely criticised by human rights groups for using heavy firepower and causing hundreds of civilian casualties.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_2010-01-29_321-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_2010-01-29-321">[321]</a></sup> A group of soldiers who took part in the conflict echoed the criticism through both the Israeli NGO <a href="/wiki/Breaking_the_Silence_(non-governmental_organization)" title="Breaking the Silence (non-governmental organization)">Breaking the Silence</a> and a special report by Israeli filmmaker <a href="/wiki/Nurit_Kedar" title="Nurit Kedar">Nurit Kedar</a> that was shown on Britain's <a href="/wiki/Channel_4" title="Channel 4">Channel 4</a> in January 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Telegraph_2011-01-23_322-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Telegraph_2011-01-23-322">[322]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-323" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-323">[323]</a></sup> Israel was accused of having a deliberate policy of <a href="/wiki/Military_necessity" title="Military necessity">disproportionate force</a> aimed at the civilian population.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_2009-09-15_324-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_2009-09-15-324">[324]</a></sup> Israel has said that operational orders emphasised <a href="/wiki/Proportionality_(international_humanitarian_law)" class="mw-redirect" title="Proportionality (international humanitarian law)">proportionality</a> and humanity while the importance of <a href="/wiki/Civilian_casualty_ratio#Israel_in_the_Gaza_War" title="Civilian casualty ratio">minimising harm</a> to civilians was made clear to soldiers.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Telegraph_2011-01-23_322-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Telegraph_2011-01-23-322">[322]</a></sup> Retired U.S. Army colonel <a href="/wiki/Douglas_Macgregor" title="Douglas Macgregor">Douglas Macgregor</a> gave his opinion as: "They went in heavy, with lots of firepower. But at the same time, because of good intel and other improvements, they were able to be selective and cut down on collateral damage."<sup id="cite_ref-DefenseNews_2009-03-23_325-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DefenseNews_2009-03-23-325">[325]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="IDF_use_of_human_shields">IDF use of human shields</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: IDF use of human shields">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>On 24 March, a report from the UN team responsible for the protection of children in war zones was released: it found "hundreds" of violations of the rights of children and accused Israeli soldiers of using children as <a href="/wiki/Human_shields" class="mw-redirect" title="Human shields">human shields</a>, bulldozing a home with a woman and child still inside, and shelling a building they had ordered civilians into a day earlier.<sup id="cite_ref-unchildren_326-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unchildren-326">[326]</a></sup> One case involved using an 11-year-old boy as a human shield, by forcing him to enter suspected buildings first and also inspect bags. The report also mentioned the boy was used as a shield when Israeli soldiers came under fire.<sup id="cite_ref-unchildren_326-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unchildren-326">[326]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BShield_327-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BShield-327">[327]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> has also received testimony from three Palestinian brothers aged 14, 15, and 16, who all claimed to have been used as human shields.<sup id="cite_ref-GShield_328-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GShield-328">[328]</a></sup></p>
<p>The UK newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> conducted an investigation of its own, which, according to the paper, uncovered evidence of war crimes including the use of Palestinian children as human shields.<sup id="cite_ref-329" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-329">[329]</a></sup></p>
<p>The UN fact-finding mission investigated four incidents in which Palestinian civilians were coerced, blindfolded, handcuffed and at gunpoint to enter houses ahead of Israeli soldiers during military operations. The mission confirmed the continued use of this practice with published testimonies of Israeli soldiers who had taken part in the military operations. The mission concluded that these practices amounted to using civilians as human shields in breach of international law. Some civilians were also questioned under threat of death or injury to extract information about Palestinian combatants and tunnels, constituting a further violation of international humanitarian law.<sup id="cite_ref-UNFFMGCReport_pdf_50-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNFFMGCReport_pdf-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="White_phosphorus">White phosphorus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: White phosphorus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>From 5 January, reports emerged of use by Israel of <a href="/wiki/White_phosphorus" class="mw-redirect" title="White phosphorus">white phosphorus</a> against the Palestinian population, which was initially denied by Israel.<sup id="cite_ref-DailyMail_WP_330-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DailyMail_WP-330">[330]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-331" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-331">[331]</a></sup> There were numerous reports of its use by the IDF during the conflict. On 12 January, it was reported that more than 50 phosphorus burns victims were in Nasser Hospital. On 16 January the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Relief_and_Works_Agency_for_Palestine_Refugees_in_the_Near_East" class="mw-redirect" title="United Nations Relief and Works Agency for Palestine Refugees in the Near East">UNRWA</a> headquarters was hit with phosphorus munitions.<sup id="cite_ref-Israel_admits_using_white_phosphorus_in_attacks_on_Gaza_332-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Israel_admits_using_white_phosphorus_in_attacks_on_Gaza-332">[332]</a></sup> As a result of the hit, the compound was set ablaze.<sup id="cite_ref-Israel_reprimands_top_officers_over_UN_compound_strike_333-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Israel_reprimands_top_officers_over_UN_compound_strike-333">[333]</a></sup> On completion of the three-day Israeli withdrawal (21 January) an Israeli military spokeswoman said that shells containing phosphorus had been used in Gaza but said that they were used legally as a method to provide a smokescreen.<sup id="cite_ref-Israel_admits_using_white_phosphorus_in_attacks_on_Gaza_332-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Israel_admits_using_white_phosphorus_in_attacks_on_Gaza-332">[332]</a></sup> The IDF reiterated their position on 13 January saying that it used weapons "in compliance with international law, while strictly observing that they be used according to the type of combat and its characteristics".<sup id="cite_ref-334" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-334">[334]</a></sup> On 25 March 2009, the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>-based human rights organization <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a> published a 71-page report titled "Rain of Fire, Israel's Unlawful Use of White Phosphorus in Gaza" and said that Israel's usage of the weapon was illegal.<sup id="cite_ref-RainofFire_335-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RainofFire-335">[335]</a></sup> Donatella Rovera, Amnesty's researcher on Israel and the Occupied Palestinian Territories said that such extensive use of this weapon in Gaza's densely populated residential neighbourhoods is inherently indiscriminate. "Its repeated use in this manner, despite evidence of its indiscriminate effects and its toll on civilians, is a war crime," she said.<sup id="cite_ref-336" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-336">[336]</a></sup> The Goldstone report accepted that white phosphorus is not illegal under international law but did find that the Israelis were "systematically reckless in determining its use in built-up areas". It also called for serious consideration to be given to the banning of its use as an obscurant.<sup id="cite_ref-Goldstone_Report_337-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Goldstone_Report-337">[337]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
<div id="mwe_player_2" class="PopUpMediaTransform" style="width:220px;" videopayload="&lt;div class=&quot;mediaContainer&quot; style=&quot;width:854px&quot;&gt;&lt;video id=&quot;mwe_player_3&quot; poster=&quot;//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Aljazeeraasset-GAZAPHOSPHD110109738.ogv/854px--Aljazeeraasset-GAZAPHOSPHD110109738.ogv.jpg&quot;
