<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aljazeeraasset-GAZAPHOSPHD110109738.ogv" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Al Jazeera video. Burning Israeli white phosphorus clusters in the streets of Gaza on 11 January 2009.<br />
<a href="https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/Videos_by_Al_Jazeera_of_the_2008-2009_Gaza_War" class="extiw" title="commons:Videos by Al Jazeera of the 2008-2009 Gaza War">Videos by Al Jazeera of the 2008-2009 Gaza War</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After watching footage of Israeli troop deployments on television, a British soldier who completed numerous combat tours in Iraq and Afghanistan with the Intelligence Corps defended the Israeli Army's use of white phosphorus. The soldier noted, "White phosphorus is used because it provides an instant smokescreen, other munitions can provide a smokescreen but the effect is not instant. Faced with overwhelming enemy fire and wounded comrades, every commander would choose to screen his men instantly, to do otherwise would be negligent."<sup id="cite_ref-338" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-338">[338]</a></sup></p>
<p>Colonel Lane, a military expert testifying in front of the fact-finding mission in July 2009, told that white phosphorus is used for smoke generation to hide from the enemy. He stated, "The quality of smoke produced by white phosphorus is superb; if you want real smoke for real coverage, white phosphorus will give it to you."<sup id="cite_ref-Public_hearings_.E2.80.93_Geneva.2C_Afternoon_Session_of_7_July_2009_305-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Public_hearings_.E2.80.93_Geneva.2C_Afternoon_Session_of_7_July_2009-305">[305]</a></sup></p>
<p>Professor Newton, expert in laws of armed conflict testifying in front of the committee, said that in an urban area, where potential perils are snipers, explosive devices and trip wires, one effective way to mask forces' movement is by white phosphorus. In certain cases, he added, such choice of means would be less harmful for civilian population than other munitions, provided that the use of white phosphorus withstands the proportionality test. In discussing the principle of proportionality he said that the legality of using white phosphorus in an urban setting could only be decided on a case by case basis taking into account "the precise circumstances of its use, not in general, generically, but based on that target, at that time". He stressed that the humanitarian implications were vital in this assessment giving the example that using white phosphorus on a school yard would have different implications to its use on another area. He also said that in his view white phosphorus munition is neither chemical nor incendiary weapon and is not intended to cause damage. He said its use was not prohibited by the Chemical Weapons Convention.<sup id="cite_ref-Public_hearings_.E2.80.93_Geneva.2C_Afternoon_Session_of_7_July_2009_305-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Public_hearings_.E2.80.93_Geneva.2C_Afternoon_Session_of_7_July_2009-305">[305]</a></sup></p>
<p>An article by Mark Cantora examining the legal implications of the use of white phosphorus munitions by the IDF, published in 2010 in the <i><a href="/wiki/Gonzaga_Journal_of_International_Law" class="mw-redirect" title="Gonzaga Journal of International Law">Gonzaga Journal of International Law</a></i>, argues that Israel's use of white phosphorus in Gaza was technically legal under existing international humanitarian laws and "Therefore, it is imperative for the international community to convene a White Phosphorus Convention Conference in order to address these issues and fill this substantial gap in international humanitarian law."<sup id="cite_ref-339" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-339">[339]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Dense_inert_metal_explosives_.28DIME.29">Dense inert metal explosives (DIME)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Dense inert metal explosives (DIME)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Dense_Inert_Metal_Explosive" title="Dense Inert Metal Explosive">Dense Inert Metal Explosive</a> (DIME) is a type of bomb developed to minimize collateral damage.<sup id="cite_ref-Haaretz_new_weapon_340-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Haaretz_new_weapon-340">[340]</a></sup> DIME is a relatively new weapons technology being developed mainly in the United States. Several studies, including the one of <a href="/wiki/Armed_Forces_Radiobiology_Research_Institute" title="Armed Forces Radiobiology Research Institute">Armed Forces Radiobiology Research Institute</a>, indicate that the tungsten residuals of the DIME weapon in the muscles of the laboratory animals result in severe malignant carcinogenesis. It is yet to be seen if this will have the same effect in humans.<sup id="cite_ref-341" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-341">[341]</a></sup> Because of possible high inclination to develop cancerous tumors in humans, some argue that the use of tungsten in weapons may be more dangerous than depleted uranium.<sup id="cite_ref-342" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-342">[342]</a></sup></p>
<p>Casualties show unusual injuries. A military expert working for <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a> said judging by the nature of the wounds and descriptions given by Gazans made it seem likely that Israel used DIME weapons. A Norwegian doctor who worked at Gaza's Shifa Hospital said that pressure waves generated by missile hits are likely the cause and produced by DIME weapons.<sup id="cite_ref-Haaretz_new_weapon_340-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Haaretz_new_weapon-340">[340]</a></sup> Another Norwegian doctor said they had ″clear evidence that the Israelis are using a new type of very high explosive weapons which are called Dense Inert Metal Explosive″.<sup id="cite_ref-343" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-343">[343]</a></sup></p>
<p>Colonel Lane, military expert testifying in front of the fact-finding mission in July 2009, told the committee that through his studies, no actual proof was found that DIME rounds were used, but tungsten, iron, and sulfur were found in samples analyzed in a forensic lab. He is of the view that some weapons systems used in the conflict had some sort of DIME component to reduce the effect on the ground. Colonel Lane explained that the idea behind a Focused Lethality Munition (FLM), which is an example of a DIME munition, is that the fragments produced stay within a safety radius of about 6 meters, so anybody outside that radius is safe, while those within the area of dispersal will be affected severely. He commented on the documentations where medics described unusual amputations saying that he was no medical expert, but the use of a metal like tungsten and cobalt at short distances would likely have that effect.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated4_344-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated4-344">[344]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Goldstone_Report" class="mw-redirect" title="Goldstone Report">Goldstone Report</a> wrote that the Mission found that the allegations that DIME weapons were used Israeli armed forces required further clarification and they were unable to ascertain their usage, though it received reports from Palestinian and foreign doctors who had operated in Gaza during the military operations of a high percentage of patients with injuries compatible with their impact. It stated that the "focused lethality" reportedly pursued in DIME weapons could be seen as enhancing compliance with the principle of distinction between civilian and military objects. The report added that as it currently stands, DIME weapons and weapons armed with heavy metal are not prohibited under international law, but do raise specific health concerns.<sup id="cite_ref-Goldstone_Report_337-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Goldstone_Report-337">[337]</a></sup></p>
<p>An Amnesty International report called on Israel to confirm or deny its use of DIME in order to facilitate the treatment of those injured in the conflict.<sup id="cite_ref-AA_345-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AA-345">[345]</a></sup> After reports of <a href="/wiki/Gaza%E2%80%93Israel_conflict#2006" title="Gaza–Israel conflict">similar cases in 2006</a>, the IDF had denied the use of DIME weapons.<sup id="cite_ref-346" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-346">[346]</a></sup> Shlom haGalil' le'Oferet After Israeli forces fired shells near a UN school in Gaza killing around 30 people, Israel's military said the shelling was in response to mortar fire from within the school and asserted that Hamas were using civilians as cover. They stated that the dead near the school included Hamas members of a rocket launching cell. Two residents of the area confirmed that a group of militants were firing mortar shells from near the school and identified two of the victims as Hamas militants. Israeli attacks"].</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Accusations_of_misconduct_by_IDF_soldiers">Accusations of misconduct by IDF soldiers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Accusations of misconduct by IDF soldiers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Testimonies from Israeli soldiers allegedly admitting indiscriminate killings of civilians, as well as vandalizing homes, were reported in March 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_gaza_abuses_347-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc_gaza_abuses-347">[347]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-348" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-348">[348]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Israel_Disputes_Soldiers.27_Accounts_of_Gaza_Abuses_349-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Israel_Disputes_Soldiers.27_Accounts_of_Gaza_Abuses-349">[349]</a></sup> Soon after the publication of the testimonies, reports implying that the testimonies were based on hearsay and not on the firsthand experience started to circulate.<sup id="cite_ref-Israel_Disputes_Soldiers.27_Accounts_of_Gaza_Abuses_349-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Israel_Disputes_Soldiers.27_Accounts_of_Gaza_Abuses-349">[349]</a></sup> At the same time, another kind of evidence was collected from several soldiers who took part in the fighting, that rebutted claims of immoral conduct on the military's part during Gaza War.<sup id="cite_ref-IDF_soldiers_rebut_claims_of_immoral_conduct_in_Gaza_350-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IDF_soldiers_rebut_claims_of_immoral_conduct_in_Gaza-350">[350]</a></sup> Following investigations, the IDF issued an official report, concluding that alleged cases of deliberate shooting at civilians did not take place.<sup id="cite_ref-Gaza_offensive:_Israeli_military_says_no_war_crimes_committed_351-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gaza_offensive:_Israeli_military_says_no_war_crimes_committed-351">[351]</a></sup> Nine Israeli rights groups reacting to the closure of the investigation issued a joint statement calling for an "independent nonpartisan investigative body to be established to look into all Israeli army activity" in Gaza.<sup id="cite_ref-Gaza_offensive:_Israeli_military_says_no_war_crimes_committed_351-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gaza_offensive:_Israeli_military_says_no_war_crimes_committed-351">[351]</a></sup></p>
<p>In July 2009, the Israeli NGO Breaking the Silence published testimony from 26 soldiers (two junior officers and the rest enlisted personnel) who took part in the Gaza assault, claiming that the IDF used Gazans as human shields, improperly fired incendiary white phosphorus shells over civilian areas and used overwhelming firepower that caused needless deaths and destruction.<sup id="cite_ref-Europeans_funding_.27Breaking_the_Silence.27_352-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Europeans_funding_.27Breaking_the_Silence.27-352">[352]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Testimonies_from_Operation_Cast_Lead.2C_Gaza_2009_353-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Testimonies_from_Operation_Cast_Lead.2C_Gaza_2009-353">[353]</a></sup> The report did not represent a cross-section of the army, but rather they were troops who had approached the group or were reached through acquaintances of NGO members.<sup id="cite_ref-Europeans_funding_.27Breaking_the_Silence.27_352-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Europeans_funding_.27Breaking_the_Silence.27-352">[352]</a></sup> The accusations were made by anonymous people who claimed that they were reserves soldiers and whose faces had been blurred in the filmed talks. An Israeli military spokesperson dismissed the testimonies as anonymous hearsay and questioned why Breaking the Silence had not handed over its findings before the media had been informed. The Israeli military said some allegations of misconduct had turned out to be second or third-hand accounts and the result of recycled rumours.<sup id="cite_ref-BTS-2009-07-15_354-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BTS-2009-07-15-354">[354]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-IDF_soldiers_give_testimonies_to_counter_Gaza_war_crimes_claims_355-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IDF_soldiers_give_testimonies_to_counter_Gaza_war_crimes_claims-355">[355]</a></sup> Breaking the Silence state that their methodology includes the verification of all information by cross-referencing the testimonies it collects and that published material has been confirmed by a number of testimonies, from several different points of view. A representative stated "the personal details of the soldiers quoted in the collection, and the exact location of the incidents described in the testimonies, would readily be made available to any official and independent investigation of the events, as long as the identity of the testifiers did not become public."<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian-Naaman_356-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-Naaman-356">[356]</a></sup> A soldier who described using Gazans as human shields told in an interview to <i>Haaretz</i> that he had not seen Palestinians being used as human shields but had been told by his commanders that this occurred.<sup id="cite_ref-Barak:_Criticism_of_IDF_should_be_directed_at_me_357-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Barak:_Criticism_of_IDF_should_be_directed_at_me-357">[357]</a></sup></p>
<p>In response to the report, a dozen English-speaking reservists who served in Gaza delivered signed, on-camera counter-testimonies via the SoldiersSpeakOut group, about Hamas' "use of Gazans as human shields and the measures the IDF took to protect Arab civilians".<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_358-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-358">[358]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-.27Breaking_the_Silence.27_vs._.27Soldiers_Speak_Out.27_on_Cast_Lead_359-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-.27Breaking_the_Silence.27_vs._.27Soldiers_Speak_Out.27_on_Cast_Lead-359">[359]</a></sup> The special report by Israeli filmmaker Nurit Kedar shown on Channel 4 detailed similar allegations by former IDF soldiers that included vandalism and misconduct by Israeli troops.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Telegraph_2011-01-23_322-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Telegraph_2011-01-23-322">[322]</a></sup></p>
<p>Colonel <a href="/wiki/Richard_Kemp" title="Richard Kemp">Richard Kemp</a>, former commander of <a href="/wiki/War_in_Afghanistan_(2001%E2%80%93present)" class="mw-redirect" title="War in Afghanistan (2001–present)">British forces in Afghanistan</a>, in his address to the UNHRC asserted that during the conflict, the Israel Defense Forces "did more to safeguard the rights of civilians in a combat zone than any other army in the history of warfare" and that Palestinian civilian casualties were a consequence of Hamas' way of fighting, which involved using human shields as a matter of policy, and deliberate attempts to sacrifice their own civilians. He added that Israel took extraordinary measures to give Gaza civilians notice of targeted areas and aborted potentially effective missions in order to prevent civilian casualties.<sup id="cite_ref-UNHRC_endorses_Goldstone.27s_Gaza_report_by_large_majority_360-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNHRC_endorses_Goldstone.27s_Gaza_report_by_large_majority-360">[360]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Prosecutions">Prosecutions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Prosecutions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>The first Israeli soldier to be prosecuted for actions committed during the war was a <a href="/wiki/Givati_Brigade" title="Givati Brigade">Givati Brigade</a> soldier who stole a Visa credit card from a Palestinian home and used it to withdraw <a href="/wiki/Israeli_new_shekel" title="Israeli new shekel">NIS</a> 1,600 (<a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">$</a>405). He was arrested and tried before the Southern Command Military Court on charges of looting, credit card fraud, and indecent conduct. He was found guilty and sentenced to seven and a half months in military prison.<sup id="cite_ref-361" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-361">[361]</a></sup></p>
<p>In a report submitted to the UN in January 2010, the IDF stated that two senior officers were disciplined for authorizing an artillery attack in violation of rules against their near populated areas. Several artillery shells hit the UNRWA compound in Tel al-Hawa.<sup id="cite_ref-IDF_downplays_action_against_officers_362-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IDF_downplays_action_against_officers-362">[362]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GAZA_OPERATION_INVESTIGATIONS:_AN_UPDATE_363-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GAZA_OPERATION_INVESTIGATIONS:_AN_UPDATE-363">[363]</a></sup> During the attack on 15 January 2009, the compound was set ablaze by white phosphorus shells.<sup id="cite_ref-Goldstone_Report_337-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Goldstone_Report-337">[337]</a></sup> The officers involved were identified as <a href="/wiki/Gaza_Division" title="Gaza Division">Gaza Division</a> Commander Brigadier-General <a href="/wiki/Eyal_Eisenberg" class="mw-redirect" title="Eyal Eisenberg">Eyal Eisenberg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Givati_Brigade" title="Givati Brigade">Givati Brigade</a> Commander Colonel Ilan Malka.<sup id="cite_ref-Israel_reprimands_top_officers_over_UN_compound_strike_333-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Israel_reprimands_top_officers_over_UN_compound_strike-333">[333]</a></sup> An IDF internal investigation concluded that the firing of the shells violated the IDF orders limiting the use of artillery fire near populated areas and endangered human life.<sup id="cite_ref-GAZA_OPERATION_INVESTIGATIONS:_AN_UPDATE_363-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GAZA_OPERATION_INVESTIGATIONS:_AN_UPDATE-363">[363]</a></sup> IDF sources added later that the shells had been fired to create cover to assist in the extrication of IDF troops, some of whom were wounded, from an area where Hamas held a superior position.<sup id="cite_ref-IDF_downplays_action_against_officers_362-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IDF_downplays_action_against_officers-362">[362]</a></sup> An Israeli Government spokesman stated that in this particular case they had found no evidence of criminal wrongdoing and so had not referred the case to criminal investigation.<sup id="cite_ref-Israel_reprimands_top_officers_over_UN_compound_strike_333-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Israel_reprimands_top_officers_over_UN_compound_strike-333">[333]</a></sup></p>
<p>In October 2010, Colonel Ilan Malka was interrogated by <a href="/wiki/Military_Police_Corps_(Israel)" title="Military Police Corps (Israel)">Israeli military police</a> over the <a href="/wiki/Zeitoun_incident" title="Zeitoun incident">Zeitoun incident</a>, and a criminal investigation was opened. Malka was suspected of authorizing an airstrike on a building that left numerous members of the Samouni family dead. His promotion to the rank of Brigadier-General was suspended due to the investigation. Malka told investigatiors that he was unaware of the presence of civilians.<sup id="cite_ref-HRW_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HRW-52">[52]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-364" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-364">[364]</a></sup> He was eventually reprimanded over the incident, but it was decided not to indict him. No other charges were brought over this incident. The IDF denied that they were targeting civilians and <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> reported that <a href="/wiki/Hamas" title="Hamas">Hamas</a> members had launched rockets at Israel about a mile away from the residents, an area "known to have many supporters of Hamas".<sup id="cite_ref-arabclan_365-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-arabclan-365">[365]</a></sup> The Palestinian Center for Human Rights called the result "disgraceful" and Btselem stated the need for an external investigator to look into IDF actions during Cast Lead.<sup id="cite_ref-366" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-366">[366]</a></sup></p>
<p>In June 2010, <a href="/wiki/Military_Advocate_General" title="Military Advocate General">Chief Advocate General</a> <a href="/wiki/Avichai_Mandelblit" title="Avichai Mandelblit">Avichai Mandelblit</a> summoned a recently discharged Givati Brigade sniper for a special hearing. The soldier was suspected of opening fire on Palestinian civilians when a group of 30 Palestinians that included women and children waving a white flag, approached an IDF position. The incident, which occurred on 4 January 2009, resulted in the death of a non-combatant. Mandelblit decided to indict the soldier on a charge of manslaughter, despite contradictory testimony and the fact that IDF investigators could not confirm that the soldier was responsible for the death.<sup id="cite_ref-367" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-367">[367]</a></sup></p>
<p>In July 2010, the officer who authorized the airstrike on the Ibrahim al-Maqadna Mosque was subjected to disciplinary action, as shrapnel caused "unintentional injuries" to civilians inside. The IDF said that the officer "failed to exercise appropriate judgement", and that he would not be allowed to serve in similar positions of command in the future. Another Israeli officer was also reprimanded for allowing a Palestinian man to enter a building to persuade Hamas militants sheltering inside to leave.<sup id="cite_ref-368" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-368">[368]</a></sup></p>
<p>In November 2010, two Givati Brigade Staff Sergeants were convicted by the Southern Command Military Court of using a Palestinian boy as a human shield. The soldiers had been accused of forcing nine-year-old Majed R. at gunpoint to open bags suspected of containing bombs in the <a href="/wiki/Tel_al-Hawa" title="Tel al-Hawa">Tel al-Hawa</a> neighborhood. Both soldiers were demoted one rank and given three-month suspended sentences.<sup id="cite_ref-HRW_52-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HRW-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_State" title="United States Department of State">U.S. State Department</a>'s 2010 Human Rights Report, the <a href="/wiki/Military_Advocate_General" title="Military Advocate General">Military Advocate General</a> investigated over 150 wartime incidents, including those mentioned in the Goldstone Report. As of July, the Military Advocate General launched 47 criminal investigations into the conduct of IDF personnel, and completed a significant number of those.<sup id="cite_ref-369" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-369">[369]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 1 April 2011, Judge <a href="/wiki/Richard_Goldstone" title="Richard Goldstone">Richard Goldstone</a>, the lead author of the UN report on the conflict, published a piece in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Post" title="The Washington Post">The Washington Post</a></i> titled 'Reconsidering the Goldstone Report on Israel and war crimes'. Goldstone noted that the subsequent investigations conducted by Israel "indicate that civilians were not intentionally targeted as a matter of policy" while "the crimes allegedly committed by Hamas were intentional goes without saying." He further expressed regret "that our fact-finding mission did not have such evidence explaining the circumstances in which we said civilians in Gaza were targeted, because it probably would have influenced our findings about intentionality and war crimes."<sup id="cite_ref-WP0401_370-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WP0401-370">[370]</a></sup> The other principal authors of the UN report, <a href="/wiki/Hina_Jilani" title="Hina Jilani">Hina Jilani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christine_Chinkin" title="Christine Chinkin">Christine Chinkin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Desmond_Travers" title="Desmond Travers">Desmond Travers</a>, have rejected Goldstone's reassessment arguing that there is "no justification for any demand or expectation for reconsideration of the report as nothing of substance has appeared that would in any way change the context, findings or conclusions of that report with respect to any of the parties to the Gaza conflict".<sup id="cite_ref-afp1404_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-afp1404-63">[63]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-g2011-04-14_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-g2011-04-14-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Effects">Effects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Effects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_the_Gaza_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Effects of the Gaza War">Effects of the Gaza War</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:War_in_Gaza_009_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/War_in_Gaza_009_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg/220px-War_in_Gaza_009_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/War_in_Gaza_009_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg/330px-War_in_Gaza_009_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/War_in_Gaza_009_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg/440px-War_in_Gaza_009_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="3072" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:War_in_Gaza_009_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Destroyed buildings in <a href="/wiki/Gaza_City" title="Gaza City">Gaza City</a>, January 2009</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Along with a high casualty rate, there were multiple economic, industrial and medical effects of the Gaza War. The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Development_Programme" title="United Nations Development Programme">United Nations Development Programme</a> warned that there will be long-term consequences of the attacks on Gaza because the livelihoods and assets of tens of thousands of Gaza civilians have been affected.<sup id="cite_ref-371" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-371">[371]</a></sup></p>
<p>Early estimates by independent contractors in Gaza say that Gaza lost nearly $2 billion in assets, including 4,000 homes destroyed.<sup id="cite_ref-bbcjan192009-earthquate_372-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcjan192009-earthquate-372">[372]</a></sup> The IDF destroyed 600–700 factories, small industries, workshops and business enterprises throughout the Gaza Strip,<sup id="cite_ref-373" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-373">[373]</a></sup> 24 mosques, 31 security compounds, and 10 water or sewage lines.<sup id="cite_ref-374" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-374">[374]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> said that 34 health facilities (8 hospitals and 26 primary health care clinics) were damaged over the course of the offensive and the <a href="/wiki/UNOCHA" class="mw-redirect" title="UNOCHA">UNOCHA</a> said that over 50 United Nations facilities sustained damage, of which 28 reported damage in the first three days of the operation.<sup id="cite_ref-UNOCHAJan22_375-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNOCHAJan22-375">[375]</a></sup> On 22 January 2010, Israel paid $10.5 million in compensation to the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> for damages to UN property incurred during the Israeli offensive.<sup id="cite_ref-376" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-376">[376]</a></sup></p>
<p>A satellite-based damage assessment of the Gaza Strip by the United Nations revealed 2,692 destroyed and severely damaged buildings, 220 <a href="/wiki/Impact_craters" class="mw-redirect" title="Impact craters">impact craters</a> on roads and bridges with an estimated length of 167&#160;km (104&#160;mi) of <a href="/wiki/Paved_road" class="mw-redirect" title="Paved road">paved</a> and unpaved roads damaged, 714 impact craters on open ground or cultivated land with an estimated land area of 2,100 hectares (21&#160;km²), 187 <a href="/wiki/Greenhouses" class="mw-redirect" title="Greenhouses">greenhouses</a> completely destroyed or severely damaged with an estimated area of 28 hectares (0.28&#160;km²), and 2,232 hectares (22.32&#160;km²) of demolished zones targeted by IDF <a href="/wiki/Bulldozers" class="mw-redirect" title="Bulldozers">bulldozers</a>, tanks and <a href="/wiki/White_phosphorus" class="mw-redirect" title="White phosphorus">phosphorus</a> shelling.<sup id="cite_ref-unosat_2_19_377-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unosat_2_19-377">[377]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health_problems_in_Gaza">Health problems in Gaza</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Health problems in Gaza">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Following the war, Gaza has witnessed increasing epidemics of health problems. At the Al Shifa hospital a constant increase in the percentage of children born with birth defects of about 60% was witnessed when the period of July to September 2008 was compared to the same period in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-378" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-378">[378]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-379" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-379">[379]</a></sup> Dr. Mohammed Abu Shaban, director of the Blood Tumors Department in Al-Rantisy Hospital in Gaza has witnessed an increase in the number of cases of blood cancer. In March 2010 the department had seen 55 cases so far for that year, compared to the 20 to 25 cases normally seen in an entire year.<sup id="cite_ref-380" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-380">[380]</a></sup> During the war, Norwegian medics said that they had found traces of depleted uranium, a radioactive and genotoxic material used in some types of munition, in some Gaza residents who were wounded.<sup id="cite_ref-381" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-381">[381]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-382" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-382">[382]</a></sup> Lawyers who brought back soil samples from Gaza said that areas where these samples were taken contained up to 75 tons of depleted uranium.<sup id="cite_ref-383" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-383">[383]</a></sup> The Israeli government denied it used Depleted Uranium, and the United Nations opened an investigation.<sup id="cite_ref-384" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-384">[384]</a></sup> Israel had also initially denied the use of white phosphorus during the war, but later acknowledged that indeed it had used white phosphorus to cover troop movements.<sup id="cite_ref-385" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-385">[385]</a></sup></p>
<p>The policy of the Government of Israel is to condition the access of Palestinians who live in the Palestinian territories to healthcare in Israel upon financial coverage from the <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_National_Authority" title="Palestinian National Authority">Palestinian Authority</a>. In January 2009, following the war, the Palestinian Authority cancelled financial coverage for all medical care for Palestinians in Israeli hospitals, including coverage for chronically ill Palestinian patients, and those in need of complex care that is not available in other tertiary medical centers in the region. This decision was protested by human rights organizations.<sup id="cite_ref-386" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-386">[386]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Gaza_humanitarian_crisis">Gaza humanitarian crisis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Gaza humanitarian crisis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/2008-2009_Gaza_Strip_aid" class="mw-redirect" title="2008-2009 Gaza Strip aid">2008-2009 Gaza Strip aid</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:UNOSAT_GazaStrip_Damage_Review_19Feb09_v3_Lowres.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/UNOSAT_GazaStrip_Damage_Review_19Feb09_v3_Lowres.png/220px-UNOSAT_GazaStrip_Damage_Review_19Feb09_v3_Lowres.png" width="220" height="311" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/UNOSAT_GazaStrip_Damage_Review_19Feb09_v3_Lowres.png/330px-UNOSAT_GazaStrip_Damage_Review_19Feb09_v3_Lowres.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/UNOSAT_GazaStrip_Damage_Review_19Feb09_v3_Lowres.png/440px-UNOSAT_GazaStrip_Damage_Review_19Feb09_v3_Lowres.png 2x" data-file-width="2481" data-file-height="3509" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:UNOSAT_GazaStrip_Damage_Review_19Feb09_v3_Lowres.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A satellite-based damage assessment of the Gaza Strip by the United Nations (<a href="/wiki/UNOSAT" title="UNOSAT">UNOSAT</a>). February 2009</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The United Nations <a href="/wiki/Office_for_the_Coordination_of_Humanitarian_Affairs" class="mw-redirect" title="Office for the Coordination of Humanitarian Affairs">Office for the Coordination of Humanitarian Affairs</a> reported that the Gaza humanitarian crisis is significant and should not be understated. It also states that the situation is a "<a href="/wiki/Human_dignity" class="mw-redirect" title="Human dignity">human dignity</a> crisis" in the Gaza strip, entailing "a massive destruction of livelihoods and a significant deterioration of <a href="/wiki/Infrastructure" title="Infrastructure">infrastructure</a> and basic services". Fear and panic are widespread; 80% of the population could not support themselves and were dependent on humanitarian assistance.<sup id="cite_ref-ocha_report_1_2_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ocha_report_1_2-8">[8]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/International_Committee_of_the_Red_Cross" title="International Committee of the Red Cross">International Red Cross</a> said the situation was "intolerable" and a "full blown humanitarian crisis".<sup id="cite_ref-387" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-387">[387]</a></sup> The importation of necessary food and supplies continues to be blocked even after the respective ceasefires.<sup id="cite_ref-388" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-388">[388]</a></sup> According to the World Food Programme, the UN's Food and Agriculture Organization and Palestinian officials, between 35% and 60% of the agriculture industry was wrecked. With extensive damage occurring to water sources, greenhouses, and farmland. It is estimated that 60% of the agricultural land in the north of the Strip may no longer be arable.<sup id="cite_ref-389" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-389">[389]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-390" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-390">[390]</a></sup> More than 50,800 Gazans were left homeless.<sup id="cite_ref-bbcjan192009-earthquate_372-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcjan192009-earthquate-372">[372]</a></sup> Extensive destruction was caused to commercial enterprises and to public infrastructure. According to Palestinian industrialists, 219 factories were destroyed or severely damaged during the Israeli military operation. They accounted as part of the 3% of industrial capacity that was operating after the Israeli blockade was imposed, which was mostly destroyed during the operation.<sup id="cite_ref-ocha_report_1_29_391-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ocha_report_1_29-391">[391]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 3 January before the IDF ground operation, Israel's foreign minister <a href="/wiki/Tzipi_Livni" title="Tzipi Livni">Tzipi Livni</a> said that Israel had taken care to protect the civilian population of Gaza, and that it had kept the humanitarian situation "completely as it should be", maintaining Israel's earlier stance.<sup id="cite_ref-livni_no_crisis_in_gaza_392-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-livni_no_crisis_in_gaza-392">[392]</a></sup> The Secretary-general of the <a href="/wiki/Arab_League" title="Arab League">Arab League</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amr_Moussa" title="Amr Moussa">Amr Moussa</a>, criticized Livni's statement and further criticized the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">Security Council</a> for not responding faster to the crisis.<sup id="cite_ref-haaretz_humanitarian_393-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-haaretz_humanitarian-393">[393]</a></sup> On subsequent reports, the UN stated that "only an immediate cease-fire will be able to address the large-scale humanitarian and protection crisis that faces the people of Gaza."<sup id="cite_ref-ocha_report_1_11_394-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ocha_report_1_11-394">[394]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Emergency_Relief_Coordinator" class="mw-redirect" title="Emergency Relief Coordinator">Emergency Relief Coordinator</a> of the United Nations has stated that after the end of the Israeli operation, at best, only 120 truckloads get into Gaza, instead of the normal daily requirement, including commercial traffic, of 500 trucks at minimum. It is also reported in his statement and other UN <a href="/wiki/OCHA" class="mw-redirect" title="OCHA">humanitarian office</a> reports that essential items such as construction materials, water pipes, electrical wires, and transformers continue to be effectively banned, or only allowed infrequently.<sup id="cite_ref-ocha_report_1_29_391-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ocha_report_1_29-391">[391]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sir_john_holmes_statement_395-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sir_john_holmes_statement-395">[395]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ocha_report_1_19_396-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ocha_report_1_19-396">[396]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ocha_report_2_5_397-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ocha_report_2_5-397">[397]</a></sup> He also stated that commercial goods must be allowed in and out, since Gaza Palestinians "do not want or deserve to be dependent on humanitarian aid" and that the "limited trickle" of items into Gaza continue the effective collective punishment of the civilian population and force the counter-productive reliance on tunnels for daily essentials.<sup id="cite_ref-sir_john_holmes_statement_395-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sir_john_holmes_statement-395">[395]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-unric_holmes_398-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unric_holmes-398">[398]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tent_camp_gaza_strip_april_2009.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Tent_camp_gaza_strip_april_2009.jpg/220px-Tent_camp_gaza_strip_april_2009.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Tent_camp_gaza_strip_april_2009.jpg/330px-Tent_camp_gaza_strip_april_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Tent_camp_gaza_strip_april_2009.jpg/440px-Tent_camp_gaza_strip_april_2009.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3504" data-file-height="2336" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tent_camp_gaza_strip_april_2009.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Tent camp, Gaza Strip, April 2009</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>As a result of the conflict, the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation" title="Organisation of Islamic Cooperation">Organisation of the Islamic Conference</a> and over 50 nations donated humanitarian aid to Gaza, including the United States, which donated over $20 million.<sup id="cite_ref-399" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-399">[399]</a></sup> On 7 January a UN Relief Works Agency spokesman acknowledged that he was "aware of instances where deliveries of humanitarian aid into Gaza" were diverted by the Hamas government, though never from his agency.<sup id="cite_ref-400" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-400">[400]</a></sup> Additionally, on 3 February, blankets and food parcels were confiscated by Hamas police personnel from an <a href="/wiki/UNRWA" title="UNRWA">UNRWA</a> distribution center, and on 4 February, the UN <a href="/wiki/Emergency_Relief_Coordinator" class="mw-redirect" title="Emergency Relief Coordinator">Emergency Relief Coordinator</a> demanded that the aid be returned immediately.<sup id="cite_ref-ocha_report_2_5_397-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ocha_report_2_5-397">[397]</a></sup> The Hamas government issued a statement stating that the incident was a misunderstanding between the drivers of the trucks and has been resolved through direct contact with the UNRWA.<sup id="cite_ref-401" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-401">[401]</a></sup> On 9 February, UNRWA lifted the suspension on the movement of its humanitarian supplies into Gaza, after the Hamas authorities returned all the aid supplies confiscated.<sup id="cite_ref-ocha_report_2_9_402-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ocha_report_2_9-402">[402]</a></sup> The UN <a href="/wiki/Office_for_the_Coordination_of_Humanitarian_Affairs" class="mw-redirect" title="Office for the Coordination of Humanitarian Affairs">Office for the Coordination of Humanitarian Affairs</a> has described the Israeli procedures for humanitarian organizations entrance to Gaza as inconsistent and unpredictable ones that impedes the ability of organizations to effectively plan their humanitarian response and obstructs efforts to address the humanitarian crisis brought by the 18 months blockade and Israel's military operation.<sup id="cite_ref-ocha_report_2_2_403-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ocha_report_2_2-403">[403]</a></sup> The UN also reported that international organizations faced "unprecedented denial" of access to Gaza by Israel since 5 November and that humanitarian access remained unreliable and needed to be granted on an unrestricted daily basis.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (March 2013)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup><sup id="cite_ref-ocha_report_1_26_404-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ocha_report_1_26-404">[404]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Destruction_In_Gaza.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Destruction_In_Gaza.jpg/220px-Destruction_In_Gaza.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Destruction_In_Gaza.jpg/330px-Destruction_In_Gaza.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Destruction_In_Gaza.jpg/440px-Destruction_In_Gaza.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3402" data-file-height="2267" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Destruction_In_Gaza.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Destroyed buildings in Gaza</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In a damage assessment by the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a>, 48% of the 122 health facilities assessed were found to be damaged or destroyed, 15 of Gaza's 27 hospitals and 41 <a href="/wiki/Primary_health_care" class="mw-redirect" title="Primary health care">primary health care</a> centers suffered damage, and 29 ambulances were partially damaged or destroyed.<sup id="cite_ref-who_report_2_4_405-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-who_report_2_4-405">[405]</a></sup> Injured patients needing referral outside Gaza for specialized care were evacuated exclusively through the Egyptian <a href="/wiki/Rafah_Border_Crossing" title="Rafah Border Crossing">Rafah border crossing</a>. In the early stages of the conflict, Hamas sealed the border, and prevented wounded Palestinians from seeking medical attention in Egypt.<sup id="cite_ref-ReutersAfrica_406-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReutersAfrica-406">[406]</a></sup> On 30 December, the organization allowed a trickle of medical evacuations from Gaza, but restricted their number.<sup id="cite_ref-PalestinianWoundedFinally_407-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PalestinianWoundedFinally-407">[407]</a></sup> Gaza Ministry of Health reported that between 29 December and 22 January, 608 injured were evacuated through Rafah. The Israeli Erez crossing was closed much of the period and only 30 patients were able to exit during the crisis.<sup id="cite_ref-ocha_report_2_2_403-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ocha_report_2_2-403">[403]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-who_report_2_4_405-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-who_report_2_4-405">[405]</a></sup> An initial survey conducted by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Development_Programme" title="United Nations Development Programme">United Nations Development Programme</a> (UNDP) estimates that 14,000 homes, 68 government buildings, and 31 non-governmental organization offices (NGOs) were either totally or partially damaged, creating about 600,000 tonnes of concrete rubble needing to be removed.<sup id="cite_ref-ocha_report_2_5_397-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ocha_report_2_5-397">[397]</a></sup> Since 2007, Israel has not permitted the entry of construction material into Gaza, adversely affecting UN projects, in particular <a href="/wiki/UNRWA" title="UNRWA">UNRWA</a> and UNDP, who suspended more than $100 million in construction projects due to lack of materials.<sup id="cite_ref-ocha_report_1_19_396-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ocha_report_1_19-396">[396]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Health_(Israel)" title="Ministry of Health (Israel)">Israeli Health Ministry</a> and <a href="/wiki/Magen_David_Adom" title="Magen David Adom">Magen David Adom</a> established an emergency clinic for wounded Gazans at the Erez crossing on 17 June. The clinic received only<sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="This term requires quantification. (March 2013)">quantify</span></a></i>]</sup>patients, none of them with war-related injuries, and it was suspected that Hamas had instructed civilians not to seek treatment there. The clinic closed after ten days.<sup id="cite_ref-408" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-408">[408]</a></sup> Subsequently, the <a href="/wiki/Jordanian_Army" class="mw-redirect" title="Jordanian Army">Jordanian Army</a> established a <a href="/wiki/Field_hospital" title="Field hospital">field hospital</a> in the Gaza Strip, which is still operating.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (March 2013)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> The hospital's equipment, staff, and military guards are transferred from Jordan through Israel via the <a href="/wiki/Allenby_Bridge" title="Allenby Bridge">Allenby Bridge</a>, and outgoing personnel return the same way.<sup id="cite_ref-409" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-409">[409]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-410" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-410">[410]</a></sup></p>
<p>One year after the ceasefire approximately 20,000 people remained displaced.<sup id="cite_ref-unhm200912_411-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unhm200912-411">[411]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Effects_on_Israel">Effects on Israel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Effects on Israel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rocketpopmap.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Rocketpopmap.jpeg/220px-Rocketpopmap.jpeg" width="220" height="168" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Rocketpopmap.jpeg/330px-Rocketpopmap.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Rocketpopmap.jpeg/440px-Rocketpopmap.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="1366" data-file-height="1045" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rocketpopmap.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
According to <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">HRW</a>, during the Gaza War, rocket attacks placed up to 800,000 people within range of attack.<sup id="cite_ref-Hamas:_Investigate_Attacks_on_Israeli_Civilians_238-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hamas:_Investigate_Attacks_on_Israeli_Civilians-238">[238]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During the conflict, life in much of southern Israel was paralyzed by Hamas rocket and mortar fire.<sup id="cite_ref-412" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-412">[412]</a></sup> The Israeli <a href="/wiki/Home_Front_Command" title="Home Front Command">Home Front Command</a> issued detailed emergency instructions to Israeli citizens for preparing for and dealing with rocket attacks from the Gaza Strip. The instructions included orders to stay within a certain distance of <a href="/wiki/Bomb_shelter" title="Bomb shelter">bomb shelters</a> based on proximity to the source of the rockets.<sup id="cite_ref-413" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-413">[413]</a></sup> Hamas' Grad rockets' increased range of 40&#160;km put more than 700,000 Israelis within strike range,<sup id="cite_ref-414" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-414">[414]</a></sup> prompting 40% of the residents of the southern city of <a href="/wiki/Ashkelon" title="Ashkelon">Ashkelon</a> to flee the city, despite official calls to stay.<sup id="cite_ref-irinnews.org_415-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-irinnews.org-415">[415]</a></sup> Throughout the war, Palestinian rocket attacks into Israel damaged or destroyed more than 1,500 homes and buildings and 327 vehicles.<sup id="cite_ref-416" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-416">[416]</a></sup> Numerous agricultural fields near Gaza also sustained damage. Twenty-eight Israeli families lost their homes to rocket attacks, and had to temporarily live in hotels.<sup id="cite_ref-417" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-417">[417]</a></sup> Among the buildings hit were nine educational facilities and three synagogues.<sup id="cite_ref-golstonereport.com_418-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-golstonereport.com-418">[418]</a></sup></p>
<p>Schools and universities in southern Israel began to close due to rocket threats on 27 December.<sup id="cite_ref-419" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-419">[419]</a></sup> Studies officially resumed on 11 January. Only schools with fortified classrooms and bomb shelters were allowed to bring students in, and IDF Home Front Command representatives were stationed in the schools;<sup id="cite_ref-irinnews.org_415-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-irinnews.org-415">[415]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-420" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-420">[420]</a></sup> attendance was low.<sup id="cite_ref-421" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-421">[421]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-back_422-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-back-422">[422]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-423" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-423">[423]</a></sup> Palestinian rocket attacks that hit educational facilities caused no casualties.<sup id="cite_ref-golstonereport.com_418-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-golstonereport.com-418">[418]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-424" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-424">[424]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-school_425-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-school-425">[425]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-426" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-426">[426]</a></sup></p>
<p>The largest hospital on Israel's southern coast, Ashkelon's <a href="/wiki/Barzilai_Medical_Center" title="Barzilai Medical Center">Barzilai Medical Center</a>, moved its critical treatment facilities into an underground shelter after a rocket struck beside its <a href="/wiki/Helipad" title="Helipad">helicopter pad</a> on 28 December.<sup id="cite_ref-fear_427-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fear-427">[427]</a></sup></p>
<p>Most business in Southern Israel stopped upon orders of the Home Front Command, with retailers losing an estimated $7 million in the first week. Numerous small businesses suffered in decreased sales, and were unable to pay employee salaries due to low revenues.<sup id="cite_ref-golstonereport.com_418-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-golstonereport.com-418">[418]</a></sup> Major industries remained open, but had high absence rates.<sup id="cite_ref-428" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-428">[428]</a></sup> The Manufacturers Association of Israel estimated the direct cost to business and industry to be 88 million <a href="/wiki/Israeli_new_shekel" title="Israeli new shekel">NIS</a>, and indirect financial losses at several tens of millions of shekels.<sup id="cite_ref-globes_429-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-globes-429">[429]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Israel Tax Authority received 1,728 compensation claims for damages related to the conflict, mostly from <a href="/wiki/Ashkelon" title="Ashkelon">Ashkelon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ashdod" title="Ashdod">Ashdod</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-globes_429-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-globes-429">[429]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to Israeli economist Ron Eichel, the war effort cost the Israeli military about 5 billion NIS in military expenditure, or 250 million NIS per day.<sup id="cite_ref-430" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-430">[430]</a></sup> An anonymous political source told <a href="/wiki/Ynetnews" title="Ynetnews">Ynetnews</a> that the aerial assaults were costing $27 million to $39 million a day in munitions and fuel, totaling the first six days of the operation at nearly $265 million for air-strikes alone. Both the IDF and Treasury refused to disclose the exact amount, and the Treasury adamantly denied these figures.<sup id="cite_ref-431" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-431">[431]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_law">International law</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: International law">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/International_law_and_the_Gaza_War" class="mw-redirect" title="International law and the Gaza War">International law and the Gaza War</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Fact_Finding_Mission_on_the_Gaza_Conflict" title="United Nations Fact Finding Mission on the Gaza Conflict">United Nations Fact Finding Mission on the Gaza Conflict</a></div>
<p>Accusations of violations regarding <a href="/wiki/International_humanitarian_law" title="International humanitarian law">international humanitarian law</a>, which governs the actions by belligerents during an armed conflict, have been directed at both Israel and Hamas for their actions during the Gaza War. The accusations covered violating laws governing <a href="/wiki/Distinction_(law)" title="Distinction (law)">distinction</a> and <a href="/wiki/Proportionality_(international_humanitarian_law)" class="mw-redirect" title="Proportionality (international humanitarian law)">proportionality</a> by Israel, the indiscriminate firing of rockets at civilian locations and <a href="/wiki/2009_Hamas_political_violence_in_Gaza" title="2009 Hamas political violence in Gaza">extrajudicial violence</a> within the Gaza Strip by Hamas.<sup id="cite_ref-AI_briefing_66-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AI_briefing-66">[66]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Under_Cover_of_War_432-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Under_Cover_of_War-432">[432]</a></sup> As of September 2009, some 360 complaints had been filed by individuals and <a href="/wiki/NGO" class="mw-redirect" title="NGO">NGOs</a> at the prosecutor's office in <a href="/wiki/The_Hague" title="The Hague">the Hague</a> calling for investigations into alleged crimes committed by Israel during the Gaza War.<sup id="cite_ref-JTA1_433-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JTA1-433">[433]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 15 September 2009, a 574-page <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Fact_Finding_Mission_on_the_Gaza_Conflict" title="United Nations Fact Finding Mission on the Gaza Conflict">report by UN inquiry team</a> was released, officially titled "Human Rights in Palestine and Other Occupied Arab Territories: Report of the United Nations Fact Finding Mission on the Gaza Conflict". It concluded that the Israel Defense Forces (IDF) and Palestinian armed groups committed <a href="/wiki/War_crimes" class="mw-redirect" title="War crimes">war crimes</a> and possibly <a href="/wiki/Crimes_against_humanity" title="Crimes against humanity">crimes against humanity</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-434" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-434">[434]</a></sup> On 16 October 2009, the UN <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="Human Rights Council">Human Rights Council</a> endorsed the report.<sup id="cite_ref-APFOct16_435-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-APFOct16-435">[435]</a></sup> Israel's Defense Minister said that the report was distorted, falsified and not balanced.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_2010-01-29_321-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_2010-01-29-321">[321]</a></sup></p>
<p>Human rights organizations have urged both Israel and Hamas to implement an independent investigation into the alleged violations of international law as stipulated by the Goldstone report.<sup id="cite_ref-Letter_to_Prime_Minister_Haniya_436-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Letter_to_Prime_Minister_Haniya-436">[436]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-437" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-437">[437]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-438" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-438">[438]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 1 April 2011, Goldstone wrote an op-ed that appeared in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Post" title="The Washington Post">The Washington Post</a></i> in which he stated that he no longer believes the report's finding that Israel targeted Palestinian civilians as a matter of policy, the most serious accusation the report made against Israel.<sup id="cite_ref-439" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-439">[439]</a></sup> The three other signatories to the UNHRC report, <a href="/wiki/Hina_Jilani" title="Hina Jilani">Hina Jilani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christine_Chinkin" title="Christine Chinkin">Christine Chinkin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Desmond_Travers" title="Desmond Travers">Desmond Travers</a>, co-authored an op-ed that appeared in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> in which they replied that there was no evidence that refutes any of the report's findings.<sup id="cite_ref-440" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-440">[440]</a></sup></p>
<p>In April 2012, the <a href="/wiki/International_Criminal_Court" title="International Criminal Court">International Criminal Court</a> (ICC) rejected the Palestinian Authority's (PA) request that Israel be investigated for claimed war crimes in Gaza in 2009, holding that since the PA is recognized by the UN General Assembly as an <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_observers" title="United Nations General Assembly observers">"observer"</a> rather than a "state", the ICC lacked jurisdiction to hear its request.<sup id="cite_ref-441" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-441">[441]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-442" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-442">[442]</a></sup> The decision was heavily criticized by human rights groups.<sup id="cite_ref-443" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-443">[443]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Media_and_the_Gaza_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Media and the Gaza War">Media and the Gaza War</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Photojournalists_in_2008-2009_Israel-Gaza_conflict.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Photojournalists_in_2008-2009_Israel-Gaza_conflict.jpg/220px-Photojournalists_in_2008-2009_Israel-Gaza_conflict.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Photojournalists_in_2008-2009_Israel-Gaza_conflict.jpg/330px-Photojournalists_in_2008-2009_Israel-Gaza_conflict.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Photojournalists_in_2008-2009_Israel-Gaza_conflict.jpg/440px-Photojournalists_in_2008-2009_Israel-Gaza_conflict.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="853" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Photojournalists_in_2008-2009_Israel-Gaza_conflict.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Photojournalism" title="Photojournalism">Photojournalists</a> during the conflict</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>International news networks named the conflict "War in Gaza" and focused on the assault. Israeli media called it the "War in the South" (<a href="/wiki/Hebrew_language" title="Hebrew language">Hebrew</a>: <span lang="he" dir="rtl" xml:lang="he">מלחמה בדרום</span>‎‎ <i>Milẖama BaDarom</i>) and dispatched reporters to Israeli towns hit by rockets.<sup id="cite_ref-AFP_2009-01-14_444-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AFP_2009-01-14-444">[444]</a></sup> Al Jazeera suggested that it was a war against Palestinian civilians with the title "War on Gaza".<sup id="cite_ref-Bill_Meyer_2008-01-13_445-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bill_Meyer_2008-01-13-445">[445]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Denied_media_access">Denied media access</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Denied media access">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Reporter access to the war zone was limited. During the Gaza raids against Hamas, the Israeli army denied international media access to the conflict zone, against a decision by the Israeli Supreme Court to lift the embargo.<sup id="cite_ref-446" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-446">[446]</a></sup> The Foreign Press Association of Israel released a statement saying, "The unprecedented denial of access to Gaza for the world's media amounts to a severe violation of <a href="/wiki/Press_freedom" class="mw-redirect" title="Press freedom">press freedom</a> and puts the state of Israel in the company of a handful of regimes around the world which regularly keep journalists from doing their jobs."<sup id="cite_ref-447" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-447">[447]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Attacks_on_the_media">Attacks on the media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: Attacks on the media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Media facilities in Gaza, both foreign and domestic, came under Israeli fire in the military campaign.<sup id="cite_ref-CPJ_448-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPJ-448">[448]</a></sup> On one occasion a <a href="/wiki/BM-21" class="mw-redirect" title="BM-21">Grad rocket</a> may have been launched from a location near the television studios in the Al-Shuruk tower in Gaza City. Although the Israeli recording of a reporter describing a rocket launch was during the initial aerial bombardment phase the tower was only bombed in the final few days.<sup id="cite_ref-Al-Arabia-Grad_449-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Al-Arabia-Grad-449">[449]</a></sup> On 29 December the IDF destroyed the facilities and headquarters of <a href="/wiki/Al-Aqsa_TV" title="Al-Aqsa TV">Al-Aqsa TV</a> (though broadcasts continue from elsewhere), and a week later, IDF soldiers entered the building and seized the equipment. The Israelis also hacked into the station's signal and broadcast an animated clip of Hamas' leadership being gunned down. On 5 January the IDF bombed the offices of the Hamas-affiliated Al-Risala newsweekly.<sup id="cite_ref-CPJ_448-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPJ-448">[448]</a></sup> On 9 January the IDF hit the Johara tower of Gaza City, which houses more than 20 international news organizations, including Turkish, French, and Iranian outlets.<sup id="cite_ref-maan_20press_450-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-maan_20press-450">[450]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/IDF_Spokesperson%27s_Unit" title="IDF Spokesperson's Unit">IDF Spokesperson's Unit</a> said that the building had not been targeted, though it may have sustained damage from a nearby Israeli strike.</p>
<p>On 12 January two Arab journalists from <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">Jerusalem</a> working for an <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iranian</a> television station were arrested by <a href="/wiki/Israel_Police" title="Israel Police">Israeli Police</a> and indicted in the Jerusalem District Court for violating military <a href="/wiki/Censorship" title="Censorship">censorship</a> protocols. They had reported on the IDF ground offensive hours before they were cleared to do so. The journalists maintained that they merely stated what was already being said in the international media.<sup id="cite_ref-451" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-451">[451]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="New_media">New media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: New media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Media relations also played an important role, with the use of <a href="/wiki/New_media" title="New media">new media</a> (up to and including <a href="/wiki/Cyber_warfare" class="mw-redirect" title="Cyber warfare">cyber warfare</a>) on the part of both Israel and Hamas.<sup id="cite_ref-452" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-452">[452]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Haaretz" title="Haaretz">Haaretz</a></i> reported that Israeli <a href="/wiki/Foreign_Affairs_Minister_of_Israel" class="mw-redirect" title="Foreign Affairs Minister of Israel">Foreign Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Tzipi_Livni" title="Tzipi Livni">Tzipi Livni</a> "instructed senior ministry officials to open an aggressive and diplomatic international public relations campaign to gain support for Israel Defense Forces operations in the Gaza Strip". Israeli officials at embassies and consulates worldwide have mounted campaigns in local media, and to that end have recruited people who speak the native language. Israel has also opened an international media centre in <a href="/wiki/Sderot" title="Sderot">Sderot</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-haaretz_israel_PR_453-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-haaretz_israel_PR-453">[453]</a></sup> To improve Israeli public relations, the <a href="/wiki/Immigrant_Absorption_Minister_of_Israel" class="mw-redirect" title="Immigrant Absorption Minister of Israel">Ministry of Immigrant Absorption</a> has recruited 1,000 volunteers with the objective of flooding news websites and blogs that the ministry term as anti-Israeli with pro-Israeli opinions. Volunteers proficient in languages other than Hebrew were particularly sought after.<sup id="cite_ref-454" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-454">[454]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-455" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-455">[455]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-456" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-456">[456]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-457" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-457">[457]</a></sup></p>
<p>Foreign Press Branch head <a href="/wiki/Avital_Leibovich" title="Avital Leibovich">Avital Leibovich</a> believes the "new media" is another war zone, stating, "We have to be relevant there." As part of its <a href="/wiki/Public-relations" class="mw-redirect" title="Public-relations">public-relations</a> campaign, the Israeli army opened a <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a> channel "through which it will disseminate footage of precision bombing operations in the Gaza Strip, as well as aid distribution and other footage of interest to the international community".<sup id="cite_ref-458" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-458">[458]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-459" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-459">[459]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reactions">Reactions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: Reactions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/International_reaction_to_the_Gaza_War" class="mw-redirect" title="International reaction to the Gaza War">International reaction to the Gaza War</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Antisemitic_incidents_during_the_Gaza_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Antisemitic incidents during the Gaza War">Antisemitic incidents during the Gaza War</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2009_Anti_Israel_Protest_Tanzania.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/2009_Anti_Israel_Protest_Tanzania.JPG/220px-2009_Anti_Israel_Protest_Tanzania.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/2009_Anti_Israel_Protest_Tanzania.JPG/330px-2009_Anti_Israel_Protest_Tanzania.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/2009_Anti_Israel_Protest_Tanzania.JPG/440px-2009_Anti_Israel_Protest_Tanzania.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1333" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
