Protest against the war in <a href="/wiki/Dar_es_Salaam" title="Dar es Salaam">Dar es Salaam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tanzania" title="Tanzania">Tanzania</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Israel_peace_rally,_London_Jan_11_2009_P.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Israel_peace_rally%2C_London_Jan_11_2009_P.JPG/220px-Israel_peace_rally%2C_London_Jan_11_2009_P.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Israel_peace_rally%2C_London_Jan_11_2009_P.JPG/330px-Israel_peace_rally%2C_London_Jan_11_2009_P.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Israel_peace_rally%2C_London_Jan_11_2009_P.JPG/440px-Israel_peace_rally%2C_London_Jan_11_2009_P.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Israel_peace_rally,_London_Jan_11_2009_P.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Protest against the war in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, <a href="/wiki/UK" class="mw-redirect" title="UK">UK</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>While Israel defined its operation as a war against Hamas, Palestinian representatives and individuals, among others, viewed it as a "war on the <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Palestinian people">Palestinian people</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-460" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-460">[460]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-461" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-461">[461]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-462" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-462">[462]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">Security Council</a> issued a statement on 28 December 2008, calling "for an immediate halt to all violence".<sup id="cite_ref-worsnip1_463-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worsnip1-463">[463]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Arab_League" title="Arab League">Arab League</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-464" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-464">[464]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> and many nations made similar calls.<sup id="cite_ref-465" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-465">[465]</a></sup> On 9 January 2009, following an earlier, failed attempt at a ceasefire resolution,<sup id="cite_ref-Reuters_466-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters-466">[466]</a></sup> the United Nations Security Council passed <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_1860" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution 1860">Resolution 1860</a> calling for "an immediate, durable and fully respected cease-fire" leading to a full Israeli withdrawal and an end to Gaza arms smuggling, by 14 votes to one abstention (the United States).<sup id="cite_ref-467" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-467">[467]</a></sup> The resolution was ignored by both Israel and Hamas.<sup id="cite_ref-468" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-468">[468]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:International_reaction_to_the_2008%E2%80%932009_Israel%E2%80%93Gaza_conflict.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/International_reaction_to_the_2008%E2%80%932009_Israel%E2%80%93Gaza_conflict.png/220px-International_reaction_to_the_2008%E2%80%932009_Israel%E2%80%93Gaza_conflict.png" width="220" height="96" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/International_reaction_to_the_2008%E2%80%932009_Israel%E2%80%93Gaza_conflict.png/330px-International_reaction_to_the_2008%E2%80%932009_Israel%E2%80%93Gaza_conflict.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/International_reaction_to_the_2008%E2%80%932009_Israel%E2%80%93Gaza_conflict.png/440px-International_reaction_to_the_2008%E2%80%932009_Israel%E2%80%93Gaza_conflict.png 2x" data-file-width="1425" data-file-height="625" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:International_reaction_to_the_2008%E2%80%932009_Israel%E2%80%93Gaza_conflict.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Governmental proclamations regarding the 2008–2009 Israel–Gaza conflict
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #000000; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Israel-Gaza</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #0F37DB; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;States that endorsed the Israeli position/defined Israel's action as falling within its right to defense.</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #918BFE; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;States that condemned Hamas action only.</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #9ADD84; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;States that called for an end to hostilities, and condemned neither/both belligerents.</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #FF7777; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;States that condemned Israeli action only.</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #F20000; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;States that endorsed the Hamas position/defined Hamas' actions as falling within its right of resistance.</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #DCDCDC; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;States that made no official statement on the conflict.</div>
<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Many governments expressed positions on the conflict, most condemning both belligerents, or neither of them. Thirty-four states, mostly members of the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation" title="Organisation of Islamic Cooperation">Organisation of the Islamic Conference</a>, condemned Israel's attacks exclusively. Three of them expressed support for Hamas' operations or defined them as falling within its right of resistance. Nineteen states, mostly members of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, condemned Hamas' attacks exclusively. Thirteen of them expressed support for Israel's operations or defined them as falling within Israel's right to self-defense.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Bolivia" title="Bolivia">Bolivia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">Jordan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mauritania" title="Mauritania">Mauritania</a> and <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a> significantly downscaled or severed their relations with Israel in protest of the offensive.<sup id="cite_ref-469" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-469">[469]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-470" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-470">[470]</a></sup></p>
<p>The conflict saw worldwide civilian demonstrations for and against both sides.<sup id="cite_ref-471" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-471">[471]</a></sup></p>
<p>The conflict triggered a wave of <a href="/wiki/Antisemitic_incidents_during_the_Gaza_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Antisemitic incidents during the Gaza War">reprisal attacks</a> against Jewish targets in Europe and elsewhere.<sup id="cite_ref-472" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-472">[472]</a></sup> The worldwide number of recorded <a href="/wiki/Antisemitism" title="Antisemitism">antisemitic</a> incidents during the conflict more than tripled the number of such incidents in the same period of the previous year, marking a two-decade high.<sup id="cite_ref-AS_high_473-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AS_high-473">[473]</a></sup></p>
<p>The British government reviewed its export licenses to Israel for violations of EU and national arms export control laws and revoked five export licenses for replacement parts and other equipment for <a href="/wiki/Saar_4.5_class_missile_boat" class="mw-redirect" title="Saar 4.5 class missile boat">Sa'ar 4.5</a> missile boats used by Israel because they were used in the Gaza offensive, although 16 export licenses for other British defense items to Israel were approved.<sup id="cite_ref-474" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-474">[474]</a></sup></p>
<p>The conflict has been called the Gaza Massacre (<a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl" xml:lang="ar">مجزرة غزة</span>‎‎) in the Arab world.<sup id="cite_ref-475" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-475">[475]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-476" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-476">[476]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-477" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-477">[477]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Khaled_Mashal" title="Khaled Mashal">Khaled Mashal</a>, Hamas' leader in <a href="/wiki/Damascus" title="Damascus">Damascus</a> called for suicide bombings. <a href="/wiki/Ismail_Haniyeh" title="Ismail Haniyeh">Ismail Haniyeh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Governance_of_the_Gaza_Strip" title="Governance of the Gaza Strip">Prime Minister</a> of the Hamas government in Gaza, said: "Palestine has never witnessed an uglier massacre."<sup id="cite_ref-Hamas_massacare_478-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hamas_massacare-478">[478]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 28 December 2008, a Palestinian laborer working in the <a href="/wiki/Israeli_settlement" title="Israeli settlement">Israeli settlement</a> of <a href="/wiki/Modi%27in_Illit" title="Modi'in Illit">Modi'in Illit</a> struck his supervisor on the head with a sledehammer, stabbed and injured four civilians, and beat up several others. He was shot and severely wounded by an emergency response team member as he attempted to flee. His actions were suspected of being a reprisal for Israel's attack. The worker had been employed in the city for about 10 years with no previous trouble, but had spoken out against the war shortly before his rampage.<sup id="cite_ref-479" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-479">[479]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Reactions_in_Israel">Reactions in Israel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: Reactions in Israel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:TAU_Demo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/TAU_Demo.jpg/220px-TAU_Demo.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/TAU_Demo.jpg/330px-TAU_Demo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/TAU_Demo.jpg/440px-TAU_Demo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:TAU_Demo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Tel-Aviv_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Tel-Aviv University">Tel-Aviv University</a> students demonstrate in support for operation "Cast Lead" and the citizens of <a href="/wiki/Southern_District_(Israel)" title="Southern District (Israel)">south Israel</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The war provoked mixed reactions inside Israel, with the Jewish majority largely supporting it, and the Arab minority mostly opposing it. A poll taken on 8 January 2009 showed that 91% of the Jewish public supported the war, and 4% opposed it, while a separate poll conducted 4–6 January showed a 94% approval of the war among Jews and 85% disapproval among <a href="/wiki/Israeli_Arabs" class="mw-redirect" title="Israeli Arabs">Israeli Arabs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-INSS_480-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-INSS-480">[480]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the war, Arab protests took place across the country. Within hours of the war's start, the Higher Follow-Up Committee for Arab citizens of Israel met in <a href="/wiki/Nazareth" title="Nazareth">Nazareth</a>, and declared a "day of wrath and mourning for the martyrs among our compatriots in the Gaza Strip", and a general strike for the following day. Arab demonstrations took place across the country almost every day during the offensive, and were described as the "largest Arab demonstrations in Israel's history". Arab parties and parliamentarians in the <a href="/wiki/Knesset" title="Knesset">Knesset</a> also opposed the offensive.<sup id="cite_ref-481" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-481">[481]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Massacre_Claims_3_482-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Massacre_Claims_3-482">[482]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">Jerusalem</a>, Arabs held violent demonstrations, which included rock-throwing, <a href="/wiki/Arson" title="Arson">arson</a>, and the vandalization of Jewish graves. Police arrested dozens of rioters. At the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Haifa" title="University of Haifa">University of Haifa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tel_Aviv_University" title="Tel Aviv University">Tel Aviv University</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Hebrew_University_of_Jerusalem" title="Hebrew University of Jerusalem">Hebrew University of Jerusalem</a>, Jewish leftist and Arab students staged anti-war demonstrations, which were met with pro-war counter-demonstrations. Some confrontations occurred despite police keeping protesters apart.<sup id="cite_ref-483" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-483">[483]</a></sup></p>
<p>The legal rights agency <a href="/wiki/Adalah" title="Adalah">Adalah</a> produced a report highly critical of the Israeli police and court system's response to the opposition to Operation Cast Lead. The report said that the Israeli authorities had shown a lack of tolerance for protests, and had damaged the freedom of expression of those opposing the attacks on Gaza. The report said that the actions showed the lessons of the <a href="/wiki/Or_Commission" title="Or Commission">Or Commission</a> had not been learned. The Israeli Ministry of Justice responded that the risk to human life and public welfare had justified their actions.<sup id="cite_ref-484" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-484">[484]</a></sup></p>
<p>The term <a href="/wiki/Sderot_cinema" class="mw-redirect" title="Sderot cinema">Sderot cinema</a> has been coined for the tradition of residents in Sderot sitting to view the bombardment of the Gaza strip.</p>

<li id="cite_note-37"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-37">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation news"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/middle_east/7845428.stm">"Gaza: Humanitarian situation"</a>. <li id="cite_note-38"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-38">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The operation began in the midst of celebrating the <a href="/wiki/Jewish_holiday" class="mw-redirect" title="Jewish holiday">Jewish holiday</a> of <a href="/wiki/Hanukkah" title="Hanukkah">Hanukkah</a>; the name "Cast Lead" (<span lang="he" dir="rtl" xml:lang="he">עופרת יצוקה</span>‎, <small>Hebrew pronunciation:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Hebrew" title="Help:IPA for Hebrew">[ofeʁet jetsuka]</a></span>) is a famous phrase from Israel's <a href="/wiki/National_poet" title="National poet">national poet</a> <a href="/wiki/Hayim_Nahman_Bialik" title="Hayim Nahman Bialik">Hayim Nahman Bialik</a>'s popular Hebrew children's song "Likhvod haḤanukkah" (<span lang="he" dir="rtl" xml:lang="he">לכבוד החנוכה</span>‎). In the song (see <a href="https://he.wikipedia.org/wiki/%D7%9C%D7%9B%D7%91%D7%95%D7%93_%D7%94%D7%97%D7%A0%D7%95%D7%9B%D7%94" class="extiw" title="he:לכבוד החנוכה">article</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Hebrew_Wikipedia" title="Hebrew Wikipedia">Hebrew Wikipedia</a>), the child narrator is given a <a href="/wiki/Dreidel" title="Dreidel">dreidel</a> made of cast lead. See <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=Qc-xfP6b3gsC&amp;pg=PA42">"Operation Cast Lead"</a> in: <cite class="citation book">Gavriely-Nuri, Dalia (2013). <i>The Normalization of War in Israeli Discourse, 1967-2008</i>. Lanham, MD: Lexington Books. pp.&#160;42–43. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-7391-7260-5" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-7391-7260-5">978-0-7391-7260-5</a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGaza+War+%282008%9309%29&amp;rft.aufirst=Dalia&amp;rft.aulast=Gavriely-Nuri&amp;rft.btitle=The+Normalization+of+War+in+Israeli+Discourse%2C+1967-2008&amp;rft.date=2013&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-7391-7260-5&amp;rft.pages=42-43&amp;rft.place=Lanham%2C+MD&amp;rft.pub=Lexington+Books&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span>, on <a href="/wiki/Google_Books" title="Google Books">Google Books</a>; Gavriely-Nuri, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=nyIRetBfHzY&amp;t=65m52s">"mi'Shlom haGalil' le'Oferet Yetzuka': hashemot shel mivtze'ei Tzahal"</a>, "30 shana leMilkhemet Levanon haRishona: mabat mekhudash" (conference), 3rd session: yitzugei Levanon vehamilkhama batarbut haYisre'elit, The Hebrew University of Jerusalem - The Leonard Davis Institute for International Relations, The Department of International Relation and The Department of Communication and Journalism, 2 May 2012, 1:05:52 ff. (lecture begins at 56:25) (Hebrew).</span></li>

Shapir and Gal Perl Finkel, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.inss.org.il/uploadImages/systemFiles/Subterranean%20Warfare_%20A%20New-Old%20Challenge.pdf">Subterranean Warfare: A New-Old Challenge</a>, a chapter inside "<i>The Lessons of Operation Protective Edge</i>", eds. <li id="cite_note-99"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-99">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.terrorism-info.org.il/data/pdf/PDF_08_300_2.pdf">"The Six Months of the Lull Arrangement"</a>, <a href="/wiki/Intelligence_and_Terrorism_Information_Center" title="Intelligence and Terrorism Information Center">Intelligence and Terrorism Information Center</a> December 2008: 'A period of relative quiet between June 19 and November 4: As of June 19, there was a marked reduction in the extent of attacks on the western Negev population. The lull was sporadically violated by rocket and mortar shell fire, carried out by rogue terrorist organizations, in some instance in defiance of Hamas (especially by Fatah and Al-Qaeda supporters). Hamas was careful to maintain the ceasefire.... The escalation and erosion of the lull arrangement, November 4 to the time of this writing, December 172: On November 4 the IDF carried out a military action close to the border security fence on the Gazan side to prevent an abduction planned by Hamas, which had dug a tunnel under the fence to that purpose. Seven Hamas terrorist operatives were killed during the action. In retaliation, Hamas and the other terrorist organizations attacked Israel with a massive barrage of rockets.... During the second period a new dynamic was created which replaced the former relative calm: Hamas and the other terrorist organizations extended their attacks (rocket and mortar shell fire, IEDs and light-arms fire), the IDF operated to prevent attacks within the Gaza Strip (Israeli Air Force attacks, firing at terrorist squads within the Gaza Strip near the border), the terrorist organizations responded with barrages of rocket and mortar shell fire to retaliate for their losses and continued daily sporadic fire, in response to which Israel closed the border crossings, exerting pressure on Hamas and the Gaza Strip residents.... With the escalation in rocket and mortar shell attacks which began on November 4, Israel began closing the crossings for longer periods. That led to shortages of basic goods in the Gaza Strip and to disruptions in the supply of various types of fuel (although electrical power was not cut off, since the plant in Ashqelon, which supplies 65% of the Gaza Strip's electricity, provided an uninterrupted flow of power).'</span></li>
